I have chosen my own mix of [[Spices|spices]]; all the [[Seeds|seeds]] are left whole for this.\n\nIf you don't have an [[airfryer]] this could just as easily be done as a pan-fried dish, probably reduce the size of the potato chunks and also reduce the cooking time slightly too.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 900g Cara [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and cut into chunks, about half the size of a small [[Roast|roast]] [[Potato|potato]]\n| 3 [[Cloves of garlic|cloves of garlic]], peeled and sliced\n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[ghee]]\n}}\n====spice mixture====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 thin [[Green Indian chilli|green indian chilli]], deseeded and chopped\n| Pinch of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Black mustard seeds|black mustard seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon white [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Black cumin seeds|black cumin seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Nigella|nigella]] [[Seeds|seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Fennel seeds|fennel seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add the [[Olive oil|olive oil]], [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] to your [[Air-fryer|air-fryer]]\n| ''This recipe is best suited to a paddle-type [[Air Fryer|air fryer]], otherwise you are going to have to keep mixing the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] very often''\n| Set the [[Air-fryer|air-fryer]] to the about 200\u00b0 C\n| Cook them for 20 minutes\n| After 20 minutes shake in all of the [[Spice|spice]] mixture and cook for a further 10 to 20 minutes until they are slightly crispy\n| Serve  immediately\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Air Fried Panchphoran Aloo Potatoes In Whole Spices.jpg|All of the spices!\nImage:Air Fried Panchphoran Aloo Potatoes In Whole Spices cooked.jpg|After 35 minutes in the [[air-fryer]]\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nWe've served this with [[Sausages|sausages]], [[Eggs|eggs]] and [[Baked beans|baked beans]] as a sort of spicy [[Chip|chip]] substitute but these will accompany most dishes perfectly.\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Based on a recipe I saw [[Nigella]] Lawson doing on her TV program.\n===Variations===\nWe've used Car [[Potatoes|potatoes]] as  they are in season and very good for air-[[Frying|frying]]; use your favourite potatoes or what is available.  [[New Potatoes|new potatoes]] or waxy are not ideal for this dish.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Air fried recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#potatoes #potatoesinwholespices #airfriedpanchphoranaloopotatoesinwholespices #nigella #seeds #airfryer #oliveoil #ghee #spice #vegetarianrecipes #clovesofgarlic</code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This recipe is my variation on the classic Aloo Chop recipe that usually uses minced lamb. \n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=1st July 2018\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  2 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  1 hour, 30 minutes\n|CookTime =  45 minutes\n|TotalCalories = 2839\n|PortionCalories = 709\n|Image = [[Image:Aloo Chop recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Wierd, but good!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Strange idea and even looks odd but it was really good.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nCrispy [[Baked|baked]] [[Mashed potato|mashed potato]] with very spicy [[Mince|mince]].\n\nThis recipe is my variation on the classic Aloo Chop recipe that usually uses [[Minced|minced]] [[Lamb|lamb]].\n\nIt stared as a way to use up the odd singe [[Bramblebee Farm|bramblebee farm]] Aberdeen Angus [[Burger|burger]],  and has developed into a family staple.\n\nI usually use a [[Bramblebee Farm]] [[Burger|burger]] and make the  weight up to 300g with other [[Meat|meat]] from the [[Freezer|freezer]].\n\nRather than mess around filling the [[Potato|potato]] balls as with the classic recipe, I just spread a layer of [[Mashed potato|mashed potato]] on an [[Oven tray|oven tray]], [[Bake|bake]] it until the potato is getting golden and crispy, then top with the [[Mince|mince]] add pop for a final 10 minutes to reheat the [[Meat|meat]].\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n}}\n==== for the crispy baked mashed potato====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 500g [[Potatoes|potatoes]]\n| 25g [[Butter|butter]]\n| Good pinch of [[Salt|salt]]\n| Good pinch [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| Pinch of freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Nutmeg|nutmeg]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Dried|dried]] [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| 1 [[Egg|egg]], beaten\n| 1 teaspoon [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n}}\n==== for the spicy mince====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 tablespoons [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Ghee|ghee]]\n| 2 large [[Onions|onions]], peeled and sliced\n| 2 inches of freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Ginger|ginger]]\n| 8 large [[Garlic cloves|garlic cloves]], peeled and crusged\n| 2 [[Red chillies|red chillies]], deseeded and chopped\n| 2 [[Green chillies|green chillies]], deseeded and chopped\n| 450g [[Minced|minced]] [[Lamb|lamb]] (see variations)\n| 2 teaspoons [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| Handful of fresh [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]] (see variations)\n| 3 [[Green cardamom pods|green cardamom pods]], shells removed\n| 3 [[Brown|brown]] [[Cardamom pods|cardamom pods]], shells removed\n| 4 [[Clove buds|clove buds]]\n| A sliver of [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]] bark\n| 1 teaspoon [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]]\n| 2 tablespoons of sweet [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 1 tablespoon of you r favourite [[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]]\n| 5 tablespoons of [[Red wine|red wine]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[sesame seeds]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Peel the [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Boil|boil]] for 25 minutes, drain, add [[Butter|butter]] and [[Salt|salt]]. [[Mash]]  and and allow to cool\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7), [fan oven 200\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Aloo-chop-ready to cook the meat.jpg|Meat added to the crispy mashed potatoes\nImage:Baked mash potato - nice and crispy.jpg|Crisped after 15 minutes in the oven\nImage:Aloo-mash.jpg|Raw mash, ready to cook - the extra portion is for my breakfast!\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n}}\n====for the baked mashed potatoes====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Once the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] have cooled, sprinkle the [[Mash|mash]] with [[Parsley|parsley]] and [[Nutmeg|nutmeg]] and mix in the beaten [[Egg|egg]].  it will be quite liquid at this stage.\n| If it's too wet, add a tablespoon of [[Ground|ground]] [[Yellow cornmeal|yellow cornmeal]].\n| Grease an [[Oven tray|oven tray]] with 1 teaspoon of [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| Spread the [[Mashed potato|mashed potato]] in a thin layer over the tray\n| If you're not cooking immediately, place in a cool place until you are ready\n}}\n====for the spicy mince====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add all of the [[Dried|dried]] [[Spices|spices]] to a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] and grind to a powder \n| Add the [[Oil|oil]] and [[Ghee|ghee]] and cook the [[Onion|onion]] slices in a [[Wok|wok]] for 5 minutes\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a further few minutes\n| Stir in the [[Meat|meat]] and [[Fry|fry]] for a few minutes\n| Add the fresh [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]] or [[Parsley|parsley]] and [[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]] and mix really well.\n| The mixture does not need any more cooking at this stage and the [[Potato|potato]] mix and the [[Meat|meat]] can be prepared ahead of time if needed.\n}}\n====final assembly and cooking====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the tray of [[Mashed potato|mashed potato]] in the [[Oven|oven]] while it preheats to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7), [fan oven 200\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n| Once the [[Oven|oven]] had reached temperature, pop the tray in the middle of the oven and cook until it is crispy and has a golden colour - obout 15 minutes.\n| Spread the [[Meat|meat]] evenly over the [[Mash|mash]], sprinkle with [[sesame seeds]] and pop back in the [[Oven|oven]] for 15 minutes\n| Slice up and serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with cold [[Yoghurt|yoghurt]] and a [[Green vegetable|green vegetable]]\n===Variations===\n1 usually use 1 [[Bramblebee Farm]] 6 oz Aberdeen Angus [[Burger|burger]] & 300 g mixed [[Minced|minced]] / [[Pork|pork]] / [[Beef|beef]] / [[Lamb|lamb]]\n\nOut of season, I use another tablespoon of [[Dried|dried]] [[Parsley|parsley]], instead of the fresh [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]].\n===Chef's notes===\nWe usually pop the tray of [[Mashed potato|mashed potato]] in the [[Oven|oven]] while it gets to temperature and judge the remaining [[Mashed|mashed]] [[Potato|potato]] cooking time by eye.\n==See also==\n\n* [[Bramblebee Farm]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#mashedpotato #bramblebeefarm #parsley #potatoes #burger #vegetableoil #dried #potato #basilleaves #mash #lamb </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Aloo saag",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Aloo saag, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#potatoes #spinach #mustardseeds #garlic #chilli #aloosaag #chillipowder #onion #ginger #boiledorsimmered #boiling \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Fragrant Indian spices - ginger, garlic, black mustard seeds and fiery chilli give a superb bite to spinach and potatoes in this easy to make curry\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 833\n|PortionCalories = 208\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 50 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Aloo sag recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Yum!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Spicy spinach \ud83e\udd58</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]]</span></span>\n}}\nFragrant Indian [[Spices|spices]] - [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Garlic|garlic]], black [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]] and fiery [[Chilli|chilli]] give a superb bite to [[Spinach|spinach]] and [[Potatoes|potatoes]] in this easy to make curry side-dish recipe.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1 lb) [[Spinach|spinach]].\n| 2 tablespoons [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]].\n| 2 teaspoons whole black [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]].\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced.\n| 4 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed.\n| 2.5 cm (1\") [[Ginger root|ginger root]], peeled and [[Julienned|julienned]].\n| 675g 91.5 lb) waxy [[Potatoes|potatoes]] - new and [[salad potatoes]] are good. [[Pink fir apples]] are brilliant in this dish and do not need peeling.\n| 1 teaspoon hot [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]], or to taste.\n| 1 green [[Chilli|chilli]], de-seeded and cut into rings\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 120 ml water\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* [[Blanch]] the [[Spinach|spinach]] in [[Boiling|boiling]] water for 4 minutes.\n* Drain and allow to cool.\n* When cool enough to handle, squeeze with your hands to remove the remaining liquid.\n* Cut the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] into 2.5 cm (1\") chunks.\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a high-sided saucepan, add the [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]] and [[Fry|fry]] for 2 minutes until they start to pop.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for 5 minutes.\n| Add the [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] and slices, pour in the water and cook for about 8 minutes.\n| Add the [[Spinach|spinach]], cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 10 to 15 minutes until the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] are to your liking.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#potatoes #spinach #mustardseeds #garlic #chilli #aloosaag #chillipowder #onion #ginger #boiledorsimmered #boiling </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Apem cake (translation)",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Apem cake (translation), Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cake #flour #coconutmilk #yeast #riceflour #dough #pancake #snack #knead #rest #savory \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This 'street food' recipe was added by an Indonesian visitor: ROWI\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 5214\n|PortionCalories = 521\n|DatePublished=22nd May 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Klappertaart\n|Servings = Serves 10\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 55 minutes\n|PrepTime =  1 hour, 40 minutes\n|CookTime =  15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Coconut custard klappertaart-wiki.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Thanks Rowi</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">It's lovely to get authentic recipes from our visitors!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n==Editor's notes==\nThis 'street food' recipe was added by an Indonesian visitor: [[User:ROWI]]. It was added in the Indonesian language so for the benefit of others, I have translated the recipe from Indonesian using Google Translate and formatted it for [[Cookipedia]]'s recipe pages.\n\nWe do not have an Indonesian or Javanese category so I have added it to the closest geographical categories we have to Indonesia: Chinese and Indian.\n\nThe original recipe and related references can be found in the ''See also'' section.\n\n[[User:Chef|Jerry, aka Chef]] ([[User talk:Chef|talk]])\n\n\n\nMake cooking or food is an exciting hobby. Not only for women but also for men and even children and adolescents. A variety of menus ranging [[Snacks|snacks]] to heavy meals can be prepared and processed foods dikreasi be new and unique. Traditional and unique and still remain stable even still be an idol. It is true what people say that \"taste never lie\", as evidenced by the good food will still taste delicious on the [[Tongue|tongue]] yet. Well on this one website to review many typical Indonesian food menu. Variety can be known to her directly by visiting the site directly. For example, here is one menu that has been presented, namely apem [[Cake|cake]]. There are not yet familiar with apem [[Cake|cake]]? If Java people would know yes. Apem national language is [[Pancakes|pancakes]], and international language is its dorayaki cake Doraemon (Japan has) he he he. Whatever its name, the same shape, so yes it doang. Most modified slightly contrived nothing like wings wide, there are built like a flying saucer aircraft, there is a simple round doang sprawl, all sorts lah. Well we all know yet what makes this delicious [[Pancake|pancake]] until hunted many culinary connoisseur? Nothing less than the tender [[Meat|meat]] chewy, sweet and distinctive taste like [[Coconut|coconut]] sticky [[Savory|savory]] mixes, and unique texture when cut open his flesh like a pattern perforated like a honeycomb.\n\nSERABINYA JAVA-[[Cake|cake]] APEM In the Java community, this [[Cake|cake]] easily found in traditional markets, [[Vegetable|vegetable]] stalls, night market, and even being sold by street vendors on the roadside. In addition as a [[Snack|snack]], this cake usually served at a celebration event in Java or known by the name \"berkahan\". Sometimes on the show \"ruwahan\" or \"nyadran\" ada.-Nyadran is also clean-up activities tomb area, usually performed in conjunction with the fasting month-.\n\nAPEM-easy or hard MAKE IT? The [[Cake|cake]] is quite unique [[Snack|snack]]. One that makes it unique is the way to cook it. In the Java community, there apem cooking that uses a special mold made of clay, but many also have used common molds that are sold freely in the market or supermarket. Cook it must also be careful not to use too large a [[Stove|stove]] fire. A small flame that is important enough heat evenly. Here's a little review about the ins and outs of how to make a [[Cake|cake]] apem with the materials needed as well as other important things. Nothing is hidden or secret recipe. Indonesian recipes kitchen team will review it briefly but clearly is solid and has been successfully tried and succeeded.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 250 g [[Rice flour|rice flour]]\n| 200 g [[Flour|flour]]\n| 2 tablespoons instant [[Yeast|yeast]]\n| 200 g [[Fermented|fermented]] [[Cassava|cassava]] which has been crushed\n| 200 g [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 2 [[free range eggs]]\n| 500 ml of warm [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| half teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Vanilla|vanilla]] powder\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Material source: mix [[Yeast|yeast]] with 2 tablespoons [[Flour|flour]], [[Knead|knead]] with a little added water until smooth. And diamlan for about 15 minutes\n| Combine the [[Rest|rest]] of the [[Flour|flour]] with [[Rice flour|rice flour]], [[Sugar|sugar]], sticky tape, and [[Salt|salt]]. Mix well and add the source material. [[Knead]] the [[Dough|dough]], adding the [[Egg|egg]] and warm [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] little by little. Continue to knead until the dough becomes smooth. After that, allow the dough for 1 hour.\n| [[Dough]] will inflate after 1 hour settling. Then stir evenly. 4. Preheat apem cookie cutters, and do not forget to spread with [[Oil|oil]]. Pour [[Batter|batter]] into each mold, each one spoon, then closed. Cook for 5 minutes.\n|Behind the dough with the help of a spoon, then continue to cook again until done.\n|Remove and serve while warm.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nApem more delicious when eaten while warm, flesh firmness when it's cold turned into a bit stiff / hard.\n===Variations===\nThat was the basis of [[Cake|cake]] recipes apem / [[Pancake|pancake]]. Let me look different, you can add sprinkles meses creation with [[Chocolate|chocolate]] or [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]] on top as well. Or might want to try was given pieces of [[Pineapple|pineapple]], [[Strawberry|strawberry]], or jackfruit on it also allowed. Good luck and enjoy the delights apem.\n==See also==\n* [[User:ROWI|Recipe (in Indonesian) as added by User:ROWI]]\n* [http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Klappertaart Coconut cake 'Klappertarrt' - Wikipedia]\n* [http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kue Indonesian snacks 'Kue' - Wikipedia]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cake #flour #coconutmilk #yeast #riceflour #dough #pancake #snack #knead #rest #savory </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Balti chicken with leeks and lentils",
                "revisions": [
                    {

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Balti chicken with leeks and lentils\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#lentils #chicken #mustardseeds #leeks #chillies #ghee #corianderleaves #cucumberraita #lemonjuice #curryleaves #currypowder \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This delicious hot and spicy curry just needs a paratha and cucumber raita. This is a fabulous meal, for us it had just the right amount of heat and spices.\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1556\n|PortionCalories = 389\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Curry served, with Thomas eagerly watching\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 2 hours 45 minutes\n|PrepTime = 2 hours 10 minutes\n|CookTime = 35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Balti chicken with lentils recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">One of the best Indian meals</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A wonderful meal that is easier to make each time you make it, so make it a lot!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis delicious hot and spicy curry just needs a [[Paratha|paratha]] and [[cucumber raita]].  This is a fabulous meal, for us it had just the right amount of heat and spices.  The [[leeks]] make an interesting change in a curry. \n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 75 g split red [[Lentils|lentils]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[ghee]] or [[Corn|corn]] [[Oil|oil]]\n| 1 heaped  teaspoon black [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]]\n| A large pinch of [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 2 medium [[Leeks|leeks]], washed and chopped\n| 4 [[Indian green chillies]] or a mix or red and green, split down the middle.  These types of [[chillies]] keep brilliantly in the [[freezer]]. \n| 4 [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]], a few [[bay leaves]] will do as a poor substitute\n| Juice and grated [[lemon zest|zest]] of 1 lemon\n| 2 large [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], chopped\n| 1 teaspoon of [[curry powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[turmeric]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]], ground\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 450 g whole [[Chicken|chicken]], skinned, boned and cut into cubes\n| Freshly chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] to garnish\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\nPlace the [[chicken]] pieces, [[lemon juice]] and [[zest]] in a [[Lock & Lock]] box, give then a good shake and leave to [[marinade]] in a cool place fo a few hours or more, if you have the time.  Leave the lemon pieces in while the chicken marinates and discard them before cooking\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| ''Wash the lentils carefully and pick over them to remove any stones'', is always advised on [[lentil]] recipes, though I have yet to find any pebbles in my lentils.  I guess food standards have improved since the first [[Indian recipes]] were penned!\n| Place the [[Lentils|lentils]] in a pan with just enough cold water to cover\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] vigorously until soft, about 10 minutes, but it does depend on the type of [[Lentils|lentils]] you are using\n| Most of the water should have been absorbed, keep a few tablespoons of the cooking liquor to loosen the curry a little.  Set the lentils to one side\n| Add the [[ghee]] or [[Oil|oil]] to a [[Wok|wok]] together with the [[black pepper]] and the [[mustard seeds]] and bring it to a medium heat\n| As soon as the [[mustard seeds]] start to pop, quickly add the [[Leeks|leeks]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]] and and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] gently for 3 to 4 minutes\n| Add the [[chicken]] pieces, together with the [[lemon juice]] and [[stir-fry]] for 7 minutes\n| Tip in the chopped [[tomatoes]], [[curry powder]], ground [[coriander]], [[turmeric]], mix well and cook for a few minutes more\n| Mix in the cooked [[lentils]] with enough of the cooking liquor to loosen the curry\n| Heat and stir until the [[chicken]] is properly cooked, this should probably take another 10 minutes\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Balti chicken with lentils stir-frying.jpg|Ready to serve\nImage:Balti chicken with lentils ingredients.jpg|The ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nGarnish with [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and serve hot with [[Parathas|parathas]] or [[naan breads]] and [[cucumber raita]]\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lentils #chicken #mustardseeds #leeks #chillies #ghee #corianderleaves #cucumberraita #lemonjuice #curryleaves #currypowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Check the [[Lamb|lamb]] is cooked to your liking and serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Naan breads|naan breads]], [[Pillau rice|pillau rice]] and a [[Green salad|green salad]].\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you don't have [[Black cumin|black cumin]], just use [[White cumin|white cumin]] instead.\n\nAdjust the [[Chili|chili]] levels to suit your tastes, this can be fairly hot with these quantities, depending upon the types of chili you use.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lamb #baltilambtikka #tomatopuree #garammasala #lemonjuice #chilipowder #marinade #greensalad #corianderseeds #blackcumin #cumin </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Basic sauce for making curries an Indian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#vegetableoil #ginger #basicsauceformakingcurries #garlic #tomatoes #sauce #curries #chilli #boiledorsimmered #cumin #coriander \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is my effort at making a basic sauce for restaurant style curries\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1907\n|PortionCalories = 238\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Stage one ingredients\n |Servings = Serves 8\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 20 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour\n |Image = [[Image:Stage 1 ingredients.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n}}\n\nThis is my effort at making a basic [[Sauce|sauce]] for restaurant style [[Curries|curries]].  The following quantity is for 8 people, as you may wish to [[Freeze|freeze]] some for a later [[Date|date]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 120 ml [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 950 g or about 8 cooking [[Onions|onions]], thinly sliced\n| 175 g (about 3-4 bulbs) [[Garlic|garlic]], diced \n| 50 g [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and diced\n| 1.5 [[Litres|litres]] water\n| 2 good teaspoons [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 additional tablespoon [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli|chilli]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin|cumin]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Coriander|coriander]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cardamom|cardamom]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e\n| 1 tin chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], pur\u00e9ed\n\n}}\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n}}\n'''Stage 1'''\n#Heat the [[oil]] over a medium-high heat.\n#Add the [[onion]] slices and fry for about 10 minutes, until they are starting to brown, and even stick slightly.\n#Stir vigorously, add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[ginger]] and cook for a further few minutes until softened.\n#Add the water and blend thoroughly - the mixture must be absolutely smooth.\n#Add the [[salt]], bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and turn down the heat to low.\n#Simmer, covered, for 40-45 minutes and allow to cool.\n#If you wish to freeze the sauce, do so at this stage.\n'''Stage 2'''\n# Meanwhile, heat the 1 additional tablespoon [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] in a clean pan, add the spices and tomato pur\u00e9e cook for about a minute - no longer.\n#Add the [[tomatoes]], bring to the boil , reduce heat and cook for about 10 minutes.\n#Skim, allow to cool and refrigerate for up to 4 days.\n===Variations===\nCombine spices to your taste.\n===Chef's notes===\nMake your the [[Sauce|sauce]] two to three days in advance and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]]. This will improve the flavour and gives more of a restaurant aroma.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Curry sauce]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces|Curry sauce]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Curry sauce]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Curry sauce]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Curry sauce]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#vegetableoil #ginger #basicsauceformakingcurries #garlic #tomatoes #sauce #curries #chilli #boiledorsimmered #cumin #coriander </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Indian beef curry recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#ginger #beefcurry #coconutblock #onions #spices #curryleaves #grated #tomatoes #fry #chilli #julienned \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Another tasty curry from my early Indian cookery courses. You can vary the flavours to suit your taste, but this recipe is a good starting point\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2474\n|PortionCalories = 618\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour\n |Image = [[Image:Beef curry recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n=====Best recipe review=====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice aroma</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Very authentic tasting</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nAnother tasty curry from my early Indian cookery courses.\n\nYou can vary the flavours to suit your taste, but this recipe is a good starting point.\n\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 675 g (1.5 lb) of [[Braising steak]], cut into thin strips\n| 2 teaspoons [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Chili powder|chili powder]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]]\n| 4 [[Cloves garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 2.5 cm (1\") peeled [[Ginger|ginger]], &frac12; [[Grated|grated]], &frac12; [[Julienned|julienned]] (cut into very thin strips)\n| 6 [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]]\n| 50g slice of [[Coconut block|coconut block]]\n| 2 large [[Onions|onions]], peeled and slices\n| 1 can of [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] or equivalent amount of fresh tomatoes\n| 1 green [[Chilli|chilli]], chopped finely\n| 1 tablespoon [[Malt vinegar|malt vinegar]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]], [[Oil|oil]] or [[Butter|butter]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Grind all of the whole [[Spices|spices]], except for the [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]],  to a powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]].\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Oil|oil]] to a heavy [[Frying pan|frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]], [[Brown|brown]] the [[Meat|meat]] quickly over a high heat, remove and reserve.\n| [[Fry]] the [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Grated|grated]] [[Ginger|ginger]] until the onions are sort, about 8 minutes.\n| Add the [[Ground|ground]] [[Spices|spices]] and [[Fry|fry]] for a minute more.\n| Stir in the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Vinegar|vinegar]] and [[Julienned|julienned]] [[Ginger|ginger]] and mix well.\n| Cover and cook until the [[Meat|meat]] is tender, about 30 to 40 minutes.  If the [[Meat|meat]] is still tough, add &frac12; a cup of [[Boiling|boiling]] water and continue cooking for 20 minutes.\n| Remove the cover, add the [[Coconut block|coconut block]], green [[Chilli|chilli]] mix well and cook until the [[Coconut|coconut]] is dissolved.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]]\n===Variations===\nAdd cubed [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and a little extra liquid at the start.\n\nIf you don't have curry leaves, just use a couple of bay leaves.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#ginger #beefcurry #coconutblock #onions #spices #curryleaves #grated #tomatoes #fry #chilli #julienned </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Beef strip roti",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Beef strip roti, a Indian rice recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#rice #beef #limejuice #preparingacoconut #desiccatedcoconut #coriander #ghee #coconut #onions #murghiroti #spices \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is my version of a murghi roti, but using beef which would be against all Hindu beliefs in India\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2716\n|PortionCalories = 679\n|DatePublished=30th April 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Served with peas\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes\n |CookTime = 25 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Beef roti recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Probably not authentic</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I would not think you would find this in India, but if you did you would enjoy it (secretly!)</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Beef roti grilled.jpg|thumb|300px|right|After the frying and the grilling]]\n[[Image:Beef roti mixed together.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Mix everything together in a large bowl]]\n[[Image:Beef roti mixing beef and onions.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Mixing the beef into the cooked onions just before adding the chilles]]\n[[Murghi roti]] is a South Indian style dish made with cooked rice, cooked chicken and lots of [[Spices|spices]].  This another of my variations on this dish but using cooked strips of [[beef]].  It is not the least bit authentic as the cow is sacred and forbidden as food in the Hindu religion of India.  I had about 250 g of ready cooked [[Sous vide beef prime topside joint]] so I thought I should try using it in this recipe.  It was delicious as always ([[Murghi roti]] is one of my all time favourite recipes), but I have to say I prefer the chicken version over beef.\n\nA great recipe for using up leftovers.  Please be very careful if storing cooked [[Rice|rice]].  [[Refrigerate]] the moment it has cooled and use within 1 day.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 225 g (8 oz) uncooked [[basmati rice]].\n| 250g g (6 oz) cooked [[Sous vide beef prime topside joint]] cut into strips - any left over [[beef]] would be good also\n| 2 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]] or vegetable [[Oil|oil]]\n| 5 [[Fat|fat]] [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 5 cm (2\") [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and roughly [[Grated|grated]]\n| 150 g (5 oz) [[Onions|onions]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 fresh [[coconut]] ,flesh removed and grated\n|* see [[Preparing a coconut]]\n| 4 hot [[Chilli peppers|chilli peppers]] (red or green), finely chopped - de-seeded if desired\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n| A bunch of [[coriander]], chopped\n}}\n'''spices'''\n\n''The charm of this dish is the 'bite' of the whole spices, don't be tempted to grind them!''\n* 2 teaspoons whole [[coriander seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon of whole [[cumin seeds]] (white)\n* 1/2 a teaspoon of whole [[fenugreek seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Quickly wash and drain the [[rice]] but don't rinse it as you normally would, this dish is best with rice of a starchy consistency. \n| Cook in boiling water for 7 to 11 minutes.\n| Rinse the cooked rice in cold water until it is cold.  Drain well.\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade and blend to a thick creamy pur\u00e9e - adding a little milk if it needs thinning.  Remember, the inside is not going to change much whilst being cooked and will remain at roughly the same consistency as it was when first mixed. \n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a [[Wok|wok]] or [[frying pan]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] all of the [[Spices|spices]] for half a minute, then add the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and allow them to cook for a minute or so.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and reduce the heat a little and let them cook until translucent; about 5 minutes.\n| Add the [[beef]], [[Coconut|coconut]] and [[Chilli|chilli]] to the [[Onions|onions]], mix well and remove from the heat.\n| In a large bowl add the rice and the onion mixture together with the chopped [[coriander]] and mix really well\n| Lightly [[Oil|oil]] a large heavy non-stick oven proof [[Frying pan|frying pan]] put on a gentle heat.\n| Ensure the mixture is evenly distributed and cook gently for about 5 minutes or until the [[Rice|rice]] [[Cake|cake]] has properly solidified.\n| You can leave it as it is or mix it up as its cooking, pressing it flat again before you finally grill it.\n| Preheat the [[Grill|grill]].\n| Pop the pan under the grill and grill for 10 minutes or until it is nicely browned.\n| Sprinkle with [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and serve immediately.\n}}\n\nInstead of fresh [[green chillies]], I have used 3/4 teaspoon of diced [[ancho]] & 3/4 teaspoon diced [[chipotle]] (dried) [[chillies]].\n\nI heeded [[Preparing a coconut|my own advice]] and tasted the coconut before preparing it.  It was totally rancid, thank you Morrisons.  Luckily I had both [[coconut flakes]] and [[desiccated coconut]]. For two people, I used two big handfuls of flakes and 4 tablespoons of [[desiccated coconut]] soaked in boiling water for 5 minutes then drained in a sieve.  It worked fine and saved the day!\n\n[[Image:Action coconut scraper with vacuum suction base.jpg|300px|thumb|right|An easier way to prepare the grated coconut - [http://www.amazon.co.uk/gp/product/B00B7JDDL6?psc=1&redirect=true&ref_=oh_aui_detailpage_o07_s00 Action coconut scraper with vacuum suction base - \u00a38.98 Amazon UK]]]\n\n===A better way of cooking this===\nAfter making variants of this for many years, I've discovered the best method of cooking is to spread the ingredients out on a lightly greased [[baking tray]] and bake at 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7) for 35 minutes, stirring up the contents every 10 minutes.  It might be an idea with a meat other than crayfish, to add the meat (or prawns) for the last 10 minutes so they don't dry out.\n[[Image:Crayfish & coconut chili, 1.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Baking tray method shown here with [[Crayfish and coconut rice cake with hot chillies]]]]\n\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{Template:SeeAlso Roti}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #beef #limejuice #preparingacoconut #desiccatedcoconut #coriander #ghee #coconut #onions #murghiroti #spices </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

Tasting regularly to check it's to your liking.\n\n===Chef's tip===\n\n[[Rice]] can be cooked before the meal is due to be served, providing it is properly stored and used the same day. Set on a plate. Scatter half the [[Curry|curry]] [[Spice|spice]] over. Massage in. Gloss with a little [[Oil|oil]]. Set aside.\n| Get a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] hot. Add enough [[Oil|oil]] to create a 1cm pool of [[Oil|oil]]. Add your sliced [[Onions|onions]] and a pinch of [[Salt|salt]]. Sizzle over medium-high heat till golden and crisp. Place a fine [[Sieve|sieve]] over a [[Glass|glass]] bowl or pan. Drain the [[Onions|onions]]. (Use the oniony oil to make a [[Salad dressing|salad dressing]] another day.)\n| Place the [[Frying pan|frying pan]] back on the heat. Once hot, add your steaks, ensuring you mop up as much of the [[Spice|spice]] and [[Oil|oil]] as possible before pressing them into the pan. Cook over medium-high heat till golden and cooked to your liking, about 3 mins on each side for medium-rare.\n| Set your cooked steaks on a cutting board to [[Rest|rest]].\n| Tumble your [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]], the juices from their tins and the [[Garlic|garlic]] into a saucepan. Cook over medium heat for 5 mins, or till warmed through. Drain.\n| Add the [[Zest|zest]] and a good squeeze of [[Juice|juice]] from your [[Limes|limes]]. Crush the [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] with a [[Potato masher|potato masher]] or fork till you have a rough [[Mash|mash]]. Swirl in the [[Rest|rest]] of your [[Curry powder|curry powder]] and the [[Coriander|coriander]]. Taste. Season as needed. 7. Thinly slice your [[Steak|steak]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe on a bed of [[Chickpea mash|chickpea mash]] with the crispy [[Onions|onions]] scattered over the top.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Abel and Cole veg box recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n{{Template:Abel and Cole veg box recipes attribution}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onions #chickpeas #coriander #garlic #rest #bombaybavettewithcorianderchickpeamash #spice #currypowder #limes #steak #unusualrecipes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

The best way would be to put it in a dish in the [[Oven|oven]] with the chicken.\n\nI use [[Cock Brand green curry paste]] - It's brilliant because it can be [[Frozen|frozen]] so it keeps forever.  Even better, you can still [[Scoop|scoop]] out a tablespoon of paste while it is still frozen.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 250g [[Greek yogurt]]\n| 1 heaped tablespoon [[Curry paste|curry paste]]\n| 2 [[chicken breasts]]\n| 8 tablespoons of [[Panko]] [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Add the [[Yogurt|yogurt]] to a [[Lock and Lock box]], stir in the [[Curry paste|curry paste]] and mix well add the [https://www.cookipedia.co.uk/cgi-bin/cc.pl?cftk=2#jump chicken breasts] and [[Marinate|marinate]] for 12 hours or more.\n* Shake to box every few hours if you have the chance.\n* Preheat your [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| After 12 hours [[Marinading|marinating]], remove the [[Chicken breasts|chicken breasts]] and allow most of the [[Marinade|marinade]] to drip off.\n| Add the [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]] to a bowl and press the [[Chicken breasts|chicken breasts]] into the breadcrumbs to coat really well.\n| [[Bake]] on a [[Grill tray|grill tray]] in the middle of the [[Oven|oven]] [ 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4) ] for 30 to 35 minutes or until the [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]] are golden [[Brown|brown]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Rice|rice]], [[Peas|peas]] and [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]].\n===Chef's notes===\nAny [[Yogurt|yogurt]] would do, we just happened to have [[Greek yogurt]] in the fridge.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#breadcrumbs #breadcrumbedcurrychickenbreasts #chickenbreasts #greekyogurt #currypaste #chicken #marinade #yogurt #sauce #frozen #panko </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Then it was commonly eaten at breakfast time\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2080\n|PortionCalories = 520\n|DatePublished=15th August 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|ImageComment = Buttery kedgeree with [[asparagus]]\n|TotalTime = 50 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Buttery kedgeree dish.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Anne's favourite</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I get Brownie points every time I make this for her.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Buttery kedgeree recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ingredients for buttery kedgeree]]\nA wonderful mix of Asian and English flavours that originated amongst the British colonials in India.  Then it was commonly eaten at breakfast time. It's a bit much for breakfast but it makes a superb evening meal. This recipe is based on Delia Smith's famous buttery kedgeree recipe.\n\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 225 ml [[basmati rice]]\n| 450 ml of the water that the fish was cooked in\n| 700g [[smoked haddock]], [[smoked basa]] or [[hoki]] fillets\n| 110g [[butter]]\n| 1 [[onion]], chopped finely\n| &#189; to &#190; teaspoon [[harissa paste]], [[curry powder]] or [[curry paste]] ( vindaloo paste gives a unique flavour for the hot-heads!)\n| 4 hard boiled [[eggs]], peeled and quartered\n| 4 tablespoons chopped [[parsley]]\n| Juice of 1 [[lime]] or [[lemon]]\n| Sea [[salt]] and freshly ground [[black pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon chopped [[chives]] to garnish\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rinse the rice in a sieve for 1 minute under cold running water to remove the excess starch and leave in a colander to drain\n| Put the fish fillets in a pan and cover with 570 ml cold water.  You can leave the skins on as they will fall off later anyway\n| Bring the fish to the boil and simmer for 8 minutes\n| Reserve 450ml of the haddock water in a [[measuring jug]]\n| Place the [[haddock]] in a covered bowl and keep warm\n| Using the same pan, melt 55g of the [[butter]] and soften the [[onions]] for 6 minutes.  Don't brown them\n| Mix in the [[curry paste]] and cook for a few seconds, stirring well\n| Stir in the rice and add the reserved haddock water\n| Once it reaches a simmer, give it a quick stir to lift any rice that has stuck to the base of the pan, cover with a layer of [[tin foil]] and then put on the pan lid so you have a really good seal\n| Simmer for 15 minutes then remove from the heat\n| Remove the skin from the fish and flake it into the rice using a fork\n| Add the hard boiled eggs, remaining [[butter]], [[parsley]], [[lemon]] juice and season with [[salt]] and [[black pepper]]\n| Cover the pan with tin foil, replace the lid and gently heat for 5 minutes.  Don't be tempted to stir it or lift the lid until then\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nGarnish with chopped [[chives]] and serve immediately.\n\n===Chef's note===\n\nIf you and your partner both cook, this recipe, a glass of wine and some good music is a great way to spend some time together.\n\n==See also==\n\nA baked version with garlic and chili, [[Salmon kedgeree]] and [['Greasy spoon' kedgeree]] which speaks for itself.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:British recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Poached]]\n\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#butterykedgeree #butter #blackpepper #parsley #lemon #chives #currypaste #eggs #unusualrecipes #onions #measuringjug </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

leaves]].\n}}\n===Variations===\nUse any [[Nuts|nuts]] you like and add [[Chillies|chillies]] and/or other [[Vegetables|vegetables]]. A great addition to any curry.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tin of [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] (430 g), drained (reserve some of the water for later) and rinsed in cold running water\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| &#189; green [[Chili|chili]], chopped\n| sprigs of fresh [[Coriander|coriander]], chopped\n| 1 large fresh [[Tomato|tomato]], chopped (or 2 tablespoons of tinned [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], chopped)\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sunflower oil|sunflower oil]]\n| 50g from a block of [[creamed coconut]]\n| &#189; teaspoon freshly [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[chili powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon freshly [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]] seeds\n| 1 teaspoon [[Garam masala|garam masala]] or [[Curry powder|curry powder]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and [[Brown|brown]] the [[Onions|onions]]\n| Add the chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Fry|fry]] for a minute or two\n| Add the powdered [[Spices|spices]] and [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a minute\n| Add the [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]], [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 10 minutes\n| If you want more 'gravy' add a little of the reserved water\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe garnished with chopped [[Coriander|coriander]]\n===Variations===\n\nDaal can be made with most varieties of [[lentils and pulses]], though the soaking and cooking time may vary.\n\n==See also==\n* [[Dal|A selection of other Daal recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chanadaal #chickpeas #tomatoes #lemonjuice #coriander #fry #sidedish #simmer #onions #garammasala #boiledorsimmered </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Chapati",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chapati, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chapati #dough #foodprocessor #unleavened #tava #panfried #vegetableoil #indiandishes #flour #frying #yogurt \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Chapati is a staple flat bread of North India and Western India. It is rather thin, unleavened cooked dough\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1104\n|PortionCalories = 184\n|DatePublished=2nd January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Whole wheat chapati\n |Servings = Servings: 6 - Makes 6 chapatis\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 35 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Whole wheat chapati recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">An easy \ud83d\udc73 recipe</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Worth making</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nChapati is a staple flat [[bread]] of North India and Western India. It is rather thin, [[unleavened]] cooked [[dough]]. It is a type of [[roti]].\n\nWhilst kneading [[dough]] can be therapeutic, if time is your enemy, then the [[food processor]] is your friend.\n\nChapatis are the perfect accompaniment to most [[Indian dishes]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 cup [[whole wheat atta flour]] or [[strong whole wheat flour]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n| 2 tablespoons [[yogurt]] (optional) \n| &#189; cup water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Tip all of the ingredients and half of the water into the [[food processor]] with a plastic blade or dough hook attachment\n| Blitz the mixture whilst adding a more water a little at a time until you have a soft, pliable dough that is not too sticky\n| Remove from the processor, dust with a little [[flour]] and rest for 30 minutes in a bowl, covered with a damp tea-towel\n| Divide into 6 equal parts and roll into balls\n| With a rolling pin on a floured surface, roll each chapati out into a disc, about 2.5 mm (1/8 \") thick\n| Without using any [[oil]], heat a [[tava]] or [[frying]] pan until very hot\n| Cook each chapati for about 2 minutes a side, they should puff up slightly\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nKeep warm whilst the remainder are cooked\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chapati]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Chapati]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Chapati]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Chapati]]\n[[Category:Starters|Chapati]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chapati #dough #foodprocessor #unleavened #tava #panfried #vegetableoil #indiandishes #flour #frying #yogurt </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This recipe is based on one from Gordon Ramsay's book '''Gordon Ramsay's Great Escape''' (ISBN 0007267053) and has been adapted for use with a Panasonic [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]] and [[Tortilla press|tortilla press]].\n\n===Breadmaker settings===\n* For the Panasonic SD253 breadmaker and similar models, use the pizza setting.\n* For the [[Panasonic SD-ZB2502 automatic breadmaker]] use menu option 22, pizza dough.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 250 g wholemeal chapatti [[Flour|flour]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 150 ml or more water\n| Small amount of [[Oil|oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the ingredients in the [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]] in the order given in your manufacturer's instruction book.\n| Use the [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]] setting or the shortest [[Dough|dough]] setting that your machine has.\n| Remove from pan an allow to rest, covered, in the [[refrigerator]] for 30 minutes.\n| Divide the [[Dough|dough]] into 12 equal sized balls.\n| Press each ball into a thin circle using the [[Tortilla press|tortilla press]].\n| Cover the chapattis as you press them.\n| [[Brush]] a small frying pan lightly with [[Oil|oil]] and heat to medium.\n| Cook each chapatti until it starts to [[Bubble|bubble]].\n| Turn and cook for a further minute or two until [[Brown|brown]] speckles from and it has [[Puffed|puffed]] up.\n| Keep warm and covered until you have cooked all of the chapattis.\n| Serve straight away.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Curries|curries]] and dahls.\n===Chef's notes===\nAny [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]] will be fine, so long as you follow your manufacturer's instructions.  A [[Tortilla press|tortilla press]] is not necessary, but useful.  If you do not have one, roll out the [[Dough|dough]] between two sheets of [[Bake-O-Glide]] or similar.\n\nChapattis can be [[Frozen|frozen]], after which they should be thoroughly [[defrosted]] and gently reheated.\n===Chef's note===\nIf you don't have a [[tortilla press]], use 2 chopping boards or just two sheets of wood as a substitute.  Place ball of [[dough]] between two non-stick surfaces such as small squares of [[Bake-O-Glide]] and stand on them!\n===Suppliers===\nSee the [[Tortilla Press]] page for UK suppliers.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chapattis]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Chapattis]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Chapattis]]\n[[Category:Breadmaker recipes|Chapattis]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Chapattis]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Chapattis]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Chapattis]]\n[[Category:Dry fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chapattis #tortillapress #dough #breadmaker #puffed #curries #flour #dryfried #brush #pizzadough #refrigerator </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Don't leave it any longer or the [[leavening]] effect of the [[baking powder]] will be lost.\n| Add enough [[vegetable oil]] to a [[wok]] or [[frying pan]] to [[shallow fry]]\n| Making 5 fritters at a time, add a tablespoon of batter to the pan for each fritter and cook until golden brown.\n|Flip them and repeat for the other side.\n|Remove and drain on [[paper towels]] \n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n* Serve hot with [[tomato ketchup]].\n\n===Recipe source===\n* Based on '[[Cheese]] ke Bhajiya' taken from Mr Pushpesh Pant's wonderful \"India\":  ISBN 978-0714859026.\n==See also==\n{{FritterRecipes}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cheese #bakingpowder #tomatoketchup #vegetableoil #chiliflakes #papertowels #cheddar #rapeseedoil #cheesefrittersindian #leavening #wok </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Chicken biriani",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chicken biriani, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#onions #ghee #chickenbiriani #coriander #rice #yogurt #chicken #almonds #ginger #raisins #sultanas #Biryani #biriani #beriani\n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Biryani, biriani, or beriani is a range of primarily South Asian rice-based foods made with spices, rice (usually basmati) and meat/vegetables\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1451\n|PortionCalories = 241\n|DatePublished=3rd December 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 13 hours\n |PrepTime = 12 hours 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 40 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Chicken biriani recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Better than any restaurant version</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is the real-deal.  And you know it's going to taste so good.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n'''Biryani''', '''biriani''', or '''beriani''' is a range of primarily South Asian [[Rice|rice]]-based foods made with [[Spices|spices]], rice (usually [[Basmati|basmati]]) and [[Meat|meat]] or [[Vegetables|vegetables]]. It was spread throughout the Middle East and South Asia (and Southeast Asia to an extent) by Muslim travellers and merchants, and is popular in Pakistan, India, Bangladesh, Iraq, Iran, Afghanistan and Sri Lanka.\n\nThe name is derived from the Persian word bery\u0101(n) which means \"[[Fried|fried]]\" or \"[[Roasted|roasted]]\".\n\nThis recipe comes from a hand-typed sheet, covered in curry stains, that has been with me since my first Indian cookery course.  It's a bit of an involved recipe but well worth the effort. It is best to [[Marinate|marinate]] the [[Meat|meat]] overnight so prepare this the day before.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 whole chicken, skinned and [[Jointing a chicken|jointed]]\n| You can of course use ready prepared chicken meat instead.\n| 125 ml [[Yogurt|yogurt]]\n| 2 cups [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]], rinsed in cold running water then drained well\n|  2.5 cm (1\") peeled [[Ginger|ginger]]\n| 4 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chili powder|chili powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Garam masala|garam masala]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| &frac12; cup [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and stalks, chopped\n| 2 large [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] or &frac12; small tin of tomatoes, chopped\n| Big pinch of [[Saffron strands|saffron strands]]\n| 2 large [[Onions|onions]], peeled and chopped\n| 3 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]] or [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 20 g sliced [[Almonds|almonds]]\n| 20 g [[Sultanas|sultanas]] or [[Raisins|raisins]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] to taste\n}}\n'''Leave whole and remove before serving or pick out while eating:'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2.5 cm [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]]\n| 6 whole [[Clove|clove]]s\n| 6 whole [[Cardamom pods|cardamom pods]] ([[Brown|brown]] or white)\n| 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* In a [[Food processor|food processor]], grind the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] to a paste.  Grind the whole [[Spices|spices]] in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]].  Mix well into the [[Yogurt|yogurt]] and use to [[Marinate|marinate]] the [[Chicken|chicken]], preferably overnight.\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4)\n\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Biriani ready for the oven.jpg|Ready for the oven\nImage:Biriani reducing.jpg|Most of the liquid cooked off\nImage:Biriani marinade.jpg|The chicken pieces marinading - I wish the smell of this could be captured in a photograph!\nImage:Biriani recipe.jpg|The original (curry stained) recipe\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] in half of the [[Oil|oil]], until golden, then remove half of the onions with a slotted spoon and reserve.\n| [[Brown]] the remainder of the [[Onions|onions]], stir in the [[Meat|meat]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for 5 minutes. Add the chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and cook on a low heat until the [[Meat|meat]] is cooked and tender. Add more liquid if needed, but by the time the meat is cooked, most of the liquid should have cooked off.\n| Add half of the chopped [[Coriander|coriander]] or [[Parsley|parsley]], season with [[Salt|salt]] and set aside.\n| In a large pan of [[Boiling|boiling]] water, cook the washed [[Rice|rice]] for 10 minutes only.  Drain and reserve. The final cooking will be done in the [[Oven|oven]].\n| Grease the base of a large [[Oven|oven]]-proof [[Casserole|casserole]] with a little [[Ghee|ghee]].\n| Using the cooked [[Rice|rice]], [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Coriander|coriander]], cooked [[Onions|onions]], [[Saffron|saffron]] and dabs of [[Ghee|ghee]], fill the [[Casserole|casserole]] in layers. \n| Top with [[Raisins|raisins]] or [[Sultanas|sultanas]] and sliced [[Almonds|almonds]], add a few dabs of [[Ghee|ghee]] and cover with [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]]\n| Cook for 17 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Chana daal|lentil curry]] or [[Salad|salad]] of your choice.\n===Chef's notes===\nUse [[Parsley|parsley]] if you cannot get [[Coriander|coriander]]\n==See also==\n* [[Lamb biriani]]\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Mauritian recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onions #ghee #chickenbiriani #coriander #rice #yogurt #chicken #almonds #ginger #raisins #sultanas #Biryani #biriani #beriani</code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

Don't burn the garlic\n| Reduce heat and add all the spices and fry for a few minutes\n| Add chicken portions and fry for a few minutes\n| Add &#189; cup of stock or water, cover and simmer for 20 to 25 minutes\n| Add the creamed coconut and [[tomato puree]] and stir until the coconut has mixed well.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Pulao rice|pulao rice]] or [[Plain rice|plain boiled rice]].\n===Variations===\nAdd boiled cubed [[potatoes]] at the end\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]][[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]][[Category:Main courses]][[Category:Poultry recipes]][[Category:Indian recipes]][[Category:Spicy recipes]][[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlic #tomatopuree #turmeric #chillies #chickenstock #cumin #boiledorsimmered #cinnamon #pulaorice #clarification #coriander </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Just a different version of chicken curry!\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2743\n|PortionCalories = 685\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 55 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 40 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Chicken curry (2) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I'll say Julia!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Very different, and very nice.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\nWell, what can I say? [[Peas|peas]], [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]] and [[Broccoli|broccoli]]. title": "Chicken jambalaya",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chicken jambalaya, | Cajun recipes from the cook's Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chickenjambalaya #chicken #stock #onion #bayleaf #celery #rice #worchestersauce #ham #butter #parsley \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Jambalaya always brings to mind the Carpenters song; Jambalaya (On the Bayou) - this is what they were singing about\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1847\n|PortionCalories = 307\n|DatePublished=2nd January 2013\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Chicken jambalaya with chorizo\n|Servings = 6 people\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 2 hours 15 minutes\n|PrepTime = 1 hour 15 minutes<br />(includes cooking a chicken)\n|CookTime = 1 hour\n|Image = [[Image:Chicken jambalaya recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">So this is what it is</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Until I first made this I had no idea what Jambalaya was.  It's nice - a one-pot rice dish.  Simples!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nJambalaya always brings to mind the Carpenters song; ''Jambalaya (On the Bayou)''  Not a Carpenters song but a dish traditionally made in one pot, with [[Meats|meats]] and [[Vegetables|vegetables]]. It is completed by adding [[Stock|stock]] and [[Rice|rice]].  Looking at various recipes in more detail, this strikes me now as a typical leftover dish.  Cooking up what you have around at the time.\n===Making this your own recipe===\nWhen I made this for the first time, not having the slightest idea what jambalaya was, it looked quite complex, however, having made it many times now I now think it is probably one of the easiest recipes around. It is also a brilliant recipe to adapt to your own personal taste.  It is also an excellent recipe for using up leftovers.\n\nJust follow a few basic steps and you will be able to make you own version of this recipe.\n* Rinse the rice in cold running water first.\n* Fry the onions, garlic and vegetables first, plus any meat that might need more cooking than the rice does.\n* Ensure the rice is well coated in the oil before adding any stock.\n* Measure the stock by doubling the volume of the rice (4 cups of water to 2 cups of rice, etc.)\n* Don't add all of the stock at once, add more if it looks as though it will dry out before the rice is done.\n* If you have ingredients that don't need much cooking (prawns etc.) or vegetables that you want to serve with a bit of a crunch then add them during the last five minutes of cooking.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 x 2kg (4 lb) [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Parson's nose|parson's nose removed]]\n| A few [[Bay leaf|bay leaves]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], unpeeled, chopped into quarters\n| About 200 g from one or more of cooked meat\n| 40 g (1 &frac12; oz) [[Butter|butter]], [[ghee]] or [[olive oil]]\n| 4 to 7 [[Cloves garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 6 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Chopped on the diagonal|chopped on the diagonal]]\n| 2 sticks of [[Celery|celery]], 'strings' removed with a [[Mandoline|mandoline]] and chopped into moons\n| 3 or 4 sweet [[Bell peppers|bell peppers]], any colour, deseeded and chopped\n| 3 teaspoons [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon of [[dried oregano]] or [[dried mixed herbs]]\n| 2 tablespoons fresh [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]], chopped, if available\n| 1 large can [[Plum|plum]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], chopped\n| 500ml to 600 ml of the water the [[Chicken|chicken]] was [[Boiled|boiled]] in\n| 1 tablespoon [[Worcester sauce|Worcester sauce]]\n| [[Chillies]], [[chilli sauce]] or [[chilli powder]] to add warmth, not heat.\n|* I used: 1 teaspoon chili guajillo (powder), 2 teaspoons pasilla chili (diced), 1/2 a teaspoon of chipotle chillies (diced)\n|* Suggested alternative if using sauce: 1 to 2 tablespoons [[Louisiana hot pepper sauce]] (or to taste)\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 400 g (14 oz) [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]] ([[Long grain rice|long grain rice]])\n}}\n''' Garnish'''\n* Finely chopped [[Parsley|parsley]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Remove any giblets, cut off and discard the [[Parson's nose]].\n| Wash the [[Chicken|chicken]] under cold running water, inside and out\n| Place the [[Chicken|chicken]] in a large pot and pour over just enough [[Boiling|boiling]] water to cover\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and the [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]] and [[Boil|boil]] for about 1 hour or until tender\n| Set the [[Chicken|chicken]] to one side, reserve the [[Stock|stock]] and discard the [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]] and [[Onion|onion]] quarters\n| Once chicken has cooled discard skin and bone\n| Heat the [[Butter|butter]] in a large pan and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] for a few minutes\n| Add the [[Ham|ham]], [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Celery|celery]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Saut\u00e9|saut\u00e9]] for 5 minutes\n| Rinse rice under cold running water for a few minutes until the water runs clear\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a minute so the grains are coated by the oil\n| Add the [[Stock|stock]] (about 500 ml to start), [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Spices|spices]], [[Worcester sauce|Worcester sauce]], [[Hot pepper sauce|hot pepper sauce]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Chicken|chicken]]\n| Stir well, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] on a very low hob until the liquid has gone and the [[Rice|rice]] is cooked.  Add a little more water if it dries out before the rice is done.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chicken jambalaya in pot.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chicken jambalaya, ready to cook\nImage:Chicken jambalaya boil.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chicken, ready to boil\n</gallery>\n===Variations===\nI raided the garden for anything to add to the chicken boil: a few [[carrots]], some [[leeks]] a few spare sticks of [[celery]] and bunches of [[parsley]].\n===Chef's notes===\nI have doubled the rice quantity from the original recipe as there was so little rice.  I have not quite doubled the stock quantity so keep an eye on the water level to ensure that it does not dry out.\n\nRather than using [[chili sauce]] for the heat I used a mixture of my [[Exotic chili powders]] to add more than just heat.  The quantities I used did not make this hot (like a chili), just a little warmth.\n\nThe [[stock]] left from cooking the chicken is really good quality so whatever you don't use, freeze in bags or cups far later use.\n\n==See also==\n* http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jambalaya\n* http://www.bbcgoodfood.com/recipes/1167651/chicken-and-chorizo-jambalaya\n* http://www.deliaonline.com/recipes/type-of-dish/one-pot-meals/chicken-jambalaya.html\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:North American recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chickenjambalaya #chicken #stock #onion #bayleaf #celery #rice #worchestersauce #ham #butter #parsley </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
