                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chicken tikka, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chickentikka #chicken #marinade #turmeric #coriander #cayennepepper #chillipowder #lockandlock #lime #lemonjuice #redchilipowder \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Tandoori Chicken is a chicken dish that originated in the Punjab region of the Indian subcontinent\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1252\n|PortionCalories = 313\n|DatePublished=16th November 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Using whole chicken pieces\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 9 hours 25 minutes\n|PrepTime = 9 hours+\n|CookTime = 25 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Tandoori chicken recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Colourful chicken</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Much nicer than anything you can buy in the shops.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nTandoori Chicken is a chicken dish that originated in the Punjab region of the Indian subcontinent.  [[Cayenne pepper]], [[red chili powder]], or other spices give it a red hue. A higher amount of [[turmeric]] produces a yellow-orange colour. In some modern versions, [[Tandoori red food colouring]] is often used. It is traditionally cooked at high temperatures in an earthen oven (tandoor), but can also be prepared on a traditional grill or a very hot oven. This dish is also popular among Hindi, Bengali, and Urdu speaking Indian states like West Bengal & Andra Pradesh. In Pakistan it is eaten with [[naan breads]] and, in Bangladesh, with [[rice]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1 lb) Skinless [[chicken]] breasts\n| &#189; teaspoon [[sea salt]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[tandoori colouring]] (optional)\n| 2 cloves [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 1 thumb size piece of [[ginger]], peeled and grated finely - use any juice too.\n| &#189; teaspoon [[garam masala]]\n| &#189; teaspoon grated [[nutmeg]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[chilli powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon ground [[turmeric]]\n| 150g thick natural [[yogurt]] , about 150 g (5 oz) \n| 3 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n| 4 sprigs [[coriander]]\n| Juice from and zest from a [[lemon]] or [[lime]]\n| Bamboo or wooden [[skewers]]\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chicken tikka marinaded in a lock and lock box.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Marinaded chicken pieces, shaken not stirred!\nImage:Chicken tikka ready to marinate.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chicken pieces ready to marinate, the easy way\n</gallery>\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Soak the skewers in cold water\n| Cut the [[chicken]] into 5 cm (2\") cubes\n| Place the cubed chicken in a bowl, add the [[lemon juice]] and the [[salt]] and mix well. This marinade helps to tenderise the [[chicken]]\n| Leave in a [[refrigerator]] for 30 minutes. Leaving it longer won't hurt. \n| Mix the remaining ingredients in a [[food processor]] and blend until smooth\n| Cover the [[chicken]] pieces in the spice mix, cover and marinate for 8 hours or overnight in the refrigerator\n| '''Preheat the [[oven]] to [220\u00b0C (425\u00b0F) Gas 7]'''\n| Place the cubed [[chicken]] on the skewers, leaving a small space between each piece to ensure they cook evenly\n| Cook in the top third of the oven for 10 minutes, then remove and brush with the [[marinade]]. Rotate and return for a further 10 minutes\n| Remove from the oven and rest for 5 minutes before serving\n}}\n===Chef's tip===\nUse a [[Lock and Lock]] style box at the marinading stage to coat the chicken quickly and evenly.  Just add the chicken and the marinade to the [[Lock and Lock box]], close the lid and shake well.  It's then ready to go straight in the [[fridge]] and can be mixed by shaking every now and the.\n\n===Variations===\n\nServe with [[chicken tikka masala]]\n\nCook on a very hot [[barbecue]]\n\nYou can use whole [[chicken]] pieces in this recipe.\n\nCut slits in the [[chicken]] pieces and rub the [[marinade]] well into the chicken.\n\nYou can cook at the top of the oven [220\u00b0C (425\u00b0F) Gas 7] for about 25 minutes in total if using pieces.  Check that they are properly cooked before eating.\n\nTry [[joint your own chicken|jointing your chicken]].\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with rice and a [[naan bread]]\n==See also==\n* [[Chicken tikka (cheat)]]\n* [[Chicken tikka masala]]\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Marinaded]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chickentikka #chicken #marinade #turmeric #coriander #cayennepepper #chillipowder #lockandlock #lime #lemonjuice #redchilipowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

title": "Chicken tikka (cheat)",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chicken tikka (cheat), Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #marinade #yogurt #currypaste #chickentikka #lemonjuice #dip #greensalad #naturalyogurt #barbecue #marinading \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is a really simple way to make chicken tikka, (tandoori chicken)\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1037\n|PortionCalories = 259\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = 4 with rice other dishes\n|ImageComment = Chicken tikka, [[green salad]], [[naan bread]] & [[yogurt]]\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  2 days, 40 minutes\n|PrepTime =  2 days, 10 minutes\n|CookTime = 30 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Chicken tikka (cheat) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Lovely</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">As good as any restaurant!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is a really simple way to make [[Chicken tikka|chicken tikka]], (''tandoori chicken''). All you need are [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces, a pot of [[Yogurt|yogurt]] and a jar of ready made ''[[Curry paste|curry paste]]''.  I've used vindaloo paste but you could use whatever you fancy.\n\nThe long you can leave the chicken pieces [[Marinading|marinading]], the better it will be.  I try to leave it a few days if I have managed to think that far ahead.\n\nThis will be cooked in an oven but could just as easily be cooked under a [[Grill|grill]], or on a [[barbecue]] grid or hot-plate.\n\nWe have a more authentic [[Chicken tikka|chicken tikka]] recipe here if you want to make it from scratch.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 [[Chicken|chicken]] legs and 4 [[chicken]] thighs (or similar selection)\n| 500g pot of [[Natural yogurt|natural yogurt]]\n| 3 tablespoons of your favourite [[Curry paste|curry paste]]\n| [[Lemon juice]] (optional)\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] (optional)\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chicken tikka (cheat)_resting.jpg|Rest for 4 minutes then serve\nImage:Chicken tikka (cheat)_ready_to_cook.jpg|After 2 days its ready to cook\nImage:Chicken tikka (cheat)_yogurt_curry_paste.jpg|Add the curry paste to the yogurt\nImage:Chicken tikka (cheat)_cut slashes.jpg|Cut deep slashes into the chicken pieces\nImage:Chicken tikka (cheat)_ingredients.jpg|Chicken tikka, the simplest of ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| I like to remove the skin and trim any [[Fat|fat]].  The [[Marinade|marinade]] gets better penetration without the skin on and it's also a little healthier.\n| Cut 3 or 4 deep slashes down to the bone on each piece.  This ensures really good coverage of the [[Marinade|marinade]].\n| Optionally you can [[Marinade|marinade]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces in [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] and a good pinch of [[Salt|salt]] for a few hours before adding the [[Yogurt|yogurt]] [[Marinade|marinade]].  This [[Tenderise|tenderises]] the chicken.\n| Mix 2 to 3 tablespoons of your favourite [[Curry paste|curry paste]] into about two thirds of the [[Yogurt|yogurt]].  You don't need any more yogurt for this recipe so it leaves a little spare to make a [[Dip|dip]] or dressing to go with the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces.\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces and the [[Marinade|marinade]] to a [[Lock and Lock]] style box.  replace the lid and shake like mad.\n| [[Refrigerate]] for a few days if possible shaking it now and then.\n| When you are ready to cook them, preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7), [fan oven 200\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n| Cook on a grid over a foil-lined oven tray at the top of the [[Oven|oven]] for about 25 to 30 minutes, turning once. Check the chicken is properly cooked, rest for 4 or 5 minutes then serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Plain rice|plain rice]], a simple [[Green salad|green salad]] and the remaining [[Yogurt|yogurt]] as a [[Dip|dip]].\n===Variations===\nStart with this [[Cheat|cheat]] recipe and tailor it to your liking by adding extra [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Spices|spices]].  I'm sure that you get the idea.\n==See also==\n* [[Chicken tikka]]\n* [[Chicken tikka masala]]\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n[[Category:Student recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinaded]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #marinade #yogurt #currypaste #chickentikka #lemonjuice #dip #greensalad #naturalyogurt #barbecue #marinading </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

These take a while to prepare but are most definitely worth the effort.  Whatever else you put on the kebab sticks is up to your personal taste.\n\nWe've chosen [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]] and [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]].\n\nAs I've recently bought a selection of Mae Ploy [[Curry|curry]] pastes, I've used the Mae Ploy [[Massaman curry]] paste in this recipe.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n}}\n====kebabs====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| One massive [[Chicken breast|chicken breast]] fillet\n| Two [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]], any colour\n| 24 [[Button mushrooms|button mushrooms]]\n}}\n====marinade====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 4 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 250g [[Greek yogurt]]\n| 2 teaspoons Mae Play [[Massaman curry]] paste\n| 1 teaspoon soft [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n}}\n====marinade====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix all of the [[Marinade|marinade]] ingredients together in a [[Lock & Lock box]] and stir really well to ensure they are properly mixed\n| Cut the [[Chicken|chicken]] into bite-sized pieces and add to the [[Marinade|marinade]]\n| Cover and shake hard so the [[Chicken|chicken]] is evenly coated\n| Leave to [[Marinade|marinade]] for about 5 hours, shaking now and then if you can\n}}\n====kebabs====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| While you assemble the [[Kebabs|kebabs]], preheat you [[Grill|grill]] to maximum\n| Deseed the [[Peppers|peppers]] and cut into squares so they 'fit' the [[Kebabs|kebabs]]\n| Slide the [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] slices onto your [[Kebab|kebab]] sticks - metal [[Skewers|skewers]] work well for us\n| Arrange over a [[Foil|foil]]-lined [[Oven tray|oven tray]] and coat with any spare [[Marinade|marinade]]\n| [[Grill]] for 15 minutes, turning once\n| [[Rest for]] 5 minutes before serving\n}}\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Vegetable|vegetable]] [[Rice|rice]] or [[Pittas|pittas]] and a [[Salad|salad]]\n===Variations===\n[[Cherry tomatoes]], slices of [[Fruit|fruit]] and slices of [[Red onion|red onion]] and [[Olives|olives]] go well on these [[Kebabs|kebabs]].\n===Chef's notes===\nThese would be perfect for a [[Barbecue|barbecue]] too, though not for us as it's snowing at the moment!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Greek recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Marinaded]]\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#marinade #chicken #kebabs #massamancurry #sweetpeppers #chickentikkakebabs #grill #mushrooms #rice #limejuice #olives</code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It takes a bit of time and it's a bit of a fiddle but\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1846\n|PortionCalories = 461\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 35 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Chicken tikka masala recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Worth taking time over</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">The Indian classic (that's probably more English\ud83d\udc68, than Indian\ud83d\udc73)</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nAdd this creamy sauce to [[chicken tikka]] pieces and you'll have the ladies favourite Indian meal!\n\nIt takes a bit of time and it's a bit of a fiddle but it's worth it for that special occasion.  Oh, and men like it too!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 cm (1/2 \") peeled root [[ginger]], grated\n| 2 cloves [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 50 g (2 oz) [[butter]]\n| 1 [[onion]], finely chopped\n| &#189; teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon ground [[white cumin]]\n| &#189; teaspoon ground [[black cumin]] (optional)\n| &#189; teaspoon [[ground coriander]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[garam masala]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[chili powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[tandoori colouring]] (very optional)\n| 4 tablespoons [[coconut milk]] or a 2 cm (1\") block of [[creamed coconut block]]\n| 112 ml (4 fl oz) liquid from pre cooked [[chicken tikka masala]] (or [[chicken stock]])\n| 150 ml [[double cream]]\n| 2 heaped teaspoons of ground [[almonds]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[ghee]] or [[vegetable oil]] for frying\n| Pinch of [[salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[ginger]] together with the [[salt]]\n| Gently fry the [[onions]] in the [[ghee]] or [[vegetable oil]] for 4 minutes\n| Add the [[ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] an cook for a further 2 minutes\n| Add the powdered [[spices]] and cook for anther 2 minutes\n| Pour in the stock, [[coconut]] block and the [[cream]] and heat gently, stirring until the [[coconut block]] has melted. Don't boil.\n| Add the cooked [[tandoori chicken]] pieces and simmer gently for 5 minutes so the sauce permiates the meat.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with rice and a [[naan bread]]\n===Variations===\n\nServe with tandoori lamb or tandoori prawns instead of [[chicken tikka]]\n==See also==\n* [[Chicken tikka]]\n* [[Chicken tikka (cheat)]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chickentikkamasala #garlic #ginger #chickentikka #ghee #vegetableoil #creamedcoconutblock #turmericpowder #naanbread #groundcoriander #coconutblock </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

The cuisine of the Mumbai based East Indians also includes a variation of the dish. However, it is known globally in its Anglo Indian form as a staple of curry house menus.  Make this one at home!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 tablespoons of [[ghee]] or [[vegetable oil]]\n| 2 medium onions, peeled and chopped\n| 6 chicken pieces (legs or breast - skin removed)\n}}\n\n'''marinade'''\n* &#189; teaspoon of [[salt]]\n* &#189; teaspoon freshly ground [[Black peppercorns|black pepper]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[turmeric]]\n* 4 whole cloves, ground\n* &#189; teaspoon [[Cinnamon|cinnamon powder]] or &#190;\" of rolled [[Cinnamon|cinnamon stick]], ground\n* 1 teaspoon [[turmeric]] powder\n* &#189; teaspoon [[mustard]] powder\n* 1 teaspoon of [[black mustard seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[Chillies|chili powder]] (or to taste)\n* 2 teaspoons [[paprika]] powder\n* 1 teaspoon freshly ground [[Cumin|cumin]] seeds\n* 2 teaspoons [[tomato puree]]\n* 2 teaspoons [[sugar]]\n* &#189; teaspoon ground [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]] seeds\n* 1\" [[Ginger|ginger]], grated\n* 2 cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]]\n* 2 tablespoons brandy ([[sherry]] will do)\n* 2 tablespoons [[malt vinegar]] (leftover red wine works)\n* 1 [[Chillies|whole dried chili]], crushed\n\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Make a paste with all of the marinade spices, brandy and vinegar\n| Cut a few slashes right down to the bone in each piece to allow the marinade to penetrate.\n| Put the marinade and the chicken pieces in a [[Lock and Lock]]-style box, fit the lid and shake like mad!\n| Marinade overnight in a [[refrigerator]]\n| Fry the onions in a tablespoon of [[Clarification|ghee]] until brown\n| Fry the meat for a few minutes with the [[onion]]\n| Cover, lower the heat and cook gently for 35 to 40 minutes\n| Add a little water or chicken stock if it starts to dry out.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chicken vindaloo cooked.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Cooked with a little water added\nImage:Chicken vindaloo marinading.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chicken pieces marinading in a Lock and Lock box\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[Plain rice| plain boiled rice]] and a [[Mint_and_onion_raita|mint and onion raita]].\n\n===Chef's notes===\n\nRecently made this with 3 large dried [[chile de \u00e1rbol]] (powdered) and no chilli powder.  It was warm and spicy with a bite, but not too hot.\n\n==See also==\n* A selection of [[Vindaloo|vindaloo recipes]]\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chickenvindaloo #chillies #turmeric #cinnamon #tomatopuree #boiledorsimmered #onion #garlic #blackmustardseeds #ginger #sherry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

To be taken in a shady corner of the garden, and then to sleep...\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 pint good quality [[chicken stock]]\n| 4 [[spring onions]](scallions), [[chopped on the diagonal]]\n| 2 bunches fresh [[watercress]], washed and chopped\n| 6 [[mint]] leaves\n| 6 fl oz (168 ml) [[milk]]\n| 2 tablespoons ground [[almonds]]\n| 4 fl oz (112 ml) [[single cream]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[sea salt]]\n| &#188; teaspoon ground [[white pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Skim any excess fat from the [[chicken stock]]\n| Add to a large pan and bring to the boil, add the [[spring onions]] and watercress, reduce the heat and simmer gently\n| Add a little of the [[milk]] to the ground [[almonds]] to make a paste and add the paste to the remaining [[milk]]\n| Add the [[milk]] to the soup and once it has returned to a simmer, stir until the soup begins to thicken slightly\n| Remove from the heat and allow to cool\n| Once cool enough, blend the soup in a [[food processor]]\n| Season to taste with [[salt]] and [[pepper]]\n| Chill in the [[fridge]] until ready to serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe cold in bowls.  Give each bowl a stir as you add the [[cream]] to get an arty swirl. Garnish with a [[Mint|mint leaf]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Almond]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Almond]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Almond]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes|Almond]]\n[[Category:Starters|Almond]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chilledwatercressandalmondsoup #chickenstock #mint #almonds #springonions #foodprocessor #whitepepper #singlecream #cream #watercress #boiledorsimmered </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It is fairly hot\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 712\n|PortionCalories = 178\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Chilli and garlic dip recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n======Best recipe review======\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice dip Julia</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">We make this regularly</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]]</span></span>\n}}\nThis can be served as a [[Dip|dip]] and a [[Sauce|sauce]]. title": "Chingri malai roti",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chingri malai roti, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chingrimalairoti #rice #kingprawns #garlic #basil #ghee #grill #limejuice #desiccatedcoconut #grated #ginger \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Chingri malai roti - king prawn roti: (rice cake with king prawns)\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 656\n|PortionCalories = 164\n|DatePublished=8th December 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Chingri malai roti after grilling, sprinkled with toasted sesame seeds\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Chingri malai roti grilled.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">YOU MUST MAKE THIS!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Without a shadow of doubt this is the best Indian recipe, ever.  his, and the other variants listed are just sublime.  Make the effort to make it.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Chingri malai roti mixed.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chingri malai roti - prawns mixed in and ready to fry]]\n[[Image:Murghi roti ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The ingredients for [[Murghi roti]] - ''very similar'']]\n[[Image:Action coconut scraper with vacuum suction base.jpg|300px|thumb|right|An easier way to prepare the grated coconut - [http://www.amazon.co.uk/gp/product/B00B7JDDL6?psc=1&redirect=true&ref_=oh_aui_detailpage_o07_s00 Action coconut scraper with vacuum suction base - \u00a38.98 Amazon UK]]]\nChingri malai roti - [[king prawn]] [[roti]]: ([[Rice|rice]] cake with [[king prawns]]).  This is my variation on [[Murghi roti]] but using king prawns instead of chicken.\n\nTry this using two pans, see Chef's notes below.\n\nPlease be very careful if storing cooked [[Rice|rice]].  [[Refrigerate]] the moment it has cooled and use within 1 day\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 200 g (8 oz) uncooked [[basmati rice]].\n| 1 pack of [[king prawns]] - about 200 / 300 g\n| 2 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]] or vegetable [[Oil|oil]]\n| 5 [[Fat|fat]] [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 5 cm (2\") [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and roughly [[Grated|grated]]\n| 75 g (5 oz) [[Onions|onions]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 fresh [[coconut]], flesh [[Grated|grated]] - don't be too precise with the grating, it's quite nice to have some meaty chunks mixed in.\n| 4 hot [[Chilli peppers|chilli peppers]] (red or green), finely chopped - de-seeded if desired\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n| Fresh [[basil]] leaves, chopped or roughly torn.\n}}\n'''spices'''\n\n''don't grind the spices, leave them whole''\n* 2 teaspoons whole [[coriander seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon whole [[cumin seeds]] (white)\n* 1/2 a teaspoon of whole [[fenugreek seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Quickly wash and drain the [[rice]] but don't rinse it as you normally would, this dish is best with rice of a starchy consistency. \n| Cook in boiling water for 7 to 11 minutes.\n| Rinse the cooked rice in cold water until it is cold.  Drain well.\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade and blend to a thick creamy pur\u00e9e - adding a little milk if required to make it thinner.  Remember, the inside is not going to change much whilst being cooked and will remain at roughly the same consistency as it was when first mixed. \n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a [[frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] all of the [[Spices|spices]] for half a minute, then add the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and allow them to cook for a minute or so.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and reduce the heat a little and let them cook until translucent; about 5 minutes.\n| Add the raw deveined [[king prawns]], [[Coconut|coconut]] and [[Chilli|chilli]] to the [[Onions|onions]], mix well and immediately remove from the heat.\n| Lightly [[Oil|oil]] a large non-stick oven proof [[Frying pan|frying pan]] put on a medium heat.\n| Add the [[prawn]] mix to the [[Rice|rice]] pur\u00e9e and tip this into the pan.\n| Ensure the mixture is evenly distributed and patted down, then cook for about 10 minutes or until the [[Rice|rice]] cake has properly solidified and the base has started to toast - a little burning is quite nice as it leaves a nice chewy, toasted flavour.\n| Preheat the [[Grill|grill]].\n| [[Brown|brown]] under the hot [[Grill|grill]] just to colour the top surface a little.\n| Sprinkle with [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and fresh [[basil]] leaves and serve immediately.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nHaving made this many, many times now, I'm coming to the conclusion that the best part is the glorious toasted crunchy outsides.  In future I will use two pans and made two thinner individual rotis.\n\nI heeded [[Preparing a coconut|my own advice]] and tasted the coconut before preparing it.  It was totally rancid, thank you Morrisons.  Luckily I had both [[coconut flakes]] and [[desiccated coconut]]. For two people, I used two big handfuls of flakes and 4 tablespoons of [[desiccated coconut]] soaked in boiling water for 5 minutes then drained in a sieve.  It worked fine and saved the day!\n\n===Variations===\nInstead of fresh [[green chillies]], I have used 3/4 teaspoon of diced [[ancho]] & 3/4 teaspoon diced [[chipotle]] (dried) [[chillies]].\n\nDoing a 'freezer clean out', we made a marvellous version of this with 1 [[chicken]] breast and a bag of cooked red kidney beans.  The chicken was thinly sliced and saut\u00e9ed with lots of crushed [[garlic]] and the kidney beans fried with the chicken and mashed down a little - rather like [[re-fried beans]].  This was added in place of the normally cooked chicken in this recipe.\n\n===A better way of cooking this===\nAfter making variants of this for many years, I've discovered the best method of cooking is to spread the ingredients out on a lightly greased [[baking tray]] and bake at 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7) for 35 minutes, stirring up the contents every 10 minutes.  It might be an idea with a meat other than crayfish, to add the meat (or prawns) for the last 10 minutes so they don't dry out.\n[[Image:Crayfish & coconut chili, 1.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Baking tray method shown here with [[Crayfish and coconut rice cake with hot chillies]]]]\n{{Template:SeeAlso Roti}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chingrimalairoti #rice #kingprawns #garlic #basil #ghee #grill #limejuice #desiccatedcoconut #grated #ginger </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

                "revisions": [
                    {

These coconut [[Chips|chips]] would make a novel accompaniment to a curry, as part of a selection of [[Starters|starters]] for an oriental meal or just as finger snacks with drinks.\n\nThey can be [[Frozen|frozen]] in Tupperware-type containers so it's practical to process 3 or 4 [[Coconuts|coconuts]] at a time.\n====Top Tip!====\nTaste the coconut to check that it has not gone rancid before you start.  It is a more common problem than you might think.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 fresh [[Coconut|coconut]]\n| [[Salt]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Drain the [[Coconut|coconut]] of [[Juice|juice]] by piercing one of the eyes or breaking it over a sink\n| [[Preparing a coconut|Break the coconut into two halves]].\n| With a broad-bladed knife, carefully prise big lumps of the flesh away from the shell\n| If you wish you can peel the [[Brown|brown]] skin away with a [[Potato peeler|potato peeler]]\n| Using a [[Mandoline|mandoline]], [[Food processor|food processor]] or exceptional knife skills, slice into wafer-thin shavings\n| If freezing the coconut chips, freeze at this point. They can be cooked from frozen but may take a little longer\n| Spread these evenly on one or two [[Baking|baking]] sheets, sprinkle with a little [[Salt|salt]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 30 minutes until crisp\n| Allow to cool then serve\n}}\n===Variations===\nUse lightly flavoured [[Salt|salt]] for a spicy version \n==See also==\n* [[Preparing a coconut|preparing a fresh coconut]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#coconutchips #coconut #chips #potatopeeler #bake #coconuts #starters #mandoline #juice #baking #miseenplace </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

You need a fresh [[coconut]] for this though, so down to the market or off to the funfair!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 fresh [[coconut]]\n| 400 ml (14 fl oz) tinned [[coconut milk]] (unsweetened)\n| 400 ml (14 fl oz) good [[chicken stock]] or a Knorr [[chicken stock]] cube in [[boiling]] water\n| 225 g (8 oz)  fragrant [[basmati rice]] (or any long-grain [[rice]])\n| 115 g (4 oz) freshly [[grated]] [[coconut]] flesh\n|* See our [[Preparing a coconut|step by step instructions for cracking open preparing a coconut]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Bring the coconut [[milk]] and [[stock]] to the [[boil]] in a large pan\n| Rinse the [[rice]] in a sieve under cold running water until it runs clear\n| Add the [[rice]] to the [[stock]], stir once, reduce the heat, cover and [[simmer]] for 25 minutes. Don't fiddle with it!\n| Remove from the heat and leave covered for 10 minutes to absorb all of the liquid\n| Heat a [[wok]] without [[oil]] and roast the [[coconut]] until it turns golden\n| Fluff the [[rice]] up with a fork and sprinkle the [[coconut]] over the top\n}}\n===Coconut shredder working in a 10 second video=== \n<YouTube>https://youtu.be/-0Ha0o0Xy5Q</YouTube>\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #coconut #coconutrice #chickenstock #stock #boil #boiledorsimmered #grated #simmer #coconutmilk #boiling </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Crayfish and coconut rice cake with hot chillies",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Crayfish & coconut roti with chillies \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#rice #ghee #crayfishandcoconutricecakewithhotchillies #ginger #grated #turmericpowder #onions #coconut #basil #limejuice #tomatoes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Crayfish and coconut rice cake with hot chillies\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 901\n|PortionCalories = 225\n|DatePublished=9th July 2017\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Served with lime juice and fresh basil\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes\n |CookTime = 45 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Crayfish & coconut chili, served.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">So spicy! \ud83c\udf36\ud83c\udf36\ud83c\udf36</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Another of my favourite dishes, ever. \ud83c\udf5b</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry, aka Chef]])</span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Crayfish & coconut chili, 1.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Well mixed up, 5 minutes to go...]]\n[[Image:Crayfish & coconut chili, 2.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Add the tomatoes after about 15 minutes cooking]]\n[[Image:Morrison's crayfish tails.jpg|thumb|300px|right|[https://groceries.morrisons.com/webshop/product/Big-Prawn-Company-Big-Juicy-Cray-Fish-Tails/272024011?from=search&tags=%7C105651&param=crayfish&parentContainer=SEARCHcrayfish_SHELFVIEW Morrison's Crayfish tails] \u00a33.75 per 120g pack]]\n[[Image:Action coconut scraper with vacuum suction base.jpg|300px|thumb|right|An easier way to prepare the grated coconut - [http://www.amazon.co.uk/gp/product/B00B7JDDL6?psc=1&redirect=true&ref_=oh_aui_detailpage_o07_s00 Action coconut scraper with vacuum suction base - \u00a38.98 Amazon UK]]]\nThis is another variation on one of my '''most favourite spicy recipes'''.  [[Crayfish]] work exceptionally well in this recipe as they don't seem to dry out in the high heat.\n\nThe other roti recipes in the ''see also'' section were prepared in a frying pan.  This time I used a large [[grill tray]], a far better method.  It allows the rice to ''just'' crisp up a little, leaving very little stodgy rice.\n\nPlease be very careful if storing cooked [[Rice|rice]].  [[Refrigerate]] the moment it has cooled and use within 1 day\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 170 g uncooked [[basmati rice]].\n| 240 g Crayfish tails (2 packs)\n| 2 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]] or vegetable [[Oil|oil]]\n| 5 [[Fat|fat]] [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 5 cm (2\") [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and roughly [[Grated|grated]]\n| 75 g (5 oz) [[Onions|onions]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 fresh [[coconut]], flesh [[Grated|grated]] - don't be too precise with the grating, it's quite nice to have some meaty chunks mixed in.\n| 4 hot [[Chilli peppers|chilli peppers]] (2 red, 2 green), finely chopped - 2 with seeds, 2 partially deseeded worked very well for us. (quite spicy)\n}}\n'''spices'''\n\n''don't grind the spices, leave them whole''\n* 2 teaspoons whole [[coriander seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon whole [[cumin seeds]] (white)\n* 1 teaspoon whole [[fenugreek seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n'''to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB| 6 small [[cherry tomatoes]], halved\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n| Fresh [[basil]] leaves, chopped or roughly torn.\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\nPreheat your oven to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7), [fan oven 200\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\nPlace a lightly oiled baking tray in the top third of the oven\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Quickly wash and drain the [[rice]] but don't rinse it as you normally would, this dish is best with rice of a starchy consistency. \n| Cook in boiling water until it just has a little ''bite'' left.  About 7 to 11 minutes.\n| Rinse the cooked rice in cold water until it is cold.  Drain well.\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] and the [[turmeric powder]] to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade and blend to a thick creamy pur\u00e9e - adding a little milk if required to make it thinner.  Remember, the texture is not going to change much whilst being cooked and will remain at roughly the same consistency as it was when first mixed. \n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a [[frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] all of the whole [[Spices|spices]] for half a minute, then add the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and allow them to cook for a minute or so.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and reduce the heat a little and let them cook until translucent; about 5 minutes.\n| Add a little more [[oil]] or [[ghee]] if the mixture looks dry.\n| Add the whole [[crayfish tails]], [[Coconut|coconut]] and [[Chilli|chillies]] to the [[Onions|onions]], mix well and immediately remove from the heat.\n| Add all of the ingredients, apart from the tomatoes, fresh basil and lime juice to a large bowl and mix very well.\n| Carefully spread the mixture over the hot [[baking tray]]\n| Bake for 25 to 35 minutes, adding the [[tomatoes]] about half way through and stirring well every 10 minutes.\n| The nicest results are when the rice ''just'' crisps and gets a nice chewy, toasted flavour. Be careful though - it spoils if it burns!\n| Sprinkle with [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and fresh [[basil]] leaves and serve immediately.\n}}\n\n{{Template:SeeAlso Roti}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #ghee #crayfishandcoconutricecakewithhotchillies #ginger #grated #turmericpowder #onions #coconut #basil #limejuice #tomatoes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Cumin rice",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Cumin rice, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cuminrice #rice #cuminseeds #ghee #vegetablestock #boiling #sieve #corianderleaves #blackcumin #vegetableoil #miseenplace \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I had not heard of cumin rice until I started to add recipes to the Mauritian recipe section. It's quite unusual and very nice\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 630\n|PortionCalories = 315\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 5 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Cumin rice recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Makes a nice change</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Very odd idea, but it works very well.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Cumin rice steaming cloth.jpg|thumb|250px|right|Place a cloth between the pan and the lid]]\nI had not heard of '''cumin rice''' until I started to add recipes to the [[:Category:Mauritian recipes|Mauritian recipe section]].  It's quite unusual and very nice.  The cooking method makes for a more creamy textured rice and the cumin flavour is pleasant but not overpowering.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 cup of [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] or [[Ghee|ghee]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 2 teaspoons of white [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| Boiling water or [[vegetable stock]]\n| Chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] to garnish\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Rinse the [[Rice|rice]] in a [[Sieve|sieve]] under cold running water, stirring with your hands until the water runs clear. Drain well\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cook the [[Rice|rice]] in lots of [[Boiling|boiling]] water until the rice is soft on the outside but still has a tiny bite to it.  About 5 minutes\n| Remove from the heat and drain in a [[Sieve|sieve]]\n| Meanwhile, add the [[Ghee|ghee]] and [[Onions|onions]] to a large pan and saut\u00e9 until they just turn [[Brown|brown]].\n| Stir in the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]].\n| Once they start to pop, stir in the [[Rice|rice]].\n| Add half a cup of [[Boiling|boiling]] water or [[vegetable stock]], cover with a lid, placing a cloth between the pan and the lid being careful not to catch it alight!\n| [[Simmer]] gently for a further 5 minutes then remove from the heat and let it stand for 7 to 10  minutes so all of the water is absorbed.  Don't stir or mix it at all during this process.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe garnished with chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]]\n===Variations===\nAdd a small pinch of [[black cumin]] seeds as well as the [[white cumin]] seeds.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Mauritian recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cuminrice #rice #cuminseeds #ghee #vegetablestock #boiling #sieve #corianderleaves #blackcumin #vegetableoil #miseenplace </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]

Note that the carrots and onions are net weight, ie after peeling\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1647\n|PortionCalories = 411\n|DatePublished=18th January 2013\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 45 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  1 hour, 30 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Curried carrot soup recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Wierd food, very wierd</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">But bloody marvellous - the strange things are often the best!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nA lovely warming [[Soup|soup]] for autumn and winter.  Note that the [[Carrots|carrots]] and [[Onions|onions]] are net weight, ie after peeling.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 175g [[Unsalted butter|unsalted butter]]\n| 220g [[Onions|onions]], chopped\n| 2 bulbs [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and [[Cloves|cloves]] cut in half if large \n| 500g [[Carrots|carrots]], peeled and chopped into small pieces\n| A pinch each of [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Nigella|nigella seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Jalfrezi masala|jalfrezi masala]]\n| 800ml [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 1 tablespoon chopped [[Green chillies|green chillies]] or a sprig of [[parsley]], to serve\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Melt the [[Butter|butter]] in a saucepan over a low-medium heat.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Carrots|carrots]], and [[Stew|stew]] gently for about 30 minutes until they are soft, but not [[Browned|browned]].\n| Add a pinch of [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Salt|salt]] and continue cooking until the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] are beginning to caramelise.\n| Meanwhile toast the [[Cumin|cumin]] and [[Nigella|nigella]] [[Seeds|seeds]] in a [[Dry frying|dry frying]] pan until fragrant. \n| Add the [[Toasted|toasted]] [[Seeds|seeds]] and jalfrezi masala to the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and cook a further 2-3 minutes.\n| Add the [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]] and water and bring to the [[Boil|boil]]. \n| Reduce to a [[Simmer|simmer]] and cook for 30 minutes.\n| [[Blend]] the [[Soup|soup]] in a [[Blender|blender]] until smooth. \n| Season to taste and serve, sprinkled with the chopped [[Chillies|chillies]] or the [[parsley]] sprig.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a nice hunk of [[Bread|bread]].\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Based on a recipe by '''[http://www.bbc.co.uk/food/recipes/curried_carrot_soup_29946 Michael Caines]'''\n===Variations===\nInstead of stock, use water to which has been added 2 tsps [[Marigold Swiss Bouillon Powder]] or [[Bron's Spanish vegetable stock concentrate (TM)|Bron's Spanish vegetable stock concentrate]] \nUse chopped [[Coriander|coriander]] to garnish if preferred.  Adjust [[Garlic|garlic]] quantity to taste.  Use [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] if preferred and use any [[Spice|spice]] mix you like.\n===Chef's notes===\nIf it is too thick, add a little more [[stock]] or water.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Carrot soup]]\n[[Category:British recipes|Carrot soup]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Carrot soup]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Carrot soup]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes|Carrot soup]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Carrot soup]]\n[[Category:Starters|Carrot soup]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Carrot soup]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Carrot soup]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Carrot soup]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered|Carrot soup]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#curriedcarrotsoup #garlic #carrots #vegetables #seeds #parsley #vegetablestock #soup #nigella #onions #cumin </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This one comes highly recommended: Nik's email telling me about this recipe was entitled \"Possibly the best\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 878\n|PortionCalories = 219\n|DatePublished=21st May 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour\n|PrepTime =  40 minutes\n|CookTime =  20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Curry Leaf, Split Pea and Chickpea Crusted Lemon Sole with Tomato and Yoghurt Pachadi recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Tasty fish</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">lovely crunchy finish too.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nAnother great recipe from [[Nik and Edwina]].\n\nThis one comes highly recommended: Nik's email telling me about this recipe was entitled \"Possibly the best thing we've ever cooked!\"\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 8 small fillets of [[Lemon]] [[Sole]] \n}}\n'''the [[Marinade|marinade]] '''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 teaspoons [[Salt|salt]] \n| 2 tablespoons red [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] \n| [[Juice|juice]] of half a [[Lemon|lemon]] \n| 1 tablespoon water \n| 1 teaspoon [[Sugar|sugar]] \n| 2.5cm chunk of [[Ginger|ginger]], finely chopped \n}}\n'''The [[Pachadi]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 tablespoons [[Coconut oil|coconut oil]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]] \n| 10 [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]] \n| 1 [[Red onion|red onion]], finely sliced \n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground|ground]] [[Turmeric|turmeric]] \n| 1 red and 1 green [[Chilli|chilli]], both slit lengthways and deseeded \n| 1 large [[Tomato|tomato]], skinned, and cut into eight chunks \n| 1 tablespoon finely chopped fresh [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] \n| 250g [[Greek yogurt]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]] \n}}\n'''the crust '''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 10 [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]] \n| 3 tablespoons dry [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] \n| 1 tablespoon yellow [[Split peas|split peas]] \n| \u00bd teaspoon [[Fennel seeds|fennel seeds]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]] \n| 1 [[Dried chilli|dried chilli]], finely chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Pat the [[Fish|fish]] fillets dry on kitchen paper. Mix together all the [[Marinade|marinade]] ingredients, and rub them all over the fillets. Set aside for 30 minutes \n| Meanwhile, make the [[Pachadi]]. Heat the [[Coconut oil|coconut oil]] in a heavy bottomed saucepan and add the [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]]. When they begin to crackle, add the [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]] and [[Onion|onion]], turn the heat down, and saut\u00e9 gently till the [[Onion|onion]] is soft and translucent, but not coloured. Add the [[Turmeric|turmeric]], [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Tomato|tomato]], and cook till the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] are just starting to soften. Leave to cool, then add the [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], [[Yoghurt|yogurt]] and [[Salt|salt]]. Stir, then set aside \n| To make the crust, put the [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]] on a [[Baking tray|baking tray]], and put into a very low [[Oven|oven]] until they go dry and crisp. Crush them lightly and set aside \n| Into a large heavy based [[Frying pan|frying pan]] on a low heat, put the [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]], yellow [[Split peas|split peas]], [[Fennel seeds|fennel seeds]] and [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]] and gently [[Roast|roast]] until they start to release their aroma. Put them into a [[Liquidiser|liquidiser]], and blitz to a quite fine powder. Allow to cool, then add the chopped dry [[Chilli|chilli]] and crushed [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]] \n| Dust the [[Fish|fish]] fillets with the [[Pea|pea]] and [[Curry leaf|curry leaf]] powder to form an even coating. You probably won\u0092t need all of the mixture, it keeps in a jar in a cupboard \n| Heat a tablespoon of [[Coconut oil|coconut oil]] in the [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and add the fillets, [[Frying|frying]] for 1 minute on either side. Place a neat heap of the [[Pachadi]] on each of four plates, carefully place 2 fillets on top of each heap, sprinkle with a little chopped [[Coriander|coriander]] and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]]\n===Recipe source===\n* https://sites.google.com/site/nikandedwinascookbook/Home/fish/curry-leaf-split-pea-and-chickpea-crusted-lemon-sole-with-tomato-and-yogurt-pachadi\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#curryleaves #pachadi #coconutoil #onion #fennelseeds #fish #corianderleaves #chickpeas #turmeric #tomato #ginger </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Curry sauce\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#currysauce #dried #tomatoes #onions #coconutmilk #fish #kidneybeans #fry #paprikapowder #garammasala #slowcooker \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=The result of 20 years curry sauce experiments, at last, Perfection!\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=5th November 2018\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Curry sauce, served with roasted butternut squash and pitta bread\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  5 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  5 hours\n|TotalCalories = 3298\n|PortionCalories = 824\n|Image = [[Image:Curry sauce recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Perfection</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I now make this in large batches and freeze it in plastic coffee cups, one cup per person. So easy!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n===Note to self===\nDon't forget there is now the industrial version - tried and tested, [[Curry Sauce 6 litres|makes 6 litres of curry sauce, ready to freeze]].\n----\nI have now made this curry sauce recipe around twenty times and I think it is now perfect. It is our 'go to' recipe for curries.  Give it a try!\n\nThe recipe below makes about 1500 grams of curry sauce which we split into three 500 gram portions and vacuum seal and freeze for later use. A 500g portion is ideal for two people once meat or fish is added.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 tablespoon of [[ghee]]\n| 2  tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| big pinch of [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| 2 medium [[Onions|onions]], peeled and sliced\n| 5 [[Cloves of garlic|cloves of garlic]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 1 can of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| 2 cans of chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[malt vinegar]] - '''no more!'''\n| 1 can of drained mixed beans or [[Kidney beans|kidney beans]]\n| 2 heaped teaspoons of Hot Madras [[Curry powder|curry powder]]\n| 1 heaped teaspoon of [[Hot chilli powder|hot chilli powder]]\n| 1 heaped teaspoon of [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 1 heaped teaspoon of [[paprika powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon of whole [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]]\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Muscovado sugar|muscovado sugar]]\n| 3 teaspoons of [[Dried|dried]] [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]] powder\n| 2 pinches of [[garam masala]]\n| &#189; teaspoon of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Indian_Curry_Sauce_3_Vac-sealed_bags.jpg|This recipe makes just about 3 x 500g [2 person] bags, ideal for freezing\nImage:Indian_Curry_Sauce_After_Cooking.jpg|Curry sauce after slow-cooking for 5 hours\nImage:Indian_Curry_Sauce_Before_Cooking.jpg|Curry sauce, ready to cook\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Mix all of the [[Dried|dried]] ingredients together so they can be added in one go\n| In a [[Wok|wok]], [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] for 5 minutes over a medium heat\n| Add the sliced [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Stir fry|stir fry]] for a minute or so\n| Stir in all of the [[Dried|dried]] ingredients and mix well\n| Immediately add the vinegar, tinned [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] and [[Kidney beans|kidney beans]]\n| Mix well and add to the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] on a low setting\n| Slow cook for 5 hours\n| Blend to a fine sauce using a [[stick blender]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n500g [[lamb neck fillet]] cut into cubes and slow cooked; low setting, for 5+ hours, makes the best lamb curry.\n\nWe served this with [[Roasted|roasted]] [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]], [[Baked|baked]] for 90 minutes at 200\u00b0 C\n===Variations===\nThis works as a [[Vegetarian|vegetarian]] [[Curry|curry]] [[Sauce|sauce]] but would work equally well with [[Meat|meat]] or [[Fish|fish]].\n\nI would be inclined to add any [[Meat|meat]] at the start of the slow-cooking process, but I would add [[Fish|fish]] or [[Prawns|prawns]] just for the final hour, to prevent over cooking.\n\n===Quantities for freezing===\nWe [[vacuum seal]] the curry sauce in packets of around 500g which are good for two people once meat or vegetables are added.  If you were making double quantities of this recipe you can make six 420g bags of curry sauce for the freezer.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#currysauce #dried #tomatoes #onions #coconutmilk #fish #kidneybeans #fry #paprikapowder #garammasala #slowcooker </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

[[curry sauce]] recipe that has been perfected over many, many years.\n\nIt's basically three times the quantity of the original recipe with a few extra ingredients.\n\nThis should make around 6 litres of curry sauce.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 3 tablespoons of [[ghee]]\n| 6  tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 teaspoon of of [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| 8 medium ingredients and mix well.\n| Immediately add the vinegar, tinned [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Coconut]] products.\n| Mix well and add to the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] on a low setting.\n| Slow cook for 5 to 7 hours, add extra water if needed.\n| Blend to a fine sauce using a [[stick blender]].\n}}\n\n===Quantities for freezing===\nWe [[vacuum seal]] the curry sauce in packets of around 500g class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nDal makhani: (Black lentils daal, Daal makkhani, dhaal makhani, dhal makhani, Maa Ki Daal) is a staple food, originally from Punjab in [[India]] made from beans and or lentils served in a creamy tomato sauce.\n\n''pulses''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 180 ml whole [[Urad|urad]] ([[Urad|dried black lentils]])\n| 2 tablespoons [[Dried|dried]] [[Kidney beans|kidney beans]]\n}}\n''spices etc''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 teaspoon whole [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 2 [[Green chillies|green chillies]], slit\n| 1 x 5 cm stick [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]]\n| 2 [[Cloves|cloves]]\n| 3 [[Green cardamoms|green cardamoms]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped\n| 1 tablespoon Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Grated|grated]] [[Ginger|ginger]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| &#188; teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 200 ml of tinned [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], mashed\n| 2 tablespoons [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e\n| 150 ml [[Single cream|single cream]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Butter|butter]]\n| 2 tablespoons chopped fresh [[Coriander|coriander]]\n| [[Salt]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rinse the [[Dried|dried]] [[Pulses|pulses]], soak overnight in cold water, refreshing a few times. Rinse well and drain.\n| Add the [[Pulses|pulses]] to a pan, cover with twice the volume of water, bring to the [[Boil|boil]], cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] vigorously until they are slightly overcooked. Skim any  scum from the surface and add extra boiling water if they start to dry out.  This will take about an hour and a quarter.\n| Drain the [[Beans|beans]] and [[Lentils|lentils]] and roughly mash into a [[dal]], cover and set to one side.\n| Heat the [[Butter|butter]] in a pan or [[Wok|wok]] and add the whole [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| Once they start to pop, add the [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]], [[Cardamom pods|cardamom pods]], [[Cloves|cloves]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Ginger|ginger]] and the [[Onions|onions]] and saut\u00e9 until the onions are translucent.\n| Stir in the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Tomato pur\u00e9e|tomato pur\u00e9e]], [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]], [[chillies]], [[turmeric]] and mashed [[Dal|dal]]. Taste for seasoning and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 15 minutes, adding extra water if needed.\n| Remove from the heat, add the [[Cream|cream]] and garnish with [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]].\n| Serve immediately.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nHaving no fresh [[coriander]] available, I used a mixture of fresh [[basil]] and [[parsley]].\n==See also==\n* [[Dal|A selection of other Daal recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Mauritian recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#dalmakhani #ginger #cuminseeds #tomatoes #dal #pulses #butter #simmer #chillipowder #garlic #dried </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

''Drappit eggs'' are  poached eggs, they are ''drapped'' into the water and in this context, herbs are any green vegetable.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 lb (450g) [[spinach]], washed\n| 1 head iceberg [[lettuce]], washed and broken into leaves\n| Salt and [[freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n| 3 [[tablespoons]] butter\n| 2 [[tablespoons]] fresh chervil, chopped\n| 8 sprigs [[parsley]], chopped\n| &#189; teaspoon ground [[white pepper]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[sea salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[nutmeg]], grated\n| &#188; teaspoon [[garam masala]]\n| 4 fl oz (112 ml) [[single cream]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[malt vinegar]]\n| 6 [[free range eggs]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place an oven proof dish in a preheated oven, 275\u00b0 F (140\u00b0 C - Gas 1 - Low)\n| For 3 minutes, in a sieve over a pan of boiling water, wilt the [[spinach]] and lettuce.  Drain and chop finely\n| In a large pan, melt the [[butter]], add the [[parsley]], [[chervil]] and the greens.  Add the [[nutmeg]] and [[garam masala]] and season with salt and pepper.\n| Pour in the [[cream]] and stir well.  Place the mixture in the preheated dish and keep warm in the oven.\n| Boil a pan of water, add the [[vinegar]] and [[poach]] the [[eggs]] until firm.\n| Make 6 ''nests'' in the greens and place an [[egg]] in each.\n| Brown under a grill for a few minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with grilled [[tomatoes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Eggs]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Eggs]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes|Eggs]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes|Eggs]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Eggs]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Eggs]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Eggs]]\n[[Category:Starters|Eggs]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Eggs]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Poached]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#nutmeg #spinach #garammasala #drappiteggswithherbs #tablespoons #parsley #butter #poached #egg #vinegar #tomatoes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It is of medium heat and is simple to make.\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n| &frac12; teaspoons [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| &frac12; teaspoons black [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]]\n| 45g [[Peanut|peanut]] ([[Groundnut|groundnut]]) [[Oil|oil]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and quartered\n| 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Pakistani basar]] or [[Garam masala|garam masala]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]] (omit if you are using [[Vegetable|vegetable]] [[Bouillon|bouillon]])\n| 2 teaspoons [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e or 1 teaspoon [[Concentrated tomato paste|concentrated tomato paste]]\n| 450g mixture of [[Frozen|frozen]] [[Vegetable|vegetables]] and fresh or tinned [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 2 small [[Potatoes|potatoes]], chopped into very small pieces\n| 300ml water or [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 170g [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]]\n| Chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place [[Cumin|cumin]] and [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]] into TM bowl and [[Dry roast|dry roast]] for '''8 minutes / 100\u00b0C / Speed 1'''. Remove and allow to cool.\n| Add the [[Oil|oil]] to the TM and heat for '''5 minutes / 100\u00b0C / Speed 1'''.\n| Add [[Onion|onion]] and chop for '''5 seconds / Speed 5'''. \n| Add all the [[Spices|spices]] and cook for '''5 minutes / 100\u00b0C / Speed 1/ MC Off'''.\n| Add the [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e or paste, the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and the water or [[Stock|stock]].\n| Cook for '''20-30 minutes / Temp. Varoma /  Speed 1 / Reverse Blade'''. \n| Empty the contents into a dish which will fit inside the '''Varoma''' bowl.\n| Add 1 litre water to the TM bowl, add the [[Strainer|strainer]] and pour the [[Rice|rice]] into it.\n| Place the '''Varoma''' bowl, containing the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] on the top.\n| '''5 seconds / Speed 5''' then  '''20 minutes / Temp. Varoma /  Speed 2&frac12;'''.\n| Turn the [[Rice|rice]] out into a bowl, mix in the [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and fluff up.\n| Serve on plates or in large bowls, with the curried [[Vegetables|vegetables]].\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nFor the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] I used 150g fresh, ripe [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and 100g each of [[Frozen|frozen]] [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]] and [[French beans]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes|Vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes|Vegetable curry]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#vegetables #tomatoes #mustardseeds #rice #tomato #corianderleaves #vegetable #onion #frozen #peppers #thermomixrecipesvegetablecurry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

We are now converted lovers of [[Basa|basa]] so I thought I would try using that instead.\n\nIf you can get [[Galangal|galangal]], do give it a try, it is one of the oddest [[Spices|spices]] that I've ever tried.  I've not yet decided on its flavour, but the perfume is similar to a very sweet [[Bubble|bubble]]-gum, though its many decades since I've tried [[Bubble|bubble]]-gum!\n\nDo try this, whatever [[Fish|fish]] or [[Spices|spices]] you decide to use!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 [[Basa fillets|basa fillets]]\n| Pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]].\n| [[Zest]] and [[Juice|juice]] of a [[Lime|lime]] or [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| &#189; whole [[coconut]], flesh removed and grated \n| 2 tablespoons [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 2.5 cm (1 \") fresh [[Galangal|galangal]] root, peeled and thinly sliced\n| 2.5 cm (1\") fresh [[Root ginger|root ginger]], peeled and [[Grated|grated]]\n| 2 [[Red chillies|red chillies]] or small [[Green Indian chillies|green indian chillies]], finely chopped, ''see Chef's notes below''.\n| 3 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 5 cm (2\") [[Lemon grass|lemon grass]] very finely chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Nam pla|nam pla]]\n| 200 ml of [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n| 1 400 ml can of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Jaggery|jaggery]] of [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| Fresh [[Coriander|coriander]] and chopped red [[Chilies|chilies]] to garnish\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Chop the [[Fish|fish]] into large bite-sized chunks and if not using [[Basa|basa]], remove any skin and [[bones]].\n| Season the [[Fish|fish]] with a good pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and half of the [[Citrus|citrus]] [[Zest|zest]] and [[Juice|juice]].\n| Using a dry [[Wok|wok]], [[Brown|brown]] the [[Coconut|coconut]] flesh, turning it regularly.\n| Add the [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]], [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Galangal|galangal]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Lemon grass|lemon grass]] and [[Fry|fry]] for a few minutes.Add the [[Nam pla|nam pla]] to the tin of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] and add the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] to the wok by straining through a fine [[Sieve|sieve]]. Reserve the [[Strained|strained]] [[Cream|cream]] to add later.\n| Add the [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]] and the [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] together with the remaining [[Citrus juice|citrus juice]] and [[Zest|zest]].\n| Taste and season with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]] if needed.\n| Bring to a gentle [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 10 minutes.\n| Add the [[Fish|fish]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for another 8 minutes.\n| Remove from the heat and stir in the sieved [[Coconut cream|coconut cream]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with plain [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]] and garnish with freshly chopped [[Coriander|coriander]]\n===Variations===\nUse any firm fleshed [[white fish]] or even [[King prawns|king prawns]].  I think that this recipe would work just as well using [[Chicken|chicken]] instead of [[Fish|fish]].\n\nI will try this with next with [[Chicken thighs|chicken thighs]] and [[Chicken drumsticks|chicken drumsticks]].\n===Chef's notes===\nI used 2 [[Indian green chillies]] and one similarly sized red [[chili]], finely chopped, seeds not removed, and the heat was perfect.\nWe would normally serve this with rice, but we had just been gifted some freshly dug new potatoes which actually went really well with this. Great for soaking up all that lovely gravy!\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Mauritian recipes]]\n[[Category:Portuguese recipes]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Dry fried]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fish #fishcurrywithcoconutandlemongrass #galangal #zest #coconutmilk #lemongrass #basa #vegetableoil #chickenstock #turmericpowder #coconut </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Folding samosas",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Folding samosas: Cooking Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#foldingsamosas #samosas #deepfry #fried #plainflour #unusualrecipes #slottedspoon #filo #meatsamosarecipe #cookingmethods #vegetablesamosarecipe \n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=OK, I know it's a cop-out doing it with paper and popping corn!\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n==How to fold samosas==\nOK, I know it's a cop-out doing it with paper and popping corn! But I figure that badly done instructions are way better than no instructions at all, so until I get the chance to make and photograph some real [[samosas]], this will have to suffice.\n<gallery widths=250px perrow=5>\nImage:Folding samosas2.jpg|Fold bottom left to the top middle, press the air out of the filling\nImage:Folding samosas3.jpg|Fold top right to top left, again press the air out of the filling\nImage:Folding samosas4.jpg|Seal the last fold with flour and water paste\nImage:Folding samosas5.jpg|Fold the final edge far left to right and squeeze to seal<br />Perfect paper samosas!\n</gallery>\n\nUse [[filo]] pastry and keep it moist by covering all the sheets with a damp tea-towel. Take each sheet out one at a time to make a samosa.\n\nMix a little [[plain flour]] with a few drops of water into a paste which you can use to seal the final fold.\n\nIf you are making these for the first time, find somewhere comfortable where you can sit down while you make them. Put some music on, relax and practice with sheets of paper first!  If, when you are doing it for real, the pastry tears, discard the pastry (or fry on its own and scoff by yourself later) and then start again, otherwise all the contents will just spill out when you deep fry the [[samosas]].\n\n[[Deep fry]] in small batches (this prevents the temperature of the oil from falling too much/too quickly) for about 3 or 4 minutes or until they are golden brown. Lift then out with a [[slotted spoon]] and drain on kitchen paper. Serve immediately or keep warm in the oven until they are all [[fried]].\n==See also==\n\n* A [[meat samosa recipe]]\n* A [[vegetable samosa recipe]]\n\n{{CategoryLineIngredients}}\n[[Category:Cooking methods]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Folding Samosas]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#foldingsamosas #samosas #deepfry #fried #plainflour #unusualrecipes #slottedspoon #filo #meatsamosarecipe #cookingmethods #vegetablesamosarecipe </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

There are many variants: most traditional mixes use just [[cinnamon]], roasted [[cumin]], [[caraway seeds]], [[cloves]], [[nutmeg]], [[mace]]) and [[green cardamom pods]] or [[black cardamom pods]]. Many commercial mixtures may include more of other less expensive spices and may contain [[dried red chili peppers]], dried [[Garlic|garlic]], [[ginger powder]], [[sesame seeds]], [[mustard seeds]], [[turmeric]], [[coriander]], [[bay leaves]], [[star anise]] and [[fennel]].\n\nIt can be added to recipes where required or added directly to the food as one would add [[salt]] and [[pepper]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| &#189; oz [[black cumin]]\n| &#189; oz [[white cumin]]\n| 3 oz [[coriander seeds]]\n| 1 &#189; oz [[cardamom seeds]] (removed from the pods)\n| 4 [[bay leaves]]\n| 2 oz [[clove buds]]\n| 2 oz [[peppercorns]]\n| &#189; oz [[nutmeg]]\n| &#189; oz ground [[mace]]\n| 1 &#189; oz [[cinnamon]] strips\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Grind ingredients in a [[coffee grinder]]\n| Mix well\n| Store in an airtight jar, preferably out of the light\n}}\n===Servings===\nServings: 25 - Makes one jar\n===Variations===\n\nAdjust to your taste\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Spices]]\n[[Category:Condiments]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garammasala #mace #bayleaves #nutmeg #cinnamon #clovebuds #sesameseeds #gingerpowder #corianderseeds #carawayseeds #cardamomseeds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Use the very [[Thin Indian green chillies|thin indian green chillies]] found at Indian stores and ethnic supermarkets.  It's not the same dish if it is made with [[Jalape\u00f1o]]-style [[chillies]].\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| [[Oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n| Good grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 2 Large [[Onions|onions]], peeled and sliced\n| 6 to 8 large Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 2.5 cm of [[Ginger root|ginger root]], unpeeled but finely chopped\n| 2-3 [[Chicken]] breasts\n| &frac12; pint [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] or [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 1 teaspoon whole [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 1 small [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]], [[Ground|ground]]\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon red [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Ginger powder|ginger powder]]\n| 8 to 10 whole [[green Indian chillies]], stalks removed and cut in half (so you get 2 short chillies from each one)\n| 1 can [[Plum tomatoes|plum tomatoes]] or 5 large [[tomatoes]], quartered\n| 1 tablespoon [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e\n| [[Salt]] to taste\n\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] or karai\n| Cut the [[Chicken|chicken]] into bite-sized pieces and [[Fry|fry]] them in small batches so they are [[Browned|browned]]. Remove and reserve\n| If necessary, add a little more [[Oil|oil]]\n| Add the the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] and a grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| As soon as the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] start to pop, add the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]], reduce the heat and gently [[Fry|fry]] until softened, about 4 minutes\n| Add all of the [[Spices|spices]] apart from the [[Green chillies|green chillies]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a few minutes\n| Add the [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] and the reserved [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 30 to 40 minutes \n| Add the canned [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]] and the [[Green chillies|green chillies]] and cook for a further 10 minutes\n| Remove the [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]], check seasoning and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Naan breads|naan breads]], [[Plain rice|plain rice]] and a [[Vegetable|vegetable]] curry.\n==See also==\n\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n* {{ChiliConCarne}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlicchillichicken #chicken #cuminseeds #onions #cinnamonstick #chickenstock #tomatoes #fry #greenchillies #blackpepper #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
