I prefer to use [[garlic olive oil]].\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[salt]]\n| 2 cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed\n| 1 clove of garlic, peeled and chopped finely\n| 2 tablespoons of [[natural yogurt]]\n| 100 ml water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Knead the [[dough]] by combining all the ingredients (apart from the '''chopped''' garlic) and sufficient water, this will be roughly &#190; cup.\n| Wrap the [[dough]] in a damp muslin cloth and leave it to rise for 2-3 hours.\n| Preheat an oven tray under your grill on it's very highest heat\n| Divide the [[dough]] into 4 small balls.\n| With a rolling pin or by slapping and stretching with your hands, roll out the balls so they are about the size of a pitta bread.\n| Unlike some breads, you don't need to let these prove, straight to the oven they go.\n| Sprinkle the chopped garlic onto both sides of the naans\n| [[Brush]] a little vegetable oil on to the hot tray, slap the naans on to the tray and grill for about 2 minutes a side, '''watching it like a hawk!'''  The difference between perfect naan breads and a brown biscuit is about 30 seconds.\n| They should have a crunch on the outside and a soft spongy inside.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Bread maker Naan breads.jpg|thumb|right|300px|Roll out to the size of a pitta bread\nImage:Breadmaker Naan breads.jpg|thumb|right|300px|Divided into four\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot, brushed with melted [[butter]].\n===Using a bread maker===\nIf you have a breadmaker, tip all of the ingredients into it apart from the '''chopped''' garlic, for the [[Panasonic SD-ZB2502 automatic breadmaker]] set it to menu option 16, basic dought, for the Panasonic SD253 breadmaker set it on a the basic dough setting (2:20) and start at step 3 above.  It could not be easier.\n===Variations===\nExperiment with various flours.  The seedy naans shown were made with Allinson ''seed and grain bread flour'' instead of plain flour, and they were wonderful. You could of course, just add a handful of mixed grain (barley flakes, kibbled rye, sunflower seeds, millet and linseed) to normal flour.\n===Chef's tip===\nUse a [[pizza stone]] if you have one for even better results.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Breadmaker recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlicnaan #dough #butter #pizzastone #brush #naturalyogurt #garlicoliveoil #driedyeast #bakingpowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Ensure the kitchen is very well ventilated or if you can, do this outside!\n| Remove from the [[Oil|oil]], allow to cool. \n| Add the [[chilli]] mixture and remaining [[Oil|oil]] to a [[Sterilised|sterilised]] 1.5 litre (1 x 1 litre and 1 x 500ml ) [[Preserving|preserving]] jar, shake well and seal.\n| It should be ready to eat in two weeks.\n}}\n===Blue garlic===\n\nIf your [[Garlic|garlic]] is quite young there may be a chemical reaction with [[lemon juice]] and [[vinegar]], which will can cause it to turn bluish-green.  This is nothing to worry about and the [[Garlic|garlic]] is perfectly safe to eat.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n[[Category:Pickled]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlic #garlicpickle #lemons #preserving #sesameoil #fenugreekseeds #lemonjuice #sterilised #chilli #pickled #fry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

They are usually pretty easy to make and ingredients list can be adjusted to suit your tastes.\n\nI find that the flavour of the [[Vinegar|vinegar]] used affects the overall flavour quite drastically and like to test small amounts of different [[Vinegars|vinegars]] (and blends of) before I make the main batch.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 225 g (8 oz) [[Jaggery|jaggery]] (or [[brown sugar]])\n| 900 ml (1.5 [[Pints|pints]]) [[Vinegar|vinegar]] (or vinegar blends of your choice)\n| 4 x 10 cm (4\") pieces of [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled\n| 3 [[Cloves|cloves]] [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 350 g (12 oz) [[Raisins|raisins]]\n| 100 g (4 oz) [[Dried|dried]] red [[Chillies|chillies]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[fenugreek]]\n| 2 tablespoons sea [[Salt|salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Make a syrup by [[Boiling|boiling]] the [[Jaggery|jaggery]]  in 600 ml (1 pint) of the [[Vinegar|vinegar]]\n| Dry roast the [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]] and [[Chillies|chillies]] then grind to a powder in a [[Coffee|coffee]] grinder with the sea [[Salt|salt]]\n| Reserve a quarter of the [[Ginger|ginger]] and a quarter of the [[Raisins|raisins]].\n| Add the remaining [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Raisins|raisins]] together with the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]] to a [[Food processor|food processor]] and blend the to a paste\n| Cut the quarter of [[Ginger|ginger]] into tiny cubes or slices\n| Mix together the syrup, [[Spice|spice]] paste, remaining [[Vinegar|vinegar]], [[Ginger|ginger]] cubes and remaining [[Raisins|raisins]]\n| Place in a large [[Preserving|preserving]] jar and leave for 1 month to mature\n}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper rice]] or [[lemon rice]].\n\nThe recipe is an excellent way to use up that glut of [[squashes]] you get every autumn, although this recipe calls for [[pumpkins]], [[butternut squash]] or similar [[squashes]] would work just as well.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 200 ml (7 lf oz) canned [[coconut milk]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[nuoc mam]], [[tuk trey]] or [[nam pla]] (all varieties of [[fish sauce]] used pla]]\n| Add the [[sugar]] to the [[coconut milk]]. If using block [[jaggery]], grate it first\n| Whisk this mixture until the [[sugar]] is dissolved\n| Heat 2 tablespoons of the [[oil]] in a [[wok]] and [[stir-fry]] the [[ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] until they start to take colour\n| Add the [[pumpkin]] cubes and [[stir-fry]] for a minute or two\n| Reduce the heat and add the [[coconut]] mixture, cover and [[simmer]] for 20 to 25 minutes\n| If too liquid for your taste then increase the heat and reduce a little\n| Season with [[black pepper]], divide into serving bowls\n| Drizzle with [[chilli oil]], garnish with [[basil leaves]] and [[fried]] [[onions]]\n| Serve immediately\n}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#coconutmilk #squashes #pumpkin #glazedpumpkinincoconutmilk #basilleaves #nampla #onions #jaggery #nuocmam #fry #butternutsquash </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

teaspoons [[Curry spice mix|curry spice mix]] (1)\n| 450 g [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and cut into chunks\n| 350 g [[Mixed vegetables|mixed vegetables]] of your choice, washed and prepared\n| 4 teaspoons [[Curry spice mix|curry spice mix]] (2)\n| 1 tin chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 500 ml or more of hot [[Vegetable stock|vegetable stock]] or water\n| [[Coriander leaves]], chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large pan to a high temperature.\n| Add the [[Curry spice mix|curry spice mix]] (1).\n| [[Fry]] for a few seconds until the [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]] start to pop.\n| Add the [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Vegetables|vegetables]], [[Curry spice mix|curry spice mix]] (2) and [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]].\n| Cook for 5 minutes, stirring continuously.\n| Add the hot [[Stock|stock]] or water, bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce heat and allow to [[Simmer|simmer]] for 20 minutes.  Add more water or stock if necessary.\n| Serve, garnished with the [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Pulao rice]], but leave out the [[Saffron|saffron]], [[Almonds|almonds]], [[Sultanas|sultanas]] and [[Onions|onions]].\n===Variations===\nAdd a sliced [[Onion|onion]] and Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]] if you wish (in which case, fry them before you add the other ingredients).  However many Indians do not eat [[Onions|onions]] for religious reasons, hence the use of [[Asafoetida|asafoetida]] as a substitute.\n===Chef's notes===\nChoose a good mix of [[Vegetable|vegetable]] types, such as [[Carrots|carrots]], [[Peas|peas]], [[Beans|beans]], [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]] and [[Aubergines|aubergines]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Gujarati vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Gujarati vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Gujarati vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes|Gujarati vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Gujarati vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Gujarati vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Gujarati vegetable curry]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#gujarativegetablecurry #curryspicemix #tomatoes #onions #potatoes #corianderleaves #almonds #vegetables #peas #stock #pulaorice </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

to make, especially as we always have [[Curry sauce|curry sauce]] in the [[Freezer|freezer]].\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 portion of home made [[Curry sauce|curry sauce]]\n| 250 g packet of [[Halloumi title": "Idli",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Idli, a fermented steamed rice cake recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#idli #rice #daal #urad #steamer #fenugreekseeds #india #dips #steamedrice #steamed #boil \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is a basic recipe for idli which are fermented steamed rice cakes popularly served for breakfast in Southern India and Sri Lanka\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 219\n|PortionCalories = 18\n|DatePublished=18th February 2015\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 12 - Makes 12\n|ImageComment = \n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  18 hours, 10 minutes (including soaking and fermenting time)\n|PrepTime =  18 hours (including soaking and fermenting time)\n|CookTime =  10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Idli with Sambar Chutney Chennai Banana Leaf Syndal.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Can't find Idli rice</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I've even tried Aldi for Ildi!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nThis is a basic recipe for idli which are fermented [[Steamed rice|steamed rice]]  [[Cakes|cakes]] popularly served for [[Breakfast|breakfast]] in [[Southern]] [[India]] and Sri Lanka\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n| 90g idli [[Rice|rice]]\n| 30g [[Urad|urad]] dall (the hulled, white variety)\n| \u00bd teaspoons [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]]\n| [[Salt]] to taste\n}}\n==='''Mise en place'''===\n\n* Rinse and soak the idli [[Rice|rice]] overnight\n* In a separate bowl rinse and soak the [[Urad|urad]] [[Daal|daal]] together with the [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]] overnight\n* Do not over-rinse or wash otherwise you will inhibit fermentation. Also use chlorine-free or bottled water if possible\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Drain the [[Rice|rice]] and the [[Daal|daal]] continuing to keep them separate\n| Grind the [[Daal|dal]] mixture until you have a thick but very smooth paste, adding a little cold water from time to time\n| Remove and set aside\n| Repeat the process with the [[Rice|rice]], adding water as necessary\n| Add the [[Daal|daal]] mixture to the [[Rice|rice]] and continue to grind until well mixed\n| Stir in the [[Salt|salt]]\n| Pour the mixture into a container and leave to [[Ferment|ferment]] overnight\n| Stir and check that it has the right consistency\n| Grease the idli moulds and fill a [[Steamer|steamer]] base with water\n| Bring the water to the [[Boil|boil]] and divide the mixture between the moulds\n| Place in the [[Steamer|steamer]] and cook for 8-12 minutes\n| Use a [[Cocktail stick|cocktail stick]] to test for doneness - it should come out clean if the idlis are cooked\n| Remove the idlis from the  moulds - they should be light and fluffy\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with sambar, [[Chutneys|chutneys]] or [[Dips|dips]]\n\n==See also==\n*Idli steamer\n*[[Idli rice]]\n*Wet grinder\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#idli #rice #daal #urad #steamer #fenugreekseeds #india #dips #steamedrice #steamed #boil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Indian pickles",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Indian pickles: Cooking Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#indianpickles #vegetables #pickled #fruits #limepickle #palmhearts #onionrelish #marinated #lemonjuice #prawnbalchao #garlicpickle \n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=Indian pickles are a variety of spicy pickled side dishes or condiments popular in the Indian Subcontinent, in Southeast Asia, and in many\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n[[Image:Indian pickles.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Indian pickles]]\n'''Indian pickles''' are a variety of spicy [[pickled]] side dishes or [[condiments]] popular in the Indian Subcontinent, in Southeast Asia, and in many other areas among ethnically South Asian communities. The pickle serves as a flavour enhancer and is eaten typically in small pieces with the rest of the meal. There are a wide variety of different pickles. Each is usually made with a mixture of [[fruits]] or [[vegetables]], chopped and [[marinated]] in a liquid (often [[oil]] or [[lemon juice]]) and a variety of [[spices]] (often including lots of [[chili pepper]]) and [[salt]]. Pickling in India is an ancient art of [[food preservation]]. Indian pickles are quite different from the European variety in that the pickling is usually done in [[oil]] rather than using [[vinegar]].\n\nAll sorts of [[fruits]] and [[vegetables]] in south Asia are [[pickled]] in this manner, including [[pumpkins]], [[palm hearts]], [[lotus stems]], [[mango slices]], [[limes]] and rose petals, as well as [[vegetables]] more conventionally pickled in the West.\n===Indian pickle and chutney recipes on Cookipedia===\n* [[Bird's eye chilli paste]]\n* [[Chili vinegar recipe|Chili vinegar]]\n* [[Coconut chutney]]\n* [[Garlic pickle]]\n* [[Ginger chutney]]\n* [[Lemon pickle]]\n* [[Lemon pickle (with anise)]]\n* [[Lime pickle]]\n* [[Mango chutney]]\n* [[Mango and pear chutney (TM)]]\n* [[Mango relish]]\n* [[Mango pickle]]\n* [[Mixed pickle]]\n* [[Onion relish]]\n* [[Prawn Balchao]]\n* [[Spicy hot chutney]]\n* [[Tomato chutney]]\n==See also==\n* [[Chili pepper sauce|Our selection of chilli sauce recipes]]\n{{CategoryLineIngredients}}\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Prepared foods]]\n[[Category:Store cupboard items]]\n[[Category:Vegetables]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Pickled]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#indianpickles #vegetables #pickled #fruits #limepickle #palmhearts #onionrelish #marinated #lemonjuice #prawnbalchao #garlicpickle </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Makes about 4 to 6 kheema naan\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 3 hours 10 minutes\n|PrepTime = 3 hours\n|CookTime = 10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Kheema tandoori naan recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A meaty naan</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Nice to be able to add your own meat to a keema, sometimes they can be a bit stingy.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]])</span></span>\n}}\nKeemah naan, Keema nan or keema naan is an interesting meaty variation on the standard [[naan bread]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 350 g (12 oz) plain [[Flour|flour]] or wholewheat flour\n| 1 teaspoons [[Dried|dried]] active [[Yeast|yeast]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[baking powder]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[natural yogurt]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[vegetable oil]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Sugar|sugar]], [[Honey|honey]] or  or [[Jaggery|jaggery]]\n| 1 teaspoon sea [[Salt|salt]]\n| 100 g (4 oz) spiced [[Minced|minced]] [[Beef|beef]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the [[Yeast|yeast]] with 2 teaspoons of warm water and the [[Sugar|sugar]], stir well and leave in a [[warm place]] for 10 minutes until it starts to froth\n| Add the [[Flour|flour]] to a large bowl or [[Food processor|food processor]], tip in the [[Yeast|yeast]] mixture\n| Knead for about 15 minutes, adding enough water to make a firm [[dough]]\n| Cover with a damp [[Tea|tea]]-towel, leave in a [[warm place]] until it rises, this may take up to 3 hours, depending upon temperature\n| Add the [[mince]] and the [[Salt|salt]] and [[Kneading bread|knead]] in well\n| Divide into 6 pieces and with floured hands, roll and pat until they are a little larger than saucers\n| Cook under a hot [[Grill|grill]] for about 2 minutes a side, turning once.  Watch it like a hawk as the difference between perfect naan breads and brown biscuits is about 30 seconds!\n| These can also be cooked on a hot [[Barbecue|barbecue]], or of course in a tandoor if you are lucky enough\n}}\n===Using a breadmaker===\n\nIf you have a breadmaker, tip all of the ingredients into it, set in to the long (2.5 hour) [[dough]] program continue from step 6 above.\n\n===Chef's tip===\n\nUse a [[pizza stone]] if you have one for even better results.{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#yeast #kheematandoorinaan #dough #warmplace #flour #jaggery #barbecue #bakingpowder #pizzastone #kneadingbread #dried </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Stir well to mix\n| Add the water and [[Salt|salt]] and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| Reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] with the lid ajar\n| Lower the heat, partially cover the pot and cook until the [[Rice|rice]] and [[Lentils|lentils]] are cooked - about 35 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[Yogurt|yogurt]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #lentils #cuminseeds #turmericpowder #khichdirecipe #lentil #mild #whitebasmatirice #khichdi #boil #fry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "King prawn and coconut roti with tomatoes, chillies and ginger",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=King prawn and coconut roti with tomatoes, chillies and ginger recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#kingprawnandcoconutrotiwithtomatoeschilliesandginger #rice #kingprawns #ginger #onions #coconut #grill #ghee #limejuice #tomatoes #chillies \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is another variation on Changri Mali Roti - absolutely my most favourite recipe of all time\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2449\n|PortionCalories = 612\n|DatePublished=29th December 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment =\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 55 minutes\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:King prawn and coconut roti with tomatoes, chillies and ginger.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I love this so much</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">And it's a meal I've never seen in a restaurant! \ud83d\ude1f</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is another variation of my favourite recipe of all time, [[Chingri malai roti]], a crunchy hot and spicy rice cake that is a one pan main meal.\n\nThis time I've used a few fresh [[tomatoes]] chopped up and added with the raw [[king prawns]] before the roti is crisped under the grill.\n\nPlease be very careful if storing cooked [[Rice|rice]].  [[Refrigerate]] the moment it has cooled and use within 1 day\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 200 g (8 oz) uncooked [[basmati rice]].\n| 12 large raw [[king prawns]], deveined and each chopped into 3 pieces\n| 2 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]] or vegetable [[Oil|oil]]\n| 5 [[Fat|fat]] [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 5 cm (2\") [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and roughly [[Grated|grated]] - try making some [[Frozen ginger paste]], it is a good as fresh and lasts for years.\n| 75 g (5 oz) [[Onions|onions]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 whole [[Coconut|coconut]], flesh removed and roughly grated - see [[Action coconut scraper with vacuum suction base]] for the easy way to do this.\n| 4 hot [[Chilli peppers|chilli peppers]] (red or green), finely chopped - de-seeded if desired\n| 2 large tomatoes chopped into small pieces\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n}}\n'''spices'''\n\n''don't grind the spices, leave them whole''\n* 2 teaspoons whole [[coriander seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon whole [[cumin seeds]] (white)\n* 1/2 a teaspoon of whole [[fenugreek seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:King prawn and coconut roti with tomatoes, chillies and ginger breakfast.jpg|Ready to serve with some left over for my breakfast!\nImage:King prawn and coconut roti with tomatoes, chillies and ginger browned.jpg|Browned under the grill\nImage:King prawn and coconut roti with tomatoes, chillies and ginger prawns.jpg|Prawns added, ready to grill\nImage:King prawn and coconut roti with tomatoes.jpg|Tomatoes mixed in; the rice cake is ready to [[pan-fry]]\n</gallery>\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Quickly wash and drain the [[rice]] but don't rinse it as you normally would, this dish is best with rice of a starchy consistency. \n| Cook in boiling water for 7 to 11 minutes.\n| Rinse the cooked rice in cold water until it is cold.  Drain well.\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] and [[Coconut|coconut]] to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade and blend to a thick creamy consistency - adding a little milk if required to make it thinner.  Remember, the inside is not going to change much whilst being cooked and will remain at roughly the same consistency as it was when first mixed. \n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a [[frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] all of the [[Spices|spices]] for half a minute, then add the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and allow them to cook for a minute or so.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and reduce the heat a little and let them cook until translucent; about 5 minutes.\n| Add the [[Chilli|chilli]] to the [[Onions|onions]], mix well and immediately remove from the heat.\n| Preheat the [[Grill|grill]].\n| Lightly [[Oil|oil]] a large non-stick oven proof [[Frying pan|frying pan]] put on a medium heat.\n| Add the rice mixture to the hot pan and ensure the mixture is evenly distributed and patted down.  Distribute the chopped tomatoes evenly throughout the rice and coconut mixture.\n| Cook for about 10 minutes or until the [[Rice|rice]] cake starts to catch on the bottom, then mix it up well so you get lots of crispy bits.\n| Mix in the raw [[king prawns]] and pat down.\n| [[Brown|brown]] under the hot [[Grill|grill]] for about 5 minutes just to colour the top surface a little.\n| Sprinkle with [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and serve immediately.\n}}\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nThis is a perfect meal on its own though it can benefit from a few tablespoons of [[yogurt]] as a side dish if the [[chillies]] are really hot.  [[Peas]] and [[sweetcorn]] make a nice colourful accompaniment to this spicy recipe too.\n===A better way of cooking this===\nAfter making variants of this for many years, I've discovered the best method of cooking is to spread the ingredients out on a lightly greased [[baking tray]] and bake at 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7) for 35 minutes, stirring up the contents every 10 minutes.  It might be an idea with a meat other than crayfish, to add the meat (or prawns) for the last 10 minutes so they don't dry out.\n[[Image:Crayfish & coconut chili, 1.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Baking tray method shown here with [[Crayfish and coconut rice cake with hot chillies]]]]\n\n===Variations===\nAdd a splash of [[nam pla]] to the chopped prawns and let them [[marinade]] for a few hours for a more fishy taste.\n{{Template:SeeAlso Roti}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#kingprawnandcoconutrotiwithtomatoeschilliesandginger #rice #kingprawns #ginger #onions #coconut #grill #ghee #limejuice #tomatoes #chillies </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=King prawn patia, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#kingprawnpatia #onions #tamarindpulp #kingprawns #jaggery #naanbreads #garlic #foodprocessor #cumin #chillies #prawns \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is an exotic Parsee dish that would be served at weddings and similar occasions requiring luxurious food. You may have to search hard for one of\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3192\n|PortionCalories = 532\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 2\n|ImageComment = Awaiting the [[naan breads]]\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 1 hour\n|Image = [[Image:King prawn patia recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">The real thing!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is better than the take-away round the corner!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is an exotic Parsee dish that would be served at weddings and similar occasions requiring luxurious food.\n\nYou may have to search hard for one of the ingredients, tamarind, as it's not often found in supermarkets.  You should not have any trouble finding it a Indian or Chinese wholesalers such as [http://www.seewoo.com Seewoo]\n\nDon't be startled by the quantities of garlic, chillies or onions in this dish.  It's not overpowering and a little goes a long long way.  Be bold and try this recipe, it will become a favourite.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 large fresh [[red chillies]], deseeded\n| 2 large fresh green [[chillies]], deseeded\n| 2 dried [[chile de Arbole]]\n| 1 whole [[Garlic|garlic]] bulb, smashed and peeled\n| 1 teaspoon [[cumin]] seeds\n| 112 ml (4 fl oz) [[vegetable oil]] - whilst not authentic, I prefer [[olive oil]] for health reasons.\n| 1.3 kg (3 lb) [[onions]], peeled and finely chopped (a job for the [[food processor]]!)\n| 1 teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[ground coriander]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[cayenne powder]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[jaggery]] or [[sugar]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[sea salt]]\n| 6 tablespoons [[tamarind pulp]]\n| 1.3 kg (3 lb) [[king prawns]], shelled, de-veined and cleaned\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:King prawn patia at rest.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Resting for 40 minutes\nImage:King prawn patia ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|King prawn patia<br />The ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a [[food processor]] or [[mortar and pestle]], grind the [[chillies]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[cumin]] and one of the [[onions]] to a paste, gradually adding half a cup of water. Set to one side.\n| Heat the oil on a large pan and fry the [[onions]] to a golden colour, carefully add the spice paste and fry until it bubbles.  Add the [[turmeric]], [[coriander]] and [[cayenne]] powders and fry for a few more minutes\n| Stir in the [[tamarind pulp]], [[jaggery]] and 4 fl oz of water and cook for a further 10 minutes, stirring now and again until the sauce has thickened\n| Add the [[prawns]] and cook for 2 minutes\n| Remove from the heat and leave standing for 40 minutes so the [[prawns]] absorb the all of the flavours\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nReheat just before serving\n\nServe with plain [[boiled rice]], [[broccoli]] and [[naan breads]]\n===Chef's notes===\n\nI recently made this recipe for 4 (2 now, freeze 2) but still felt that 1.3 kg of [[king prawns]] was a bit excessive!  So I made the recipe using the same amounts as above, but with 400 g of [[king prawns]], 180 g of [[crayfish tails]] and to bulk it out a little, a winter squash, peeled, sliced and boiled until soft, a little less time than for potatoes of the same size.  I then added the squash with the prawns.\n\n'''Tamarind pulp:''' If the [[tamarind pulp]] comes with stones, then soak it in the 4 fl oz of (boiling) water for 15 minutes, stir well and sieve the stones and any skins out and then use the liquid as stock.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Prawn]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Prawn]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Prawn]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes|Prawn]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Prawn]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes|Prawn]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Prawn]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Prawn]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#kingprawnpatia #onions #tamarindpulp #kingprawns #jaggery #naanbreads #garlic #foodprocessor #cumin #chillies #prawns </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Lambadi lamb curry",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Lambadi lamb curry crockpot, Indian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#marinade #lamb #lambadilambcurry #ghee #chiledearbole #garlicpaste #onions #ginger #gingerpaste #curry #anchochilipowder \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=An interesting slow-cooked (crockpot) lamb curry originating from Rajastan, North-west India\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4041\n|PortionCalories = 1010\n|DatePublished=6th April 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  4 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  2 hours, 30 minutes\n|CookTime =  1 hour, 45 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Lambadi lamb curry recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Smokey curry!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I'm not a massive fan of lamb but this was nice and had a real smoked taste.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nAn interesting [[Lamb|lamb]] [[Curry|curry]] originating from Rajasthan, North-west [[India]].\n[[Image:Lambadi lamb curry_marinade.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Marinade in the Lock and Lock box - showing the [[chile de arbole]] so you can get an idea of the size.  They are pretty hot chillies]]\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1kg (2 1/4lb) [[Lamb|lamb]] shoulder, trimmed and cubed\n| 50g (1.8 ounces) [[Ghee|ghee]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced\n| [[Freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Ginger paste|ginger paste]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Garlic paste|garlic paste]]\n| 2 [[Black cardamom pods|black cardamom pods]], whole, cracked under a knife\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] - I used [[Ancho chili powder]] for a smokey edge.\n| 568 ml (1 [[Pints|pint]]) [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n}}\n'''[[Lamb|lamb]] [[Marinade|marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 400 ml (14 fl oz) [[Natural yogurt|natural yogurt]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 5 cm (2\") piece of [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and [[Julienned|julienned]]\n| 1 bulb of [[Garlic, peeled and crushed|garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 5g (1/8 oz) (''about 8'') dried [[chile de arbole]], left whole\n| &#188; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n}}\n'''[[Marinade|marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| To a lidded [[Lock and Lock box]], add the [[Yogurt|yogurt]] and all the [[Marinade|marinade]] ingredients.\n| Ensure everything is evenly mixed.\n| Add the [[Meat|meat]]. Close the lid and shake well. [[Refrigerate]] and leave to [[Marinade|marinade]] for at least 2 hours, more if you have time. Shaking now and then ensures a constant [[Marinade|marinade]].\n}}\n'''[[Lamb|lamb]] [[Curry|curry]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Chilli|chilli]] paste and the [[Ginger paste|ginger paste]] to a bowl or cup and mix with 4 tablespoons of water.\n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a [[Wok|wok]] or large [[Frying pan|frying pan]], add a good grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]. Once the [[Pepper|pepper]] starts to fizz, stir in the [[Onions|onions]], reduce the heat a little so the [[Ghee|ghee]] does not burn and [[Stir fry|stir fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] for 10 minutes until nicely coloured.\n| Add the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic paste|garlic paste]] mix and the [[Chilli|chilli]] power and mix well.\n| Add the [[Cardamom pods|cardamom pods]], and the cubed [[Lamb|lamb]] with its [[Marinade|marinade]] and [[Stir fry|stir fry]] for 5 minutes.\n| Top up with 800 ml (1.25 [[Pints|pints]]) of [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]].\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 1 hour 30 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]] and [[Naan breads|naan breads]].\n===Chef's notes===\nI've changed the recipe quite a lot from the original.  Originally it stated 10 g of dried chillies, crushed, in the marinade.   That equates to about 45 birds' eye chillies.  Too hot for me and I also have guests to consider.  For the chilli marinade, I've used 10g (16 x dried [[chili de arbole]], left whole.  I've also used [[Ancho chili powder]], which has a smokey hint.  None of which is the least bit authentic, but should make an interesting curry.\n\nThe resulting curry was reasonably hot, (about Madras strength).  If you want it hotter, I would suggest cutting the dried chillies in half.  That will allow more of the heat and flavour to mingle with the sauce.  If unsure, taste the sauce during cooking and if it starts to get too hot, remove some, or all of the chilles.\n\nAfter the frying stage, I  decided to use the [[slow cooker]] for the remaining cooking. As there was plenty of sauce, 2.5 hours on high made the lamb nice and tender, without overcooking. \n\nIf you want a more substantial sauce, stir in a few tablespoons of [[cornmeal]] 30 minutes before the ned of the cooking time.\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Adapted from 'Gypsy [[Meat|meat]]' (''Maas banjara'') from Mr Pushpash Pent's wonderful \"India\": ISBN 978-0714859026.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#marinade #lamb #lambadilambcurry #ghee #chiledearbole #garlicpaste #onions #ginger #gingerpaste #curry #anchochilipowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Lamb biriani",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Lamb biriani, | Indian recipes from the cook's Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#lambbiriani #onions #ghee #lamb #rice #coriander #raisins #almonds #ginger #sultanas #yogurt \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A delicious lamb biriani that is definately worth the extra effort. Better than any restaurant version\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4145\n|PortionCalories = 690\n|DatePublished=3rd December 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 13 hours 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 12 hours 45 minutes\n |CookTime = 40 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Lamb biriani and brocolli.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Home made curry powder</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Works well, just makes sure all of your spices are fresh.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Biryani''', '''biriani''', or '''beriani''' is a set of primarily South Asian [[Rice|rice]]-based foods made with [[Spices|spices]], rice (usually [[Basmati|basmati]]) and [[Meat|meat]]/[[Vegetables|vegetables]]. It was spread throughout the Middle East and South Asia (and Southeast Asia to an extent) by Muslim travellers and merchants, and is popular in Pakistan, India, Bangladesh, Iraq, Iran, Afghanistan and Sri Lanka.\n\nThe name is derived from the Persian word bery\u0101(n) which means \"[[Fried|fried]]\" or \"[[Roasted|roasted]]\".\n\nThis recipe comes from a hand-typed sheet, covered in curry stains, that has been with me since my first Indian cookery course.  \n\nIt's a bit of an involved recipe but well worth the effort. It is best to [[Marinate|marinate]] the [[Meat|meat]] overnight so prepare this the day before.\n\nI tend to use a large pot of yogurt as I prefer more sauce.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 900 g (2 lb) [[Lamb]] fillet, cubed\n| 125 ml [[Yogurt|yogurt]]\n| 2 cups [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]], rinsed in cold running water\n| 2.5 cm (1\") peeled [[Ginger|ginger]]\n| 4 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chili powder|chili powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Garam masala|garam masala]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| &frac12; cup [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and stalks, chopped\n| 2 large [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] or &frac12; small tin of tomatoes, chopped\n| Big pinch of [[Saffron strands|saffron strands]]\n| 2 large [[Onions|onions]], peeled and chopped\n| 3 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]] or [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 20 g sliced [[Almonds|almonds]]\n| 20 g [[Sultanas|sultanas]] or [[Raisins|raisins]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] to taste\n}}\n'''Leave whole and remove before serving or pick out while eating:'''\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2.5 cm [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]]\n| 6 [[Clove|clove]] buds\n| 6 whole [[Cardamom pods|cardamom pods]] ([[Brown|brown]] or white)\n| 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* In a [[Food processor|food processor]], grind the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] to a paste.  Grind the whole [[Spices|spices]] in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]].  Mix well into the [[Yogurt|yogurt]] and use to [[Marinate|marinate]] the [[Lamb|lamb]], preferably overnight.\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4)\n\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Lamb biriani from oven.jpg|Just out of the oven\nImage:Biriani with tomatoes.jpg|Stirring in the tomatoes-frozen from last summer\nImage:Toasted almonds onions and sultanas.jpg|Preparing the topping\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] in half of the [[Oil|oil]], until golden, remove half of the onions with a slotted spoon and reserve.\n| [[Brown]] the remainder of the [[Onions|onions]], stir in the meat together with the marinade and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for 5 minutes. Add the chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and cook on a low heat until the [[Meat|meat]] is cooked and tender. Add more liquid if needed, but by the time the meat is cooked, some of the liquid should have cooked off.\n| Add half of the chopped [[Coriander|coriander]] or [[Parsley|parsley]], season with [[Salt|salt]] and set aside.\n| In a large pan of [[Boiling|boiling]] water, cook the washed [[Rice|rice]] for 10 minutes only.  Drain and reserve. The final cooking will be done in the [[Oven|oven]].\n| Grease the base of a large [[Oven|oven]]-proof [[Casserole|casserole]] with a little [[Ghee|ghee]].\n| Using the cooked [[Rice|rice]], [[Lamb|lamb]], [[Coriander|coriander]], cooked [[Onions|onions]], [[Saffron|saffron]] and dabs of [[Ghee|ghee]], fill the [[Casserole|casserole]] in layers. \n| Top with [[Raisins|raisins]] or [[Sultanas|sultanas]] and sliced [[Almonds|almonds]], add a few dabs of [[Ghee|ghee]] and cover with [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]]\n| Cook for 17 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Chana daal|lentil curry]] or [[Salad|salad]] of your choice\n===Chef's notes===\nUse [[Parsley|parsley]] if you cannot get [[Coriander|coriander]]\n==See also==\n* [[Chicken biriani]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Mauritian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lambbiriani #onions #ghee #lamb #rice #coriander #raisins #almonds #ginger #sultanas #yogurt </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

teaspoon white [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Black cumin seeds|black cumin seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[coriander seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chili powder|chili powder]]\n| 3 [[Cloves garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 level teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Garam masala|garam masala]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and stalks, chopped\n| 2 tablespoons [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| [[Grated]] [[Zest|zest]] of &frac12; a [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]]\n| 1 green [[Chili pepper|chili pepper]], deseeded and sliced into thin rings\n| 3 [[Red chillies|red chillies]], deseeded and sliced into rings\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Grind all of the whole [[Spices|spices]] in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]].\n* Mix all of the ingredients into the [[Yogurt|yogurt]] to make a [[marinade]].\n* [[Marinate]] the [[Lamb|lamb]] strips for at least 4 hours, overnight if you have planned well enough in advance!\n* Preheat the grill.\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Lamb tikka grilled.jpg|thumb|right|300px|Lamb tikka, grilled\nImage:Lamb tikka marinade.jpg|thumb|right|300px|Lamb tikka marinaded, ready to cook\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Line a grill tray with [[silver foil]] and place the lamb strips together with a little of the [[marinade]] on the grill tray (see picture)\n| Grill for about 7 minutes\n| Turn the slices over and grill for another 7 minutes.  Check regularly and test to see if they are done to your liking.  Don't be over-worried about the [[marinade]] burning, it gives it great flavour and does not taste the least bit burnt.  Do worry about the lamb drying out, see Chef's Notes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Naan breads|naan breads]], [[Pillau rice|pillau rice]] and a [[Green salad|green salad]].\n\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you don't have [[Black cumin|black cumin]], just use [[White cumin|white cumin]] instead.\n\nAdjust the [[Chili|chili]] levels to suit your tastes, this can be fairly hot with these quantities, depending upon the types of chili you use.\n\nWhen I originally made this dish, I had planned to make [[Balti lamb tikka]], but changed my mind half-way through.  I would not have sliced the lamb so thinly if I had known I was to grill it. Delicious even so!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lambtikka #marinade #lamb #garlicmayonnaise #seeds #chili #mortarandpestle #whitecumin #redchillies #miseenplace #spices </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Leelu's Keralan Chicken Curry",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Leelu's Keralan Chicken Curry an Indian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#coconutmilk #garlic #leeluskeralanchickencurry #chillies #chillipowder #onions #keralanmasala #chapatis #turmeric #corianderpowder #chicken \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=To quote Nik or Edwina:\"On our trip to Kerala in India in the summer of 2009, we spent a few hours at Leelu\u0092s Homestay house\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1821\n|PortionCalories = 455\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 45 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Leelu's Keralan Chicken Curry recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nick & Edwina at their best!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Some of the most authentic curries I've ever made are by those two.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nTo quote Nik or Edwina:\n\n''\"On our trip to Kerala in India in the summer of 2009, we spent a few hours at Leelu's Homestay house (see Links), watching her making several different curries and taking copious notes. Then we sat down and ate a lovely lunch of this one, served with [[Chapatis]], [[Pachadi]], [[Pumpkin Curry]] and Potato Thoran. This is delicious, a succulent, flavoursome dish, with a perfect balance between sweet and sour. We've made it with beef too, and it was equally gorgeous.\n\nGenerally Keralans use a much lighter version of the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] we buy in tins in the UK. We've found that if you buy the reduced [[Fat|fat]] [[Coconut|coconut]] [[Milk|milk]], open the can without shaking it, pour off the liquid part and use that, it works well. Then you can dilute the remaining thicker half with a little water and [[Freeze|freeze]] it for next time. We've also recently found Maggi powdered coconut to be excellent for making this curry, though the packet instructions are a little heavy handed; we found 35 g of powder to 300 mls of water to be perfect\"''\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 teaspoons [[Keralan masala]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 4 teaspoon [[Coriander powder|coriander powder]] \n| 1kg [[Chicken|chicken]], skinned and chopped into rough chunks, [[Parson's nose|parson's nose removed]]\n| 2 [[Onions|onions]], peeled and chopped\n| &#189; thumb of [[Fresh ginger|fresh ginger]], chopped\n| 8 to 10 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], chopped\n| 1 to 2 fresh [[Chillies|chillies]], chopped\n| 1 big [[Tomato|tomato]], sliced\n| 1 big [[Potato|potato]], in 5cm [[Dice|dice]] and par boiled for 15 minutes.\n| 200ml [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] (see above)\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Keralan Curry covered with water.jpg|Just covered with water\nImage:Keralan Curry recipe.jpg|Spices, [[onions]] & [[Garlic|garlic]]\nImage:Keralan masala recipe.jpg|Kerelan masala\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| To the 2 teaspoons of [[Keralan masala|keralan masala]], add the [[Turmeric|turmeric]], the [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] and the [[Coriander powder|coriander powder]]. Add a splash of water and mix to a smooth paste\n| Heat 4 tablespoons of [[Coconut oil|coconut oil]], add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Ginger|ginger]], fresh [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and cook till soft\n| Add the masala paste, turn heat down, and cook slowly till it smells wonderful\n| Add everything else except the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] and the [[tomatoes]], add 125 ml of vegetable stock or water, cover with a snug fitting lid, bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] gently minutes until [[Chicken|chicken]] and [[potatoes]] are cooked - about 30 minutes. \n| Add the tomatoes and [[coconut milk]] and continue to simmer for 5 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nAdd 2 tablespoons of [[Keralan Curry Garnish]] , and serve with [[plain boiled rice]] and/or [[Chapatis]]\n===Chef's notes===\nI used Blue Dragon light coconut milk which was fine for this dish.  (The remains of the tin can be frozen for later use).\n\nI found this fairly bland and would definitely add more chillies next time.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#coconutmilk #garlic #leeluskeralanchickencurry #chillies #chillipowder #onions #keralanmasala #chapatis #turmeric #corianderpowder #chicken </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Lemon pickle (Summer recipe)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Lemon pickle, summer version, an Indian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#lemons #asafoetida #pickle #help #fenugreek #turmericpowder #spices #lemonpickle #wheatflour #driedgarlicgranules #mustardseed \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Lemon pickle is a traditional condiment used with Indian food\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 302\n|PortionCalories = 302\n|DatePublished=24th December 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Lemon pickle (Summer recipe)\n |Servings = 1\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 20 minutes plus 60 days fermentation\n |PrepTime = 60 days, 20 minutes\n |CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Lemon pickle (Summer recipe) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Worked well and was nice</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">But I've no idea what I'll do with 2 pints of the stuff!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Lemon pickle]] is a traditional condiment used with Indian food. Many [[Pickle|pickle]] recipes from India have [[Oil|oil]] to help [[Preserve|preserve]] the pickle, but this recipe uses no oil.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 10 unwaxed [[Lemons|lemons]], (thin skins preferred)\n| [[Juice|juice]] of 1 [[Lemons|lemons]]\n| &frac12; cup of [[Salt|salt]]\n| &frac14; cup of [[Red chili powder|red chili powder]]\n| &frac12; cup of [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 3 teaspoons [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]] [[Seed|seed]]\n| 1 teaspoon black [[Mustard seed|mustard seed]]\n| &frac14; of a teaspoon of [[Asafoetida|asafoetida]] powder\n}}\n===Method===\n\n\n'''Preparation'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Wash the [[Lemons|lemons]] in very hot water and dry them well, leaving no water on the lemons. Trim off the stalk and any odd bits.\n| Halve them and remove any pips\n| Cut the [[Lemons|lemons]] in to small pieces about 2 cm / &frac34; inch on each side, and place in a bowl.\n| [[Dry-roast]] the [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]], black [[Mustard|mustard]] and [[Asafoetida|asafoetida]] together in a pan on a medium heat for about 5 minutes. Don't burn them!\n| Grind the [[Roasted|roasted]] [[Spices|spices]] in a grinder, or a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]].\n| Add the [[Ground|ground]] [[Spices|spices]], [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Chili powder|chili powder]] to the bowl and mix together well.\n| Pack the mixture into a 2 litre (2 quart) jar, or use a couple of smaller jars. Don't fill quite to the top - allow at least 1 cm space.\n}}\n'''[[Fermentation]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Sit the jar where it will get the heat of the sun. Bring the jar inside in the evening, and put it back out in the morning. Do this for at least a month in summer, two months in winter. The warmth of the sun will [[Help|help]] the [[Pickle|pickle]] to [[Ferment|ferment]].\n}}\n===Serves===\nServings: 33 - Make 1 litre of lemon pickle, almost 2 pints\n===Chef's notes===\nUse 1/2 a teaspoon of powdered [[Dried garlic granules|dried garlic granules]] or [[Dried garlic|dried garlic]] if you cannot get [[Asafoetida|asafoetida]] powder.\n\n[[Asafoetida]] powder generally has [[Wheat flour|wheat flour]] added to it, to [[Help|help]] it flow well. You can omit this ingredient if you want to make it [[Gluten|gluten]]-free.\n==See also==\n* [[Lime pickle (Winter recipe)]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n[[Category:Pickled]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lemons #asafoetida #pickle #help #fenugreek #turmericpowder #spices #lemonpickle #wheatflour #driedgarlicgranules #mustardseed </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

Many [[Pickle|pickle]] recipes from India have [[Oil|oil]] to [[Help|help]] [[Preserve|preserve]] the pickle, but this recipe uses no oil.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 8 unwaxed [[Lemons|lemons]]\n| &frac12; cup of [[Salt|salt]]\n| &frac14; cup of [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 4 small [[Green chillies|green chillies]]\n| 1 tablespoon yellow [[Mustard seed|mustard seed]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Ground ginger powder|ground ginger powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]] [[Seed|seed]]\n| &frac14; teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 1 to 3 whole [[Star anise|star anise]] pods\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Wash the [[Lemons|lemons]] in very hot water and dry thoroughly\n| Halve the [[Lemons|lemons]] and remove the pips\n| Cut [[Lemons|lemons]] into small pieces, and place in a bowl\n| Cover with [[Salt|salt]] and set aside for at least 24 hours\n| Chop the [[Chillies|chillies]] finely.\n| Dry-roast the yellow [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]], [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]], [[Star anise|star anise]], and chopped [[chillies]] on a high heat, shaking constantly - don't burn them!\n| Strain the [[Juice|juice]] from the [[Lemons|lemons]] into a small saucepan, add the [[Turmeric|turmeric]], [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Sugar|sugar]], and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 2-3 minutes until the sugar has dissolved. If there isn't enough juice, add a tablespoon or two of water.\n| Add the [[Spices|spices]] and [[Sugar|sugar]] mixture to the bowl of [[Lemons|lemons]], and mix together well.\n| Pack into a pint jar, pressing the pieces in if needed, to ensure that the liquid covers all the [[Lemon|lemon]] pieces.\n| Set aside to mature for 1 month.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Pickled]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lemons #staranise #chillies #lemonpickle #mustardseed #mustardseeds #groundgingerpowder #ginger #help #lemon #fenugreekseeds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Lime pickle (Winter recipe)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Lime pickle, winter version, an Indian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#limes #jaggery #garlic #lime #chilipowder #onions #garammasala #pickle #vegetableoil #vinegar #juice \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Most of the lime pickle recipes I have seen require the limes to be 'cooked' in the sun for up to a month\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1486\n|PortionCalories = 45\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Bottled and ready to mature\n |Servings = Servings: 33 - Make 1 litre of [[Lime|lime]] [[Pickle|pickle]]\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 20 minutes + 24 hours\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Lime pickle bottled.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Put this down as an experiment...</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">2</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Didn't work for me.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nMost of the [[Lime|lime]] [[Pickle|pickle]] recipes I have seen require the [[Limes|limes]] to be 'cooked' in the sun for up to a month.  With frost still white on the [[Ground|ground]] in the middle of the afternoon, its going to be a while before I can experiment with that one.\n\nThis recipe however can be made even when it's snowing!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 6 unwaxed [[Limes|limes]], or more if they are small\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Chili powder|chili powder]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Garam masala|garam masala]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Jaggery|jaggery]] or [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| 6 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 125 ml [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 3 [[Onions|onions]], peeled and very finely chopped\n| 500 ml [[Malt vinegar|malt vinegar]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Wash the [[Limes|limes]] in very hot water, just in case they have been wax-treated\n| Halve them and pick out the pips\n| Cut into bite-sized pieces, reserving any of the escaping [[Juice|juice]]\n| Put the [[Limes|limes]] into a lidded Tupperware container\n| Mix the [[Chili powder|chili powder]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Garam masala|garam masala]], [[Jaggery|jaggery]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and any reserved [[Lime juice|lime juice]] together in a small bowl and mix well.  You may need to warm the [[Jaggery|jaggery]] a little first.\n| Add the mixture to the [[Limes|limes]], seal and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for up to a week if possible.  Shake daily.\n| After a week, heat the [[Oil|oil]] and saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] on a low heat until they become translucent, about 10 minutes. Don't [[Brown|brown]] them\n| Add the [[Refrigerated|refrigerated]] mixture to the pan and cook for about 15 minutes often. Take care not to break up the limes\n| Add the [[Vinegar|vinegar]], bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and immediately reduce the heat, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 1.5 hours\n| Remove from the heat, allow to cool and pack into [[Sterilised jars|sterilised jars]].\n| '''Leave in a cool dark place for a month to mature'''\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Lime pickle boil.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Bring to the boil and simmer for 1.5 hours\nImage:Lime pickle ferment.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Leave for a week in a sealed container\n</gallery>\n==See also==\n* [[Lemon pickle (Summer recipe)]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Pickled]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#limes #jaggery #garlic #lime #chilipowder #onions #garammasala #pickle #vegetableoil #vinegar #juice </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Lime Pickle 2",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Lime Pickle 2 recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#limes #ginger #garlic #turmeric #vinegar #limepickle2 #fenugreek #ground #cumin #hotchillipowder #boiledorsimmered \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A very delicious, spicy lime pickle to accompany rice dishes\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2050\n|PortionCalories = 62\n|DatePublished=17th October 2015\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Servings: 33 - Makes just over 1 litre\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 30 minutes plus 3-4 days salting time\n|PrepTime =  30 minutes\n|CookTime =  1 hour plus 3-4 days salting time\n|Image = [[Image:Lime Pickle 2 recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Sharp and tangy</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This pickle was really good with fatty meats.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\nA very delicious, spicy [[Lime pickle|lime pickle]] to accompany [[Rice dishes|rice dishes]]\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1.5kg [[Limes|limes]], left whole, but stem bits removed\n| 300g [[Salt|salt]] (I used pink Himalayan salt)\n| 70g [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and finely chopped (50g + 20g)\n| 40g [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and finely chopped (20g + 20g)\n| 150g [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]] (or other neutral [[Oil|oil]])\n| 70g extra [[Hot chilli powder|hot chilli powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]], [[Ground|ground]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Ground|ground]]\n| 50g [[Black mustard seeds|black mustard seeds]]\n| 500g water (200g + 300g)\n| 100g [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 60g [[Cider vinegar|cider vinegar]] (or [[White wine vinegar|white wine vinegar]])\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Place the [[Limes|limes]] in a [[Steamer|steamer]] containing water and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| [[Steam]] for 45 minutes.\n| Allow the [[Limes|limes]] to cool then cut each one into 8 pieces.\n| Place in a bowl and mix with the [[Salt|salt]].\n| Cover and leave for 3 days, stirring them twice daily.  No need to [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]].\n| After this [[Resting time|resting time]], rinse the [[Limes|limes]] with water and leave to drain.\n| Meanwhile, heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a pan and [[Fry|fry]] 50g of the [[Garlic|garlic]] and 20g of the [[Ginger|ginger]] until soft, then set aside.  Don\u0092t let the garlic [[Brown|brown]]. \n| Using a [[Blender|blender]], mix the [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]], [[Turmeric|turmeric]], [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]], [[Cumin|cumin]] and the remaining 20g each of the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Ginger|ginger]] with 200g of the water.  It should end up as a paste.\n| Tip the [[Fried|fried]] [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Ginger|ginger]] into a bowl, leaving some [[Oil|oil]] in the pan.\n| Re-heat the pan and when hot, add the [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]].\n| As soon as the [[Mustard|mustard]] starts to pop, add the [[Spice|spice]] paste.\n| Cook until the [[Oil|oil]] starts to separate.\n| Transfer to a [[Saucepan|saucepan]] with the remaining 300g water and [[Simmer|simmer]], covered, for 40 minutes, stirring frequently.\n| Add the [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Vinegar|vinegar]] and continue [[Simmering|simmering]], covered, for 10 minutes.\n| Add the previously cooked [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Ginger|ginger]], together with the [[Oil|oil]] and the [[Limes|limes]].\n| Mix together (off the heat) until the [[Limes|limes]] are coated in the [[Spices|spices]].\n| Put into [[Sterilised jars|sterilised jars]] with [[Vinegar|vinegar]]-proof lids and keep for at least one month before eating.\n| It is at its best after 6 months to 1 year though.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Adapted for conventional cookery from a recipe in '''Fast and Easy Indian cooking (Thermomix TM31 Cookery Book)'''\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#limes #ginger #garlic #turmeric #vinegar #limepickle2 #fenugreek #ground #cumin #hotchillipowder #boiledorsimmered </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

\n|Servings = 3-4 as part of a main meal\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  50 minutes (includes 10 minutes resting time)\n|PrepTime =  20 minutes (includes 10 minutes resting time)\n|CookTime =  30 We've used [[Filo pastry|filo pastry]] instead, so it works brilliantly warm or at room temperature\"''\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 100g lean [[Beef mince|beef mince]] \n| 1 [[Dessert|dessert]] spoon [[Keralan masala|keralan masala]] Mix\n| 1 [[Dessert|dessert]] spoon finely chopped [[Fresh ginger|fresh ginger]] \n| 1 [[Dessert|dessert]] spoon [[Nam pla|nam pla]] or other light [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]] \n| 5 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], finely chopped \n| 2 tablespoons of chopped fresh [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] \n| 1 tablespoon chopped fresh [[Coriander|coriander]] stalks \n| 1 lightly beaten [[Egg|egg]] \n| &frac14; teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] \n| A pinch of [[Sugar|sugar]] \n| 6 sheets [[Filo pastry|filo pastry]] \n| [[Coconut oil]] or [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]] for [[Brushing|brushing]] the [[Pastry|pastry]] and for [[Frying|frying]]\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to  200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the Masala Mix, [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]], [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Coriander|coriander]] stalks into a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]], and crush to a smooth paste. Add a dot of [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]] or [[Coconut oil|coconut oil]] if it\u0092s too dry \n| Heat a splash of [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]] or [[Coconut oil|coconut oil]] in a thick-bottomed saucepan and add 2/3 of the [[Chopped spring onions|chopped spring onions]]. [[Fry]] for 1 minute, then add the masala paste and fry for another 2 minutes, stirring with a wooden spoon all the while\n| Add the [[Beef|beef]], and [[Fry|fry]] for 4 minutes. Take off the heat, and add the rest of the [[Spring onions|spring onions]], the [[Coriander|coriander]], the [[Nam pla|nam pla]] and the beaten [[Egg|egg]] \n| Fold a large sheet of [[Filo pastry|filo pastry]] in half, [[Brushing|brushing]] it with [[Oil|oil]]. Cut a second sheet of [[Filo|filo]] in half , [[Brush|brush]] with oil and place it in the middle of the existing one to from a cross. Place a quarter of the [[Beef|beef]] mixture at the centre of the cross and fold the sides over it, brushing as you go with oil. Do the same lengthways to ensure that all parts of the filling are covered with at least two layers of [[Pastry|pastry]]. Place the parcel on a [[Baking tray|baking tray]], and repeat 3 more times \n| Place the tray in the [[Oven|oven]], and [[Bake|bake]] for 15 minutes, or until crisp and golden. Allow to rest for 10 minutes. \n}}\n===Serving suggestion===\nServe with a [[Green salad|green salad]] and [[Chili pepper sauce|chilli sauce]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#coconutoil #beef #groundnutoil #filopastry #coriander #dessert #brushing #madtarbark #fry #nampla #chillipowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

3470\n|PortionCalories = 348\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = 10\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 5 hours, 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 5 hours, 15 paneer|cheese]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1700 ml full [[Cream|cream]] [[Cows' milk|cows' milk]]\n| 560 ml single [[Cows|cows]]' [[Cream|cream]]\n| 70 ml distilled white [[Vinegar|vinegar]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* [[Sterilise]] all equipment\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Milk|milk]] in a saucepan over a medium heat, stirring from time to formed.\n| Line a [[Colander|colander]] with a double layer of [[Boiled|boiled]] [[Cheesecloth|cheesecloth]] and place in the sink or over a large bowl.\n| Pour the [[Cheese|cheese]] into the on the top of the cloth.\n| Leave until the [[Cheese|cheese]] is firm - this can take from three to five hours.\n| Remove the pan and the cloth and wrap in [[Cling-film|cling-film]].\n| It will keep in the [[Fridge|fridge]] for up to a week.\n}}\n===Servings===\nServings: 10 - Makes about 450 g\n===Serving suggestions===\nThe [[Cheese|cheese]] can be crumbled, [[Fried|fried]] or [[Grilled|grilled]].\n===Variations===\nIf you are on a low-fat diet, try our more traditional [[Mattar paneer|Paneer recipe]] which does not use cream.\n\nYou can make a totally organic version by using organic [[Milk|milk]] and [[Vinegar|vinegar]], including [[Cider|cider]] or white vinegar.\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you wish, you can freeze it for up to two months by placing in a self-seal bag and an airtight box such as a [[Lock&Lock boxes|Lock&Lock box]].\n* http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paneer\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Malai paneer]]\n[[Category:Cheese making|Malai teaspoon [[Ginger powder|ginger powder]]\n| 140 g [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]]\n| 100 g [[cornflakes]]\n| 100 g [[Caster sugar|caster sugar]], plus &frac12; teaspoon for dusting\n| 25 g flaked [[Almonds|almonds]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Grease a suitable [[Baking|baking]] dish with [[Butter|butter]]\n| Add the mangoes, [[brown sugar]], juice and zest of the [[tangerine]] or [[orange]] and 8 tablespoons of water\n| Stir and simmer for 5 minutes, remove from the heat and fold in your fruit of choice\n| Add the [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]] to a bowl and mix with the [[cornflakes]], scrunching them up as you go.  Add the [[Butter|butter]] [[Ginger powder|ginger powder]] and the [[Sugar|sugar]] and knead into the breadcrumbs with your fingers.\n| Spoon the crumble over the top of the [[Fruit|fruit]]\n| Sprinkle with the flaked [[Almonds|almonds]] and dust with the extra [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| [[Bake]] for 30 minutes until golden\n| As almonds can easily burn, lay a sheet of [[tin-foil]] over the crumble if it's getting too brown after 15 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with [[Home-made custard|homemade custard]] or [[Greek yogurt]].\n===Variations===\nThe original recipe called for rolled [[porridge oats]], but I changed it to [[cornflakes]] as I remember my mum making crumble like this, many years ago.  This type of crumble does not hold together as well as a flour-type crumble, but it's all crunch and delicious.\n==See also==\n* [[Mango and ginger crumble]]\n* [[Apple crumble recipe]]\n* [[Apple crumble recipe (Mum's)]]\n* [[Traditional crumble topping|traditional crumble topping]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#mangoandgingercrumble #cornflakes #butter #brownsugar #breadcrumbs #tangerine #gingerpowder #orange #almonds #porridgeoats #blueberries </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This is a translation of a recipe in '''Salsas y Ali\u00f1os con [[Thermomix]] (Susaeta Ediciones)'''.\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n| 50g [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]]\n| 160g [[Onions|onions]]\n| 1 [[Clove|clove]] [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| 100g Blanquilla pears\n| 100g [[Carrots|carrots]]\n| 380g [[Mango|mango]]\n| 200g [[Raspberry vinegar|raspberry vinegar]]\n| 100g dark [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| 100g [[White sugar|white sugar]]\n| A pinch of [[Cayenne pepper]]\n| 1 heaped teaspoons [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Fresh ginger|fresh ginger]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Peel the mangos, remove the stone and reserve the flesh.\n| Peel the [[Pears|pears]] and remove the core.\n| In the bowl, place the [[Oil|oil]], peeled and chopped [[Onions|onions]], the peeled [[Garlic|garlic]] and the washed [[Carrots|carrots]], cut into chunks.\n| Run for '''5 seconds / Speed 4'''.\n| Using the spatula, push the ingredients on the inside of the jug down to the bottom and set '''10 minutes / Temp, Varoma /  Reverse blade  /  Speed spoon'''.\n| Add the remaining ingredients and mix '''10 seconds / Speed 3'''.\n| Re-set '''30 minutes / Temp. Varoma /  Reverse blades  /  Speed spoon'''.\n| Once finished, transfer to a [[Glass|glass]] jar.\n| Leave to cool and keep in the [[Fridge|fridge]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThey are usually served as an [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] and they are made with a base of [[Fruit|fruit]] or [[Vegetables|vegetables]].  These spicy [[Sauces|sauces]] with a sweet and sour taste are eaten with [[Meat|meat]], [[Poultry|poultry]] and pat\u00e9.  They improve if left for a day.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n[[Category:Pickled]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#carrots #onions #garlic #sauces #thermomix #cayennepepper #chutneys #raspberryvinegar #whitesugar #glass #india </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Mango pachadi",
