                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Mango pachadi, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#curry #mustardseeds #mangopachadi #coconut #curryleaves #vegetables #sidedish #coconutmilk #rice #shallots #mangoes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Pachadi is a traditional South Indian side-dish. Broadly translated, it refers to food which has been pounded\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1907\n|PortionCalories = 476\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4 as a [[Side dish|side dish]]\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 25 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Mango pachadi recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A nice dip</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Great for dipping slices of vegetables and roti.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nPachadi is a traditional South Indian side-dish. Broadly translated, it refers to food which has been pounded. The definition of the word 'Pachadi' is different among different South Indian regions. While in Kerala and Tamilnadu, pachadi is a side-dish [[Curry|curry]] similar to the north Indian [[Raita]], in Andhra Pradesh, pachadi is a fresh [[Pickle|pickle]] and has very low shelf life, a maximum of two or three days. It is made of fresh [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and is served as an [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] for [[Rice|rice]], [[Snacks|snacks]] like idli, [[Dosa|dosa]], pesarattu.\n\nIn Kerala and Tamilnadu states pachadi is eaten fresh and typically made of finely chopped and [[Boiled|boiled]] [[Vegetables|vegetables]] with [[Coconut|coconut]], green or [[Red chillies|red chillies]] and tempered in [[Oil|oil]] with [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]], [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]]. [[Curd]]/[[Yogurt|yogurt]] based pachadi can be made of any [[Vegetable|vegetable]], although [[Cucumbers|cucumbers]], [[Squash|squash]], [[Mango|mango]], [[Bitter|bitter]] gourd or [[Pineapple|pineapple]] are common. Pachadi is commonly eaten with [[Rice|rice]] and a [[Lentil|lentil]] [[Curry|curry]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 or 2 ripe [[Mangoes|mangoes]], peeled, stone removed and cut into nibble-sized cubes\n| &#189; an [[Onion|onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] to taste\n| 2 or 3 [[Green chillies|green chillies]] chopped into rings\n| 2 tablespoons freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Coconut|coconut]] or 2 tablespoons [[desiccated coconut]]\n| &#189; can [200 g (7 oz)] of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| &#188; teaspoon freshly [[Ground|ground]] [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]]\n}}\n'''garnish'''\n* A few tablespoons of [[Oil|oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n* 1 red [[Chilli|chilli]], chopped into rings (optional)\n* 1 [[Shallot|shallot]], peeled and thinly sliced\n* 1 tablespoon [[Mustard seeds]]\n* A few [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]], optional\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Mangoes|mangoes]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]], [[Coconut|coconut]], [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]] powder , [[Salt|salt]] and 250 ml (0.43 pint) of water to a pan.\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] then reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 15 to 25 minutes until it thickens a little.\n| Meanwhile heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Frying pan|frying pan]], add the [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]] and once they begin to pop, stiur in the [[Shallots|shallots]], [[Red chillies|red chillies]] and [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]].\n| Once the [[Shallots|shallots]] have [[Browned|browned]] a little, stir the garnish into the [[Curry|curry]] mixture and serve as a [[Side dish|side dish]] or as a curry on its own with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]].\n}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#curry #mustardseeds #mangopachadi #coconut #curryleaves #vegetables #sidedish #coconutmilk #rice #shallots #mangoes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This is an excellent way to finish a\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1116\n|PortionCalories = 139\n|DatePublished=2nd January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Our fabulous [[ice-cream maker]]\n|Servings = Serves 8\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  2 hours, 45 minutes\n|PrepTime =  2 hours 45 minutes\n|CookTime =  none\n|Image = [[Image:Freezing Ice cream maker.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Tea flavoured ice-cream</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Strange, but true!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nYou can always expect the unexpected from [[Nik & Edwina]] as in this [[Tea|tea]] [[Ice cream]] recipe recently sent to me by Nik.\n\nThis is an excellent way to finish a [[Curry|curry]], and always reminds us of the chai - [[Indian]] [[Tea|tea]] - served on Indian trains in little clay cups. It\u0092s got a comforting, creamy [[Tea|tea]]-ish flavour, against a warm, inviting [[Spice|spice]]y background. We make it with Rooibos tea bags so it is [[Caffeine|caffeine]] free but traditionally you\u0092d use a strong tea such as Assam. Chai spice is available from Indian supermarkets throughout London - we get ours in Tooting - but can also be found [http://www.spicesofindia.co.uk/acatalog/Indian-Food-Chai-Garam-Masala.html#aDBE020 online (Spices of India)]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 litre half [[Fat|fat]] [[Milk|milk]] \n| 50g [[Caster Sugar|caster sugar]] \n| 2 [[Cardamom pods|cardamom pods]], [[Split|split]]\n| 6 Assam [[Tea|tea]] bags or 7 Rooibos [[Tea|tea]] bags \n| 1 heaped teaspoon chai [[Spice|spice]] \n| 125ml [[Double Cream|double cream]], whipped until firm but not stiff\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Put the [[Milk|milk]] in a large heavy based saucepan, bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 25 minutes or until reduced to 750ml \n| Add the [[Sugar|sugar]], [[Tea|tea]] bags, [[Cardamom|cardamom]], and chai [[Spice|spice]]. Stir well, return to the heat and [[Boil|boil]] for a further 15 minutes. This will reduce the mixture to about 500ml. Squeeze the [[Milk|milk]] out of the [[Tea|tea]] bags and remove. Allow the mixture to cool\n| Once cool, [[Sieve|sieve]] the mixture than whisk in the [[Double Cream|double cream]]\n| Put into an [[Ice cream maker|ice cream maker]] or [[Freeze|freeze]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nWe serve it with plain or [[Frozen|frozen]] [[Yoghurt|yogurt]], and it goes very well with [[Mangoes|mangoes]] too\n===Recipe source===\n\n* https://sites.google.com/site/nikandedwinascookbook/Home/desserts/masala-chai-ice-cream\n==Seea also==\n* [[Spices of India]]\n* [[:Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes|Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tea #spice #doublecream #boil #masalachaiicecream #castersugar #sieve #caffeine #curry #recipesfromothersites #fat </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Masala cheese and rice, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#khichdi #masalacheeseandrice #fried #vegetableoil #breadcrumbs #baking #batter #casseroledish #bake #seeds #bakingtray \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is based on a recipe in Vineet Bhatia's book Rasoi: New Indian Kitchen\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1334\n|PortionCalories = 166\n|DatePublished=23rd October 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Masala cheese and rice (fried)\n |Servings = 8 as a first course or 4 as part of a main meal\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Masala cheese and rice recipe1.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Curry and cheese</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Ace idea Julia, I could eat this for breakfast!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is based on a recipe in Vineet Bhatia's book '''Rasoi:  New Indian Kitchen''' (ISBN 1906650195).  In his restaurant, he serves it as a canap\u00e9, but I have adapted it to be more substantial and have treated it in two ways.  The first way is to shape it into balls, which are then [[Deep fried|deep fried]] and the second is to [[Bake|bake]] it in a [[Baking|baking]] tin or [[Casserole dish|casserole dish]].  You can do as I did and make half-in-half.\n[[Image:Masala cheese and rice recipe2.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Masala cheese and rice (baked)]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 quantity of [[Red onion khichdi|red onion khichdi]]\n| [[Plain flour]] (only if it is to be [[Fried|fried]])\n| [[Breadcrumbs]], mixed with [[Nigella|nigella]] or black [[Sesame seeds|sesame seeds]] (only if it is to be [[Fried|fried]])\n| [[Vegetable oil]] (only if it is to be [[Fried|fried]])\n}}\n'''For the filling / topping'''\n* 120g strong [[Cheddar cheese]]\n* 120g [[Mozzarella cheese|mozzarella cheese]]\n* 3 tablespoons [[Red onion|red onion]], finely chopped\n* 3 [[Green chillies|green chillies]], finely chopped\n* 1 tablespoon [[Fresh ginger|fresh ginger]], peeled and finely chopped\n* 6 tablespoon fresh [[Coriander|coriander]], chopped\n* 2 teaspoons of [[Chaat masala|chaat masala]]\n* [[Salt]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Khichdi|khichdi]] in a bowl and [[Mash|mash]] it up a bit using a fork.\n| In another bowl, mix the filling / topping ingredients until they stick together.\n| If you are [[Baking|baking]] it, simply use the [[Khichdi|khichdi]] as a base in a baking tin or [[Casserole dish|casserole dish]] and spread the topping mixture over it.\n| It can then be [[Baked|baked]] for around 20 minutes at 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - gas 5), or until the [[Cheese|cheese]] has melted.\n| To make the balls, divide both the [[Khichdi|khichdi]] and the filling into 8.\n| Take half of each [[Khichdi|khichdi]] portion into the palm of your [[Hand|hand]] and place a whole filling portion in the centre.\n| Take the remaining half of the [[Khichdi|khichdi]] and place it over the filling.\n| Shape into balls, ensuring that the filling is contained within the [[Khichdi|khichdi]].\n| Place in the [[Fridge|fridge]] on a [[baking tray]] and leave for about 30 minutes until thay have firmed up.\n| Put some [[Flour|flour]] in a bowl and add sufficient water to make a thin [[Batter|batter]].\n| In another bowl, place the [[Breadcrumb|breadcrumb]] mixture.\n| Heat the [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] in a fryer or deep saucepan to 180\u00b0 C.\n| Whilst this is heating, coat each ball in the [[Batter|batter]] and then roll it in the [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]] and [[Seeds|seeds]] until well covered.\n| [[Fry]] until golden [[Brown|brown]] and drain on kitchen paper.\n| Serve immediately.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Chilli and garlic dip|chilli and garlic dip]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#khichdi #masalacheeseandrice #fried #vegetableoil #breadcrumbs #baking #batter #casseroledish #bake #seeds #bakingtray </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Surely there's not enough moisture in a [[Poppadom|poppadom]] to enable it to puff up?\n\nWell there is and it works perfectly - I think they are much nicer than [[Deep fried|deep fried]] [[Poppadoms|poppadoms]] which always taste greasy and unhealthy.\n\nIf you really must have a '[[Fat|fat]]-kick' with your papadums, then first [[Brush|brush]] them with a tiny amount of [[Butter|butter]] or [[Olive oil|olive oil]].\n\nThey won't puff up if they are lying on top of each other, or if they are flat on the [[microwave]] turntable.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 8 [[Poppadoms|poppadoms]]\n| Spray of [[olive oil]] (optional)\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Arrange 4 [[Poppadoms|poppadoms]] at a time in a plastic bowl so they stand up independently.\n| You can spray with a little [[olive oil]] if wanted.  Not authentic, but healthier and tastier than sunflower oil.\n| [[Microwave]] for 1 to 2 minutes, checking progress as you go.\n| Remove only those that have fully [[Puffed|puffed]] up and continue until all are nice and puffy.\n| Leave to cool for 2 minutes after cooking because they don't become crisp until they have cooled down.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Microwaved poppadoms in plastic bowl.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Arrange in a bowl (plastic is best)\nImage:Khanum Poppadoms.jpg|thumb|300px|right|[https://www.amazon.co.uk/gp/product/B00TZT2EME/ref=ppx_od_dt_b_asin_title_s00?ie=UTF8&psc=1 Khanum Poppadoms Amazon uk - sometimes out of stock]\n</gallery>\n===Chef's notes===\nYou do not need special 'microwave poppadoms' for this recipe.  This works for any type of poppadom (or ''papadum'', if you so wish!).\n===The best poppadoms?===\nI've tried lots of different makes of poppadom, some good, some awful. One common problem is that they have a [[cabbage]] taste.  The best I've found (in the UK) are Khanum variety from Amazon (Prime).  They appear to go in and out of stock, but are worth hunting down.  My last order was \u00a39.90 for 10 x 220g packs. teaspoon [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]]\n| 10 green caradmom pods\n| 6 [[Cloves|cloves]]\n| 2 [[Cinnamon sticks|cinnamon sticks]], 7 cm long, broken in half\n| 2 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]] or [[Rapeseed oil|rapeseed oil]]\n| 1 large [[Red onion|red onion]], finely chopped\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 360 ml cold water\n| 1&frac12; teaspoons [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[Rice|rice]] in a bowl and cover with cold water.\n| Rub the [[Grains|grains]] of [[Rice|rice]] through your fingers to wash off any dust.\n| Drain the water and repeat the process until the water stays almost clear.\n| Drain, and return the [[Rice|rice]] to the bowl with some fresh water to cover.\n| Leave the bowl at room temperature for 30 minutes.\n| Meanwhile, coarsely grind the 4 [[Spices|spices]] in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]].\n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] or [[Oil|oil]] in a saucepan over a medium heat.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Ground|ground]] [[Spices|spices]], and saut\u00e9 until the onion is soft and turns purple [[Brown|brown]] (about 10-15 minutes).\n| Drain the [[Rice|rice]] and mix into the [[Onions|onions]].\n| Add the water and the [[Salt|salt]] and stir once.\n| Increase the heat to medium-high and cook until the water has evaporated and craters are beginning to form on the surface.\n| Stir once to bring the [[Rice|rice]] at the bottom of the pan to the surface.\n| Cover and immediately reduce the heat to the lowest setting and cook for 8-10 minutes.\n| Turn off the heat and allow the pan to stand, on the hob ring for a further 10 minutes.\n| Remove the lid, fluff the [[Rice|rice]] using a fork, and serve.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nI think you may need to be very careful to ensure that the [[Rice|rice]] does not stick to the bottom of the pan!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Mitty chawal]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Mitty chawal]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Mitty chawal]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Mitty chawal]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Mitty chawal]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #mittychawal #ghee #spices #onions #cinnamonsticks #coffeegrinder #onion #ground #grains #blackpeppercorns </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Murghi roti, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#murghiroti #rice #chicken #preparingacoconut #limejuice #desiccatedcoconut #garlic #ghee #onions #coconut #spices \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Murghi roti , (murghi ruti, chicken roti, chicken ruti): (rice cake with chicken) is a South Indian style dish made with cooked rice, cooked chicken SharmaJP\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2379\n|PortionCalories = 594\n|DatePublished=8th December 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Murghi roti served, with yogurt and peas\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Murghi roti recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">You MUST try this</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">If you love hot, spicy Indian food you will never stop making this.  Absolutely delicious, and you can tailor the spices to match your particular taste.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Murghi roti grilled.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Murghi roti after grilling]]\n[[Image:Murghi roti ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Murghi roti - the ingredients]]\nMurghi roti , (murghi ruti, chicken roti, chicken ruti): ([[Rice|rice]] cake with [[Chicken|chicken]]) is a South Indian style dish made with cooked rice, cooked chicken and lots of [[Spices|spices]].\n\nA great recipe for using up leftovers.  Please be very careful if storing cooked [[Rice|rice]].  [[Refrigerate]] the moment it has cooled and use within 1 day.\n\nTry this using two pans, see Chef's notes below.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 225 g (8 oz) uncooked [[basmati rice]].\n| 175 g (6 oz) cooked [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces - remove any [[bones]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]] or vegetable [[Oil|oil]]\n| 5 [[Fat|fat]] [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 5 cm (2\") [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and roughly [[Grated|grated]]\n| 150 g (5 oz) [[Onions|onions]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 fresh [[Coconut|coconut]], flesh grated and removed, see [[Preparing a coconut]]\n| 4 hot [[Chilli peppers|chilli peppers]] (red or green), finely chopped - de-seeded if desired\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n}}\n'''spices'''\n\n''The charm of this dish is the 'bite' of the whole spices, don't be tempted to grind them!''\n* 2 teaspoons whole [[coriander seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon whole [[cumin seeds]] (white)\n* 1/2 a teaspoon of whole [[fenugreek seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Quickly wash and drain the [[rice]] but don't rinse it as you normally would, this dish is best with rice of a starchy consistency. \n| Cook in boiling water for 7 to 11 minutes.\n| Rinse the cooked rice in cold water until it is cold.  Drain well.\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade and blend to a thick creamy pur\u00e9e - adding a little milk if it needs thinning.  Remember, the inside is not going to change much whilst being cooked and will remain at roughly the same consistency as it was when first mixed. \n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a [[Wok|wok]] or [[frying pan]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] all of the [[Spices|spices]] for half a minute, then add the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and allow them to cook for a minute or so.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and reduce the heat a little and let them cook until translucent; about 5 minutes.\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Coconut|coconut]] and [[Chilli|chilli]] to the [[Onions|onions]], mix well and remove from the heat.\n| In a large bowl, mix everything together with the rice puree.\n| Lightly [[Oil|oil]] a large non-stick oven proof [[Frying pan|frying pan]] put on a medium heat.\n| Preheat the [[Grill|grill]].\n| Add the mixture from the bowl to the frying pan and pat down so it is flat\n| Ensure the mixture is evenly distributed and cook gently for about 10 minutes or until the [[Rice|rice]] [[Cake|cake]] has properly solidified.\n| If it catches on the bottom of the pan, use a pallet knife to turn areas of the mixture over, the more crunchy bits there are, the nicer it will taste. \n| After 10 minutes or so, finish the rice cake off under a hot grill to it's nicely toasted.\n| Sprinkle with [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and serve immediately.\n}}\n\n[[Image:Action coconut scraper with vacuum suction base.jpg|300px|thumb|right|An easier way to prepare the grated coconut - [http://www.amazon.co.uk/gp/product/B00B7JDDL6?psc=1&redirect=true&ref_=oh_aui_detailpage_o07_s00 Action coconut scraper with vacuum suction base - \u00a38.98 Amazon UK]]]\n\nInstead of fresh [[green chillies]], I have used 3/4 teaspoon of diced [[ancho]] & 3/4 teaspoon diced [[chipotle]] (dried) [[chillies]].\n\nDoing a 'freezer clean out', we made a marvellous version of this with 1 [[chicken]] breast and a bag of cooked red kidney beans.  The chicken was thinly sliced and saut\u00e9ed with lots of crushed [[garlic]] and the kidney beans fried with the chicken and mashed down a little - rather like [[re-fried beans]].  This was added in place of the normally cooked chicken in this recipe.\n\nThis recipe is great for using up the leftover Christmas [[turkey]].\n===Chef's notes===\nHaving made this many, many times now, I'm coming to the conclusion that the best part is the glorious toasted crunchy outsides.  In future I will use two pans and made two thinner individual rotis.\n\nI heeded [[Preparing a coconut|my own advice]] and tasted the coconut before preparing it.  It was totally rancid, thank you Morrisons.  Luckily I had both [[coconut flakes]] and [[desiccated coconut]]. For two people, I used two big handfuls of flakes and 4 tablespoons of [[desiccated coconut]] soaked in boiling water for 5 minutes then drained in a sieve.  It worked fine and saved the day!\n\n===A better way of cooking this===\nAfter making variants of this for many years, I've discovered the best method of cooking is to spread the ingredients out on a lightly greased [[baking tray]] and bake at 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7) for 35 minutes, stirring up the contents every 10 minutes.  It might be an idea with a meat other than crayfish, to add the meat (or prawns) for the last 10 minutes so they don't dry out.\n===Variations===\nSteamed chicken works well in this recipe - Follow the [[Chinese style steamed chicken]] using a quartered onion and a handful of fresh herbs instead of the Chinese ingredients \n\n[[Image:Crayfish & coconut chili, 1.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Baking tray method shown here with [[Crayfish and coconut rice cake with hot chillies]]]]\n\n{{Template:SeeAlso Roti}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#murghiroti #rice #chicken #preparingacoconut #limejuice #desiccatedcoconut #garlic #ghee #onions #coconut #spices </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

title": "Murghi roti with nectarines and extra coconut",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Murghi roti with nectarines and extra coconut Indian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #rice #limejuice #garlic #nectarines #ghee #murghirotiwithnectarinesandextracoconut #coconut #onions #coconutmilk #spices \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This variation of Murghi roti was inspired by Miguel Ceramico (Apples) - he loved his fruity food! Murghi roti\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3779\n|PortionCalories = 944\n|DatePublished=8th December 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Murghi roti served with [[nectarines]]\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Murghi roti nectarines.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Currytastic!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">If you love curries and spicy food, you'll never stop making this.  It is really good.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis variation of [[Murghi roti]] was inspired by [[User:MiguelCer\u00e1mico|User:Apples]] - he loved his fruity food!\n[[Image:Murghi roti grilled side.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Murghi roti - after grilling]]\n[[Image:Murghi roti fried.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Murghi roti - frying one side]]\n[[Image:Murghi roti rice puree.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Murghi roti mixture - it's quite moist ]]\n\nMurghi roti , (murghi ruti, chicken roti, chicken ruti): ([[Rice|rice]] cake with [[Chicken|chicken]]) is a South Indian style dish made with cooked rice, cooked chicken and lots of [[Spices|spices]].\n\nThis recipe only differs from [[murghi roti|the original]] by the addition of 200 ml of coconut milk instead of normal milk. Oh, and its accompaniment - [[nectarines]]. A fantastic meal. \n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 225 g (8 oz) uncooked [[basmati rice]].\n| 200 ml [[coconut milk]]\n| 175 g (6 oz) cooked [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces - remove any [[bones]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]] or vegetable [[Oil|oil]]\n| 5 [[Fat|fat]] [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 5 cm (2\") [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and roughly [[Grated|grated]]\n| 150 g (5 oz) [[Onions|onions]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 [[Coconut|coconut]], flesh removed and roughly grated\n|* see [[Preparing a coconut]]\n| 4 hot [[Chilli peppers|chilli peppers]] (red or green), finely chopped - de-seeded if desired\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n}}\n'''spices'''\n''The charm of this dish is the 'bite' of the whole spices, don't be tempted to grind them!''\n* 2 teaspoons whole [[coriander seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon whole [[cumin seeds]] (white)\n* 1/2 a teaspoon of whole [[fenugreek seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Quickly wash and drain the [[rice]] but don't rinse it as you normally would, this dish is best with rice of a starchy consistency. \n| Cook in boiling water for 7 to 11 minutes.\n| Rinse the cooked rice in cold water until it is cold.  Drain well.\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade together with 200 ml of [[coconut milk]] and blend to a thick creamy pur\u00e9e.  Remember, the inside is not going to change much whilst being cooked and will remain at roughly the same consistency as it was when first mixed. \n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a [[frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] all of the [[Spices|spices]] for half a minute, then add the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and allow them to cook for a minute or so.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and reduce the heat a little and let them cook until translucent; about 5 minutes.\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Coconut|coconut]] and [[Chilli|chilli]] to the [[Onions|onions]], mix well and remove from the heat.\n| In a large bowl, mix everything together.\n| Lightly [[Oil|oil]] a large non-stick oven proof [[Frying pan|frying pan]] put on a medium heat.\n| Preheat the [[Grill|grill]].\n| Add the mixture from the bowl to the frying pan and pat down so it is flat\n| Ensure the mixture is evenly distributed and cook gently for about 10 minutes or until the [[Rice|rice]] [[Cake|cake]] has properly solidified.\n| If it catches on the bottom of the pan, use a pallet knife to turn areas of the mixture over, the more crunchy bits there are, the nicer it will taste. \n| After 10 minutes or so, finish the rice cake off under a hot grill to it's nicely toasted.\n| Sprinkle with [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and serve immediately.\n}}\n\n[[Image:Action coconut scraper with vacuum suction base.jpg|300px|thumb|right|An easier way to prepare the grated coconut - [http://www.amazon.co.uk/gp/product/B00B7JDDL6?psc=1&redirect=true&ref_=oh_aui_detailpage_o07_s00 Action coconut scraper with vacuum suction base - \u00a38.98 Amazon UK]]]\n\nDoing a 'freezer clean out', we made a marvellous version of this with 1 [[chicken]] breast and a bag of cooked red kidney beans.  The chicken was thinly sliced and saut\u00e9ed with lots of crushed [[garlic]] and the kidney beans fried with the chicken and mashed down a little - rather like [[re-fried beans]].  This was added in place of the normally cooked chicken in this recipe.\n===A better way of cooking this===\nAfter making variants of this for many years, I've discovered the best method of cooking is to spread the ingredients out on a lightly greased [[baking tray]] and bake at 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7) for 35 minutes, stirring up the contents every 10 minutes.  It might be an idea with a meat other than crayfish, to add the meat (or prawns) for the last 10 minutes so they don't dry out.\n[[Image:Crayfish & coconut chili, 1.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Baking tray method shown here with [[Crayfish and coconut rice cake with hot chillies]]]]\n\n===Chef's notes===\nSteamed chicken works well in this recipe - Follow the [[Chinese style steamed chicken]] using a quartered onion and a handful of fresh herbs instead of the Chinese ingredients.\n{{Template:SeeAlso Roti}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #rice #limejuice #garlic #nectarines #ghee #murghirotiwithnectarinesandextracoconut #coconut #onions #coconutmilk #spices </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This version uses mutton\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2971\n|PortionCalories = 742\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 45 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Mutton vindaloo recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Garlicy, but good \ud83c\udf36\ud83c\udf36\ud83c\udf36</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.67</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Made my lips tingle!</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nVindaloo is an Indian curry dish popular in the Goa region.  This version uses [[mutton]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 teaspoons whole [[Cumin|cumin]]\n| 5-6 [[Chillies|chillies]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Cardamom seeds|cardamom seeds]]\n| 1 [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]]\n| 1&frac12; teaspoons black [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]]\n| 75 ml white [[Vinegar|vinegar]]\n| [[Vegetable oil]]\n| 2 medium [[Onions|onions]], finely sliced\n| 300ml water or [[Stock|stock]]\n| 900 grams of [[Mutton|mutton]] cut into 2&frac12; cm cubes and trimmed of any [[Fat|fat]]\n| A thumb sized piece of [[Ginger|ginger]]. peeled\n| 2 bulbs [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled\n| 1 tablespoon [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Grind in a mortar or [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]], [[Cardamom seeds|cardamom seeds]], [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]] and [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]]. \n| Place the [[Ground|ground]] [[Spices|spices]] in a bowl with the [[Vinegar|vinegar]].\n| Heat [[Oil|oil]] the in a pan, over a medium heat. \n| Add the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Fry|fry]], stirring frequently, until they turn [[Brown|brown]] and crispy. \n| Leave the [[Oil|oil]] in the pan and blend the [[Onions|onions]] with 3 tablespoons water. \n| Add this [[Puree|puree]] to [[Spices|spices]] - the mixture can be [[Frozen|frozen]] at this stage if desired.\n| Grind the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] with a little water\n| Reheat the [[Oil|oil]], [[Brown|brown]] the [[Meat|meat]] cubes then remove them from the pan.\n| Add the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] paste to the [[Oil|oil]] for a few seconds, then the [[Turmeric|turmeric]] and [[Coriander|coriander]]\n| Add [[Meat|meat]] and all its [[Juice|juice]], the [[Vindaloo|vindaloo]] [[Spice|spice]] and the water. \n| Bring to a [[Boil|boil]], cover and cook until the [[Meat|meat]] is tender.\n}}\n===Serving Suggestions===\nServe with plain basmati rice and cooked vegetables of your choice.\n===Chef's notes===\nComments were that could have done with a tad more [[chilli]] and [[ginger]].\n==See also==\n* A selection of [[Vindaloo|vindaloo recipes]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mutton recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#ginger #garlic #muttonvindaloo #onions #vindaloo #chillies #mustardseeds #turmeric #cardamomseeds #peppercorns #vinegar </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Naan bread",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Naan bread, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#naanbread #dough #butter #naturalyogurt #miseenplace #pizzastone #pittas #muslin #yoghurt #driedyeast #bakingpowder \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Forget the take away, make it yourself from now on. These are way better than packaged shop bought naan breads\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 954\n|PortionCalories = 477\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Makes 4 of the best naan breads you will ever have tasted\n|Servings = 2 to 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 3 hours 15 minutes \n|PrepTime = 3 hours\n|CookTime = 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Naan.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Fluffy and crunchy</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">The only naans I've had that tasted better than these were in India!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nForget the take away, make it yourself from now on.  These are way better than packaged shop bought naan breads.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1/2 a teaspoon of [[dried yeast]]\n| 250 g (9 oz) strong white flour\n| 1 teaspoon of sugar\n| 1 teaspoon [[baking powder]]*\n| *''(can be omitted, see [[Talk:Naan_bread|discussion page]])''\n| 1 tablespoon of vegetable oil. I prefer to use [[garlic olive oil]].\n| 1/2 a teaspoon of [[salt]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[natural yogurt]]\n| *''can be replaced with 2 tablespoons of [[milk]], [[cream]] or [[buttermilk]] if [[yoghurt]] is not available''.\n| Add enough water to make a total volume 120 ml water and yogurt in total - or by weight: 120 g water and yogurt\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat your top grill to its highest temperature\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Bread maker Naan breads.jpg|Roll out to the size of a pitta bread\nImage:Breadmaker Naan breads.jpg||Divided into four\nImage:Seedy breadmaker naan breads.jpg|A seedy alternative\nImage:Rising naan breads.jpg|Leaving them to rise in a warm place for 20 minutes gives them a puffy texture. ''see text''\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Knead the [[dough]] by combining all the ingredients and sufficient water, this will be roughly &#190; cup.\n| Wrap the [[dough]] in a damp [[muslin]] cloth and leave it to rise for 2-3 hours.\n| Preheat an oven tray under your grill on it's very highest heat\n| Divide the [[dough]] into 4 small balls.\n| With a rolling pin or by slapping and stretching with your hands, roll out the balls so they are about the size of a pitta bread.\n| Unlike some breads, you don't need to let these prove, straight to the oven they go.\n| [[Brush]] a little vegetable oil on to the hot tray, slap the naans on to the tray and grill for about 2 minutes a side, '''watching it like a hawk!'''  The difference between perfect naan breads and a brown biscuit is about 30 seconds.\n| They should have a crunch on the outside and a soft spongy inside.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot, brushed with melted [[butter]].\n\n===Using a bread maker===\n\nIf you have a breadmaker, tip all of the ingredients into it, set it on a long (2:20) dough setting and start at step 3 above.  It could not be easier.\n\nFor the [[Breadmaker|Panasonic SD 253 breadmaker]], use basic dough setting.\n\n'''For the [[Panasonic SD-ZB2502 automatic breadmaker]] use menu option 16, basic dough.'''\n\n===Variations===\n\nExperiment with various flours.  The seedy naans shown were made with Allinson ''seed and grain bread flour'' instead of plain flour, and they were wonderful. You could of course, just add a handful of mixed grain (barley flakes, kibbled rye, sunflower seeds, millet and linseed) to normal flour.\n\nWe've found that by leaving them rise a little in a warm place such as on our fire, pictured, makes them puff up more that they do if you bake them immediately. They are even nicer this way and we now use naans as a preference to [[pittas]].   20 minutes is an ideal time for this, if you leave them any longer they achieve a very bready consistency and are not as nice.  Experiment!  \n\n===Chef's tip===\n\nUse a [[pizza stone]] if you have one for even better results.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Breadmaker recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#naanbread #dough #butter #naturalyogurt #miseenplace #pizzastone #pittas #muslin #yoghurt #driedyeast #bakingpowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

So nice to know you've made these yourself.</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nA popular first course in British Indian restaurants, but which can also be served as a snack or accompaniment.  This method makes use of a deep [[Fat|fat]] fryer.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 225 g ([[Chickpea|chickpea]]) [[Flour|flour]]\n| 2 level teaspoons [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Garam masala|garam masala]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], finely chopped\n| 2 tablespoons [[Mint sauce|mint sauce]]\n| 130 - 150 ml water\n| 4 medium [[Onions|onions]], finely sliced\n| [[Peanut oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Sieve]] the dry ingredients and mix in the [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and [[Mint sauce|mint sauce]].\n| Add the water and mix in to make a stiff paste; err on the dry side if necessary.\n| Stir in the [[Onions|onions]] and allow to rest for an hour or so.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] to 180 C and drop two or three tablespoons of the mixture into the basket.  Make sure that the bhajees are not touching each other.\n| [[Fry]] for two minutes, remove from pan and place on a large plate which has been covered with kitchen roll; they will not be cooked at this stage.\n| Switch off the fryer.\n| Once the mixture has been used and the bhajees have cooled slightly, shape them into balls.\n| Place them on shallow [[baking tray]]s, lined with [[Greaseproof paper|greaseproof paper]] or [[Bake-O-Glide]] and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 30 minutes or until you are ready to re-[[Fry|fry]] them.\n| Reheat the [[Oil|oil]] and [[Fry|fry]] the bhajees for a further two to three minutes until [[Brown|brown]].\n| Serve immediately.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Yoghurt mint sauce]].\n===Variations===\nFor a [[Shallow fried|shallow fried]], spicier version, see [[User:Chef|Chef's]] [[Onion bhajee (alt)|recipe]].\n===Chef's notes===\nThe amount of water needed is a case of trial and error.  If too wet, the mixture will stick to the [[Frying|frying]] basket, which will need to be washed if it does, before frying the next batch.\n\nShould you wish to keep the [[Oil|oil]] for future use, drain into a saucepan or bowl with the aid of a [[Colander|colander]] lined with [[butter muslin]].  Pour into airtight containers (such as [[Lock&Lock boxes|Lock&Lock]] jugs) and keep in the [[Fridge|fridge]].\n==See also==\n* [[Onion bhajee (alt)]]\n* [[Onion bhajis with mango salsa]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Onion bhajee]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Onion bhajee]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Onion bhajee]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Onion bhajee]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Onion bhajee]]\n[[Category:Starters|Onion bhajee]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Onion bhajee]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Onion bhajee]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onionbhajee #fry #mintsauce #corianderleaves #onions #yoghurtmintsauce #bakingtray #sieve #chickpea #fridge #flour </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

teaspoon [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chili powder|chili powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 bunch [[Coriander|coriander]], chopped\n| 150g [[Gram flour|gram flour]]\n| 1 [[Egg yolk|egg yolk]]\n| 50ml water\n}}\n'''To make the quick [[Mango chutney|mango chutney]]'''\n* 1 small [[Red onion|red onion]]\n* 2 teaspoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n* &frac12; teaspoon black [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]]\n* 1 red [[Chilli|chilli]]\n* 1 [[Mango|mango]], peeled, stoned and chopped into 8mm pieces\n* [[Juice]] of 1 [[Lime|lime]]\n* 2 tablespoons [[Sugar|sugar]]\n* 1 tablespoon fresh [[Mint|mint]], chopped\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Turmeric|turmeric]], [[Chili powder|chili powder]], [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Coriander|coriander]], [[salt]], [[Flour|flour]] and [[Egg|egg]] together. Leave to [[Marinade|marinade]] the flavours and rest the [[Batter|batter]] in the [[Fridge|fridge]] for 30 minutes. Meanwhile make the [[Mango chutney|mango chutney]].\n| [[Fry]] the [[Red onion|red onion]] in the [[Oil|oil]] for 5 minutes or until softened. Stir in the [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]] and [[Red chili|red chili]] and cook out for 1 minute. Add the chopped [[Mango|mango]], [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and [[Sugar|sugar]] and stir through. Cook on a low heat for 15 minutes or until the mango has cooked through. Remove from the heat and leave to cool. Stir though the [[Mint|mint]] then its ready to serve. You can make this a couple of days in advanced if you like and it does seem to get better with age.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large saucepan. Take a tablespoon of the [[Batter|batter]] and squeeze out any excess liquid, the drop into the oil and [[Fry|fry]] all over for 2-3 minutes, turning halfway through. Only do 4 - 5 tablespoons at a time so that they can [[Brown|brown]] nicely. Repeat with all of the mixture\n| Serve the [[Onion|onion]] bhajis hot with the quick [[Mango chutney|mango chutney]].\n}}\n==See also==\n* [[Onion bhajee]]\n* [[Onion bhajee (alt)]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:British Onions recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n{{Template:British Onions attribution}}\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#mangochutney #garlic #mint #batter #mustardseeds #coriander #mango #turmeric #ginger #fry #chilipowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

The chili flakes I have are slightly oily and would be heavier than truly dried chillies.\n\nWear rubber gloves and work in a well ventilated kitchen when handling this amount of chillies.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 250 ml [[Malt vinegar|malt vinegar]]\n| 350 ml [[red wine vinegar]]\n| 250 ml [[Juice|juice]] from [[Preserved lemons|preserved lemons]] (basically very salty lemon juice)\n| 200 ml water\n| 100 g [[Jaggery|jaggery]]\n| 2 pints (by volume) of Turkish [[Chilli flakes|chilli flakes]]\n| 2 [[Oranges|oranges]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add everything but the [[Oranges|oranges]] to a large pot and bring to the [[Boil|boil]]\n| Reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 15 minutes, stirring often\n| Meanwhile, halve the [[Oranges|oranges]] and extract the [[Juice|juice]]\n| Stir the [[Chilli|chilli]] mix to ensure the [[Jaggery|jaggery]] has dissolved\n| Mix in the [[Orange juice|orange juice]] and add the [[Orange|orange]] skins (they will be removed and discarded later)\n| [[Simmer]] the mixture for another 5 minutes\n| Remove from the heat and leave for 4 hours\n| Remove and discard the [[Orange|orange]] skins, being careful not to waste too much [[Sauce|sauce]]\n| Add the mixture to a food processor with a sharp blade and reduce to a [[Puree|puree]]\n| Decant into [[Sterilised jars|sterilised jars]] and store in a dark place for 3 months\n}}\n===Chef's tip===\nThis is very good - though it never got its 3 months rest! title": "Paneer - home-made unsalted Indian cheese",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Paneer - homemade unsalted Indian cheese recipes\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#curds #whey #ghee #lemon #cheese #rice #malaipaneer #cream #curdcheese #litres #paneer \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Paneer is an unaged, acid-set, non-melting farmer cheese or curd cheese made by curdling heated milk with lemon juice.\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2321\n|PortionCalories = 580\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Servings: 4 - Makes about 200g of paneer\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 1 day, 20 minutes\n|PrepTime = 1 day\n|CookTime =  20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Paneer.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Fun to make</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">But not as nice as my Cheddar</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\n\n[[Paneer]] (Hindi: &#2346;&#2344;&#2368;&#2352; pan&#299;r; Urdu: &#1662;&#1606;&#1610;&#1585; from Persian: &#1662;&#1606;&#1610;&#1585; panir) is a fresh [[Cheese|cheese]] common in South Asian cuisine. It is of [[Indian]] origin often referred in the Vedas dating back to 6000 BC. In eastern parts of [[India]], it is generally called Chhena. It is an unaged, acid-set, non-melting farmer [[Cheese|cheese]] or [[Curd cheese|curd cheese]] made by curdling heated [[Milk|milk]] with [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], [[Vinegar|vinegar]], or any other food acids.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1.2 [[Litres|litres]] (2 [[Pints|pints]]) full [[Cream|cream]] [[Milk|milk]]\n| 1 [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| [[Ghee]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* [[Sterilise]] all equipment\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| [[Boil]] the [[Milk|milk]], twice, leaving it to cool for 10 minutes in between boils, stirring well to prevent burning.\n| Squeeze in [[Lemon|lemon]] juice to split the [[Milk|milk]].\n| Cover a separate pan with a [[muslin]] cloth or a clean [[tea-towel]] and pour the [[Milk|milk]] through it to separate the [[curds]] and [[whey]].\n| Reserve the [[whey]], as it's useful to cook [[Rice|rice]] in.\n| Hang the [[Curds|curds]] in the cloth for a whole day to allow the remaining [[Whey|whey]] to drip out.\n| After this time, place the [[Curds|curds]] in the cloth under a weight to flatten into a [[Cake|cake]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThe paneer can also be cut into cubes and [[Fry|fried]] in hot [[Ghee|ghee]] until coloured a little.\n==See also==\n* [[Malai Paneer|Malai Paneer recipe]]\n* http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paneer\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#curds #whey #ghee #lemon #cheese #rice #malaipaneer #cream #curdcheese #litres #paneer </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

title": "Pan fried fish fillet with Malabar curry sauce",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pan fried fish fillet with Malabar curry sauce Indian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#fish #sauce #spice #turmeric #basting #ginger #nutmeg #cinnamonstick #roast #staranise #fennelseeds \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Another recipe personally recommended to me by Nik from Nik and Edwina's Cookbook. I cannot do any better than Nik's own comments:\"We both love fish\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2561\n|PortionCalories = 640\n|DatePublished=11th March 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 30 minutes\n|PrepTime =  30 minutes\n|CookTime =  1 hour\n|Image = [[Image:Fish curry with coconut and lemon grass wok simmer.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Not too spicy</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Could be a little hotter</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nAnother recipe personally recommended to me by Nik from [[Nik and Edwina's Cookbook]].\n\nI cannot do any better than Nik's own comments:\n\n\"We both love [[Fish|fish]], and we both love [[Curry|curry]], but we don't actually make that many [[Fish|fish]] [[Curries|curries]]. This though, is a gorgeous exception, a classy, sophisticated, exciting dish combining the subtle [[Spice|spice]] crusting of the fish with a complex, zesty, slightly fruity [[Sauce|sauce]]; the last [[Ingredient|ingredient]] to go into the [[Sauce|sauce]], the [[Tamarind|tamarind]], binds the flavours together perfectly. It\u2019s not a madly hot sauce, but the flavours are lifted by a medium strength [[Chilli|chilli]] heat. [[Brill]] works very well, it\u2019s quite a fishy fish, but we've tried it with [[Lemon|lemon]] [[Sole|sole]] and [[Monkfish|monkfish]] too, and they worked beautifully. The [[Butter|butter]] [[Basting|basting]] technique of cooking the fish is an interesting one, the fish is actually cooked much more slowly than conventional pan [[Frying|frying]], retaining flavour and texture and juiciness without making it greasy.\"\n\n'''pan fried fish'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n|4 x 180g [[brill]] fillets, skin on \n|2 tablespoons of [[ghee]] or [[clarified butter]] \n}}\n'''spice rub'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n|\u00bd teaspoon ground [[turmeric]] \n|1 teaspoon [[salt]] \n}}\n'''spice crust'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n|1 teaspoon [[allspice berries]] \n|1 dessertspoon ground [[nutmeg]] \n|1 teaspoon [[black peppercorns]] \n|2 [[blades of mace]] \n|5 cm piece of [[cinnamon stick]] \n|6 green [[cardamom pods]], opened, the seeds taken out, and the pods discarded \n|1 dessertspoon [[ground ginger]] \n}}\n'''masala mix for the sauce'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n|2 tablespoons ground [[coriander]] \n|2 [[green cardamom pods]], opened, the seeds taken out, and the pods discarded \n|2.5 cm piece of [[cinnamon stick]] \n|2 [[cloves]] \n|2 [[bay leaves]], finely chopped \n|2 teaspoons [[fennel seeds]] \n|1 [[star anise]] \n|\u00bc teaspoon [[ground cumin]] \n}}\n'''sauce'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n|3 tablespoons of [[coconut oil]] or [[vegetable oil]] \n|2 [[onions]], finely chopped \n|1 medium [[tomato]], finely chopped \n|10 [[curry leaves]] \n|5 cm piece of [[cinnamon stick]] \n|4 green [[cardamom pods]], opened, the seeds taken out, and the pods discarded \n|4 [[cloves]] \n|1 [[bay leaf]] \n|1 tbsp of the masala mix (see above) \n|5 cm piece [[fresh ginger]] finely chopped \n|\u00bd teaspoon ground [[turmeric]] or a 2 cm chunk of [[whole turmeric]] \n|\u00bd teaspoon [[black mustard seeds]] \n|\u00bd teaspoon hot [[chilli powder]] \n|150 ml thin [[coconut milk]] \n|2 teaspoons [[tamarind paste]]  \n|1 teaspoon [[salt]] \n}}\n'''to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB \n|Fresh [[coriander leaves]]\n|150 ml [[Greek style yogurt]] \n\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Pat the [[Fish|fish]] dry with kitchen paper, rub with the [[Turmeric|turmeric]] and [[Salt|salt]] and set aside for at least 30 minutes \n| To make the [[Spice|spice]] crust, [[Roast|roast]] all the [[Spice|spice]] crust ingredients except the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Nutmeg|nutmeg]] in a dry, heavy bottomed [[Frying pan|frying pan]] for about 4 minutes, until they start to smell lovely. Leave to cool, then grind to a coarse powder in a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]]. Add the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Nutmeg|nutmeg]] and mix well. Rub the mixture evenly into the flesh side of the four [[Fish|fish]] fillets, sprinkle some on a plate, and leave them skin side up on top. Set aside \n| To make the masala mix for the [[Sauce|sauce]], [[Roast|roast]] the [[Cardamom|cardamom]], [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]], [[Cloves|cloves]] and [[Star anise|star anise]] in a dry, heavy bottomed [[Frying pan|frying pan]] for about 4 minutes, until they are fragrant. Leave to cool, then grind to a very fine powder in a [[Spice|spice]] grinder or [[Blender|blender]]. Add the powdered [[Coriander|coriander]], [[Fennel seeds|fennel seeds]] and [[Cumin|cumin]], and give a final blitz to mix the [[Spices|spices]]. Set aside. \n| To make the [[Sauce|sauce]], heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]] and add the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]]. [[Fry]] gently for about 10 mins, or the [[Onion|onion]] is soft and translucent, then add the [[Cardamom|cardamom]], [[Cloves|cloves]], [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]] and [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]. When the [[Mustard|mustard]] [[Seeds|seeds]] begin to crackle, add the [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]], [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Turmeric|turmeric]], [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] and a tablespoon of the masala mix (the [[Rest|rest]] will keep well in an airtight container in a cupboard). Stir for one minute, then add the [[Tomato|tomato]] and [[Salt|salt]], and cook till soft. Add the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] gently for 20 minutes. Then add the [[Tamarind paste|tamarind paste]], and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 3 minutes. Then [[Sieve|sieve]] into a small saucepan and remove from the heat. Set aside and keep warm \n| [[Steam]] and drain the [[Spinach|spinach]] \n| To cook the [[Fish|fish]], heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a heavy bottomed [[Frying pan|frying pan]], add the [[Fish|fish]], skin side down, and cook over a low to medium heat for about 5 minutes, [[Basting|basting]] with melted [[Butter|butter]] as you do. Then turn over, and cook for another 4 minutes, still [[Basting|basting]] \n}}\n===Serving suggestion===\nPut a puddle of the [[Sauce|sauce]] on each of four plates and carefully place a fillet on top, skin side up. Put a spoonful of [[Spinach|spinach]] on one side and a decent sized blob of [[Yoghurt|yogurt]] on the other, scatter a couple of whole [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], and serve.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fish #sauce #spice #turmeric #basting #ginger #nutmeg #cinnamonstick #roast #staranise #fennelseeds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

693\n|PortionCalories = 115\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = 6 as a first course, or 3 as part of a main\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour\n |Image = [[Image:Cauliflower-wiki.JPG|200px|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A nice accompaniment</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.9</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Helps to pad out a curry.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Cauliflower]] in an [[Onion|onion]] and [[Chilli|chilli]] [[Sauce|sauce]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 280 ml hot, strong [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 2 [[Red onions|red onions]], 1 coarsely chopped and 1 cubed\n| 2 teaspoons [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 30 ml [[Rapeseed oil|rapeseed oil]]\n| 4 [[Indian green chillies]] (Hari [[Mirchi]]), thinly sliced\n| 1 bulb [[Garlic|garlic]], finely [[Diced|diced]]\n| 1&frac12; teaspoons [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 500 g [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]], broken into smallish florets\n| &frac12; tin chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Blend 70 ml of the [[Stock|stock]], coarsely chopped [[Onion|onion]], [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]] and [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] until you have a pur\u00e9e.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large pan until it has reached a medium-high temperature and add the cubed [[Onion|onion]] and [[Chillies|chillies]].\n| [[Fry]], stirring constantly, until the edges of the [[Onion|onion]] have [[Browned|browned]] and the [[Chillies|chillies]] begin to blacken - about 5-10 minutes.\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] when the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Chilli|chilli]] have been cooking for 3-4 minutes.\n| Add the pur\u00e9e mixture, rinse the [[Blender|blender]] out with a further 70 ml of [[Stock|stock]] and pour into the pan.\n| Reduce heat to medium and stir from time to time.\n| When the [[Sauce|sauce]] starts to stick to the pan, after about 7 minutes, remove from heat.\n| Add the remaining [[Stock|stock]] and return the pan to the heat, scraping off any [[Browned|browned]] bits that are stuck to the bottom.\n| Add the [[Salt|salt]] and the [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]], coating the florets with the [[Sauce|sauce]].\n| Reduce the heat, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for about half an hour.\n| Stir from time to time.\n| Stir in the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Coriander|coriander]] and warm through for a couple of minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Mitty chawal]] to carry through the onion-y theme.\n===Variations===\nTry with [[Broccoli|broccoli]] or any other firm [[Vegetables|vegetables]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Phool gobhi pyaaz]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Phool gobhi pyaaz]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper However, if you do, here is the recipe.\n\nI guess you could use a [[Chicken|chicken]] for this, but you won't get the wonderful livery flavour of [[Pigeon|pigeon]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 whole [[pigeons]], plucked and gutted and cleaned\n| 2 [[Onions|onions]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]]\n| Sea [[Salt|salt]] to taste\n}}\n\n'''[[Spice]] mixture'''\n* 12 dry [[Chillies|chillies]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[Cumin|cumin]] seeds\n* &#189; teaspoon black [[Mustard|mustard]] seeds\n* 2.5 cm (1\") [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and [[Grated|grated]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric|turmeric]] powder\n* 1 teaspoon [[fenugreek]] seeds, powdered\n* 6 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n* 1 to 2 tablespoons [[Malt|malt]] [[Vinegar|vinegar]], [[Sherry|sherry]] vinegar or [[Red wine|red wine]] vinegar\n\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a [[Coffee|coffee]] grinder or [[Food processor|food processor]], blend all the [[Spice|spice]] mixture ingredients to a fine paste\n| Quarter the pigeons\n| Peel and slice the [[Onions|onions]]\n| In a [[Wok|wok]], [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] in the [[Ghee|ghee]] until softened, about 4 minutes\n| Add the [[Spice|spice]] paste and sizzle for 5 minutes, stirring well\n| Add the pigeons and add just enough water to cover them\n| [[Simmer]] slowly until the [[Pigeon|pigeon]] is cooked and tender\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nI like to serve this curry with [[plain boiled potatoes]] (or even [[Chips|chips]]!) and a [[Mint riata]].\n\n==See also==\n* A selection of [[Vindaloo|vindaloo recipes]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Game recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pigeon #onions #spice #ghee #pigeonvindaloo #chips #grated #plainboiledpotatoes #sherry #boiledorsimmered #malt </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Dosa is a typical South Indian food, eaten for breakfast or dinner, and is rich in [[Carbohydrates|carbohydrates]] and protein.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 cup uncooked [[Plain rice|plain rice]]\n| 1 cup [[Parboiled|parboiled]] [[Rice|rice]]\n| &frac14; cup [[Urad dal|urad dal]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]]\n| &frac12; cup [[Yogurt|yogurt]]\n| 1 to 2 teaspoons [[Bicarbonate of soda|bicarbonate of soda]]\n| 10 to 12 teaspoons [[Ghee|ghee]] or [[Oil|oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n| Water for mixing\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Wash the [[Dal|dal]], cooked and raw [[Rice|rice]] in cold running water.\n| Add plenty of water and the [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]]\n| Leave to soak overnight\n| In the morning, wash rinse a few times and drain well\n| Grind the [[Rice|rice]] and [[Dal|dal]] with just enough water to make a smooth paste\n| Add the [[Bicarbonate of soda|bicarbonate of soda]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Yogurt|yogurt]] and mix well\n| Leave in a warm place for 12 hours\n| Give the [[Batter|batter]] a final mix and adjust the consistency by adding a little water if necessary\n| The [[Batter|batter]] should coat a dipped spoon well\n| Heat a [[Frying pan|frying pan]], [[Tava|tava]] or [[Griddle|griddle]] and add a teaspoons of [[Ghee|ghee]] when hot\n| Pour a spoonful of [[Batter|batter]] in the centre, spread with the back of the spoon to a thin round\n| Remove when crisp\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with [[Chutney|chutney]] and [[dips]]\n==See also==\n* http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dosa\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Dosa]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Dosa]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Dosa]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Dosa]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Dosa]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Dosa]]\n[[Category:Starters|Dosa]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Dosa]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #batter #plaindosa #bicarbonateofsoda #ghee #dal #fenugreekseeds #yogurt #parboiled #plainrice #chutney </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

pint) [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 150 ml pot [[Single cream|single cream]]\n| 25 g (1 oz) [[Butter|butter]]\n| 2 large [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], sliced\n| 4 [[free range eggs]]\n| Seat and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rinse the [[Rice|rice]] in a [[Sieve|sieve]] under cold water until it runs clear\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] to a large pot of [[Boiling|boiling]] water and [[Boil|boil]] for about 12 minutes - drain and keep warm.\n| [[Poached eggs|Poach the eggs]].\n| In a small pan, gently saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] in the [[Butter|butter]] for 5 minutes, don't allow it to colour.\n| Stir in the [[Curry powder|curry powder]].\n| Sprinkle the [[Flour|flour]] over the [[Onions|onions]], add the [[Milk|milk]] and stir until it thickens.\n| Season with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]].\n| Place the sliced [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] in the base of a serving dish, layer the [[Rice|rice]] next, top with the [[Poached eggs|poached eggs]] and then pour over the [[Curry|curry]] [[Sauce|sauce]].\n| Serve immediately from the dish.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Green salad|green salad]] or [[Vegetables|vegetables]] such as [[Broccoli|broccoli]] or [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Poached]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #poachedeggsindianstyle #poachedeggs #tomatoes #sauce #curry #currypowder #butter #onions #flour #plainflour </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Poppadom",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Poppadom: Cooking Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#poppadom #dough #onions #flour #appetiser #storecupboarditems #indianrecipes #cumin #roasting #dipsandcondiments #riceflour \n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=The poppadom (for alternative names see end of page) is a thin Indian wafer, sometimes described as a cracker or flatbread. An important\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n[[Image:Microwave poppadoms recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right|[[Microwave poppadoms|Microwaved poppadoms!]]<br>The best and healthiest way to cook them.|alt=Poppadom Indian bread starter]]\nThe poppadom (''for alternative names see end of page'') is a thin Indian wafer, sometimes described as a [[cracker]] or [[flatbread]].\n\nAn important part of Indian cuisine, recipes vary from region to region and family to family, but typically it is made from lentil, chickpea ([[Flour|gram]]), black gram or [[rice flour]]. In North India, the [[lentil]] variety is more popular and is usually called 'papad'. [[Salt]] and [[peanut oil]] are added to make a [[dough]], which can be flavoured with seasonings such as [[chili]], [[cumin]], [[Garlic|garlic]] or [[black pepper]]. Sometimes [[baking soda]] is also added. The [[dough]] is shaped into a thin, round flat bread and then dried (traditionally in the sun) and can be cooked by [[deep-frying]], [[roasting]] over an open flame, toasting, or microwaving, depending on the desired texture.\n\nPapadums are typically served as an accompaniment to a meal in India. It is also eaten as an [[appetiser]] or a snack and can be eaten with various toppings such as chopped [[onions]], chutney or other [[dips and condiments]]. In certain parts of India, raw papadums (dried but unroasted) are used in curries and vegetable preparations. Papadums are made in different sizes. Smaller ones can be eaten like a snack chip and the larger ones can be used to make wraps.\n\n\n'''Also know as:'''  ''Appadum'', ''Appala'', ''Appoll'', ''Appalum'', ''Papad'', ''Pappad'', ''Pappard'', ''Pappadum'', ''Popadam'', ''Poppadam'', ''Poppadom'', ''Papari''\n===[[Microwave poppadoms|Microwaved poppadoms]], the healthy option!===\nYou do not need to fry poppadoms, it's cleaned, quicker and healthier to [[Microwave poppadoms|cook them in a the microwave - recipe here]].\n{{CategoryLineIngredients}}\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Store cupboard items]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#poppadom #dough #onions #flour #appetiser #storecupboarditems #indianrecipes #cumin #roasting #dipsandcondiments #riceflour </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

639\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 days, 1 hour, 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 2 days, 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour\n |Image = [[Image:Porco com vinho e alhos recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Clever Julia, a great idea!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Lovely recipe this, just needs to spend a few days in the fridge first.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Pork with garlic and vinegar''', probably a forerunner to the famous [[:Category:Indian recipes|Indian]] [[Vindaloo|vindaloo]] dishes that the Portuguese brought to their colony of Goa on the western coast of India.\n\nFor best results, the [[Pork|pork]] needs to [[Marinate|marinate]] for 48 hours, so you need to plan in advance for this recipe.\n\n'''[[Marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 200 ml (7 fl oz) vinho verdhe [[White wine|white wine]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]\n| 4 [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 [[Clove|clove bud]]\n| 4 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Paprika|paprika]]\n}}\n'''For the stew'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 675g (1.5 lb) lean leg of [[Pork|pork]], trimmed of gristle, skin and [[Fat|fat]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 40g (1.5 oz) [[Ghee|ghee]] or [[Butter|butter]]\n| 225 g (8 oz) [[Onions|onions]], peeled and chopped finely\n| 6 cloves of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Cut the [[Meat|meat]] in to 4 cm (1.5 \") cubes.\n* Process all of the [[Marinade|marinade]] ingredients to a thin paste in a [[Food processor|food processor]] or [[Blender|blender]].\n* Mix the [[Meat|meat]] and [[Marinade|marinade]] together in a non-metallic bowl, cover and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 48 hours.\n* Preheat the oven to 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - gas 5)\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Porco com vinho e alhos marinade.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Off to the fridge for a few days\nImage:Porco com vinho e alhos ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Most of the the ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] and [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] for 10 minutes until softened.\n| Add the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Meat|meat]] and [[Marinade|marinade]] to a large [[Casserole dish|casserole dish]], mix well, cover and cook for 1 hour.\n| Check it every 20 minutes and add a little extra water if it starts to dry out.\n| Taste and season with [[Salt|salt]] before serving.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]] and [[sweetcorn]].\n===Chef's notes===\nThe original authentic recipe called for 4 [[clove buds]] which, with the similarly flavoured [[bay leaves]], I found a little overpowering and have therefore reduced the recipe to one clove.  This was a delicious dish that, strangely, gave the pork the texture, and to my mind, the flavour of beef. Although not authentic, I added a few chopped tomatoes as they were spare, and a few chillies for good measure too. Well worth making.\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n==See also==\n* A selection of [[Vindaloo|vindaloo recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Portuguese recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#porcocomvinhoealhos #marinade #onions #garlic #bayleaves #pork #ghee #vindaloo #stewedbraisedorpotroasted #sherryvinegar #butter </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
