                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Prawn and cauliflower curry with lime and coconut Indian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cauliflower #coffeegrinder #prawns #ground #garlic #noodles #nampla #bread #chillies #zest #simmer \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This simple Fishermans' curry from Vietnam has a wonderful spicy sauce and could be served with plain rice, noodles or even crusty bread\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3495\n|PortionCalories = 873\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Prawn & cauliflower curry with lime and coconut recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Basil, more basil</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">The basil makes all the difference.  If you can get Thai basil, even better.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis simple Fishermans' curry from Vietnam has a wonderful spicy [[Sauce|sauce]] and could be served with [[Plain rice|plain rice]], [[Noodles|noodles]] or even crusty [[Bread|bread]].\n[[Image:Prawn & cauliflower curry ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The ingredients]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1 lb) raw tiger [[Prawns|prawns]], [[Scampi|scampi]], [[King prawns|king prawns]] etc.\n| [[Zest]] and [[Juice|juice]] of 1 [[Lime|lime]].\n| 1 tablespoon [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]].\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped.\n| 4 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, peeled and roughly chopped.\n| 4 [[Dried|dried]] birds' eye [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Ground|ground]] to powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or crushed in a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]] (or to taste).\n| 1 [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]], broken into florets.\n| 1 teaspoon [[Jaggery|jaggery]] or [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]].\n| 1 teaspoon [[coriander seeds]], [[ground]] to a powder in a [[coffee grinder]].\n| 2 teaspoons [[fenugreek seeds]], ground to powder in a [[coffee grinder]].\n| 2 whole [[Star anise|star anise]], [[dry-fried]] and [[Ground|ground]] to a powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]].\n| 1 can (450ml) [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]].\n| A splash of [[nam pla]]\n| A handful of [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] or [[basil leaves]], stalks removed, for garnish.\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]].\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Remove the shells from the [[Prawns|prawns]] and de-vein them. \n* Place in a bowl with the [[Lime|lime]] [[Zest|zest]] and juice and leave in a cool place for an hour or so if you have time.\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Oil|oil]] to a hot [[Wok|wok]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] for 5 minutes, add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Chillies|chillies]] and as soon as the garlic starts to colour.\n| Add the [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]].\n| Add the [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]] and [[Stir-fry]] for 4 minutes, don't allow the [[Garlic|garlic]] to burn.\n| Add the [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Spices|spices]], once combined, add the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] and the [[nam pla]].\n| Reduce to a low [[Simmer|simmer]] and heat for 10 to 15 minutes.\n| [[Simmer]] for a little longer if you feel it needs further reduction.\n| Add the bowl of [[Prawns|prawns]], together with the [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and cook until the prawns turn pink, this should only take 3 minutes or so.\n| Season to taste with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and serve, sprinkled with [[Coriander|coriander]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with [[Noodles|noodles]], [[Rice|rice]], or crusty [[Bread|bread]].\n===Variations===\nInstead of [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]], try [[Broccoli|broccoli]], cubes of [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] or even [[Potatoes|potatoes]], though they will need par-[[Boiling|boiling]] first.\n===Chef's note===\nIf you prefer your cauliflower softer, then [[par boil]] it for 3 minutes before [[stir-frying]].\n'''This was a fantastic curry!'''  I made with one whole star anise (not one 'petal'), but I think it would be better with 2.  I used 6 dried [[birds' eye chillies]] and 2 large dried [[chile de Arbole]].  I had run out of limes so I used bottled lemon juice and a handful of crushed lemon leaves from our ornamental tree in the [[marinade]] and the cooking.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cauliflower #coffeegrinder #prawns #ground #garlic #noodles #nampla #bread #chillies #zest #simmer </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

title": "Prawn balchao pickle",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Prawn balchao pickle, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#ginger #driedshrimp #chillipowder #garlic #shrimps #prawns #maltvinegar #nigella #seeds #prawnbalchaopickle #pickle \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Prawn balchao (Prawn pickle - balchao is Portuguese for pickle)\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1543\n|PortionCalories = 38\n|DatePublished=2nd January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Servings: 40 - Makes about 1 litre of pickle\n |TotalTime = 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 30 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Prawn Balchao recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Fishy Pickle</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.9</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Lovely with chips!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Prawn]] balchao (Prawn [[Pickle|pickle]] - ''balchao'' is [[Portuguese]] for pickle).  Although this recipe refers to the [[Shellfish|shellfish]] as [[Prawns|prawns]], they are actually [[Shrimps|shrimps]], much smaller than prawns.\n\nThis version is made using [[Dried shrimps|dried shrimps]], which you can get from any oriental wholesaler.  Although they are [[Dried|dried]], you will find them in the chill cabinet and need to be kept [[Refrigerated|refrigerated]].  They are worth buying as they are a great addition to [[Special fried rice|special fried rice]].\n\nSoak the [[dried shrimp]] for an hour in just-[[Boiled|boiled]] water to rehydrate them. This also helps to wash off any dust and excess salt.\n\nLeave for a few weeks to mature, this [[Pickle|pickle]] is great as a [[Condiment|condiment]] and even makes a great spread for sandwiches if you like it hot!\n\n===Prawn balchao as meal===\nI have had a requests from people for a prawn balchao ''meal'' recipe, rather than one for a pickle.  I'm afraid that I have not been able to find any recipes that refer to prawn balchao as a finished dish.  Even the wonderful \"India\" - Mr Pushpash Pent:  ISBN 978-0714859026 states: \"The dish is know for it's piquant character: It is more like a pickle relish and is consumed in moderation\".\n\nIf anyone has any helpful information that may clear up this confusion, please do drop me a note via the ''Contact the Editor'' link above.--[[User:Chef|Jerry, aka Chef]] 18:14, 10 December 2012 (UTC)\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 100 g [[Dried shrimp|dried shrimp]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 5 cm (2\") piece if [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 whole bulb of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 4 tablespoons [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e\n| 140 ml [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Nigella|nigella]] [[Seeds|seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon to 1 tablespoon [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] - see Chef's notes\n| 1 to 2 tablespoons [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 1 to 2 tablespoons [[Cooking salt|cooking salt]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Jaggery|jaggery]], ([[White sugar|white sugar]] is fine)\n| 300 ml [[Malt vinegar|malt vinegar]]\n| Lime juice to taste\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Rinse the [[Dried shrimp|dried shrimp]] and leave to rehydrate for a few hours in just-[[Boiled|boiled]] water.  Drain, pat dry.\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Mezzaluna.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Half of the [[dried shrimp]] chopped with a [[mezzaluna]]\nImage:Prawn Balchao ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The ingredients for shrimp balchao\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Roughly chop the half of the [[Shrimps|shrimps]], leaving the others whole\n| Crush the [[Garlic|garlic]], chop the [[Onions|onions]] very finely\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and add the [[Nigella|nigella]] [[Seeds|seeds]] and let them [[Fry|fry]] for a few seconds, then immediately add the onions, [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[ginger]]. Reduce the heat and fry for 5 minutes or until lightly [[Browned|browned]].\n| Add the [[tomato puree]], [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]], [[Black pepper|black pepper]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Turmeric|turmeric]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a few minutes until well combined.\n| Add the whole and chopped [[Prawns|prawns]], [[Vinegar|vinegar]] and [[Sugar|sugar]].\n| Cook on a medium heat for 10 minutes.\n| Taste and make the final adjustments so it suits your taste.\n| Allow to cool and bottle in [[Sterilised jars|sterilised jars]].\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nThis is fantastic - I can't see it surviving the 2 week maturation period!\n\nWhen tinkering with the final seasoning I added a little more [[jaggery]] and the juice of a 2 limes which made the balance perfect for me. I made this batch with 1 tablespoon of black pepper but next time I would probably only use 1 teaspoon of black pepper.\n\nI no longer keep fresh [[ginger]], instead I buy in bulk from the ethnic supermarket and make my own [[very lazy ginger]] on a huge scale.  As I use it up I am left with pints of [[ginger]] flavoured [[white wine vinegar]] so in this recipe I used that instead of [[malt vinegar]].\n\nI also used Turkish [[chilli flakes]] instead of [[chilli powder]].\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Pickled]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#ginger #driedshrimp #chillipowder #garlic #shrimps #prawns #maltvinegar #nigella #seeds #prawnbalchaopickle #pickle </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Prawn curry, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#grated #prawncurry #fry #tomato #lemonjuice #simmer #coconut #tomatopuree #ghee #chili #carrot \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is the recipe from my Indian cookery evening class from years ago\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 753\n|PortionCalories = 188\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 40 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 25 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Prawn curry recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Tastes authentic to me!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">As good as any Indian take-away!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is the recipe from my Indian cookery evening class from years ago.  It's quite involved but worth the effort, especially if you have all of the ingredients to hand.\n\nIt's strange, writing this, I have an odd yearning for the 'communal cooking' that I enjoyed from those far off lessons.  If you get a chance to try evening classes then do have a go, it's great fun - it also removed all of the mystique of cookery for me.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tablespoon [[Ghee|ghee]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped finely\n| 1 [[Clove|clove]] of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 1 cm (1/2 \") [[Ginger root|ginger root]], peeled and [[Grated|grated]]\n| 1 fresh [[Tomato|tomato]], chopped\n| &#188; teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| &#188; teaspoon [[Chili powder|chili powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]] seeds\n| 1 teaspoon [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| 2 teaspoons freshly [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]] seeds\n| 7.5 cm (3\") from a packet of creamed [[Coconut|coconut]] dissolved in 426 ml (3/4 pint) [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] or warm water\n| 1 fresh green [[Chili|chili]], sliced\n| 2 tablespoons [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]]\n| 1 [[Carrot|carrot]], scrubbed and [[Grated|grated]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 450 g (1 lb) fresh [[Prawns|prawns]], peeled and cleaned\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] in the [[Ghee|ghee]] until soft, about 4 minutes\n| Add the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Fry|fry]] until they take some colour, add the powder [[Spices|spices]] and [[Stir fry|stir fry]] for a minute\n| Add [[Tomato|tomato]], [[Coconut|coconut]] and [[Stock|stock]], [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]] and green [[Chili|chili]].\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]], uncovered for 15 minutes until reduced slightly\n| Add the [[Grated|grated]] [[Carrot|carrot]], [[Prawns|prawns]] and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], [[Simmer|simmer]] for a minute or so\n| Pour into a serving bowl\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]] and [[Naan breads|naan breads]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#grated #prawncurry #fry #tomato #lemonjuice #simmer #coconut #tomatopuree #ghee #chili #carrot </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Pulao rice",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pulao rice, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pulaorice #onions #sultanas #almonds #clarification #stock #crackedwheat #rice #cardamompods #sweetcorn #pilaf \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This version of pillau rice is a bit of a fiddle but worth making it if you have the time\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1382\n|PortionCalories = 345\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 40 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 25 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Pullau rice.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Smells so nice</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Don't skimp on the spices, they make all the difference between the poor quality 'coloured' rice offered by some take-aways and the real thing.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''[[Pilaf]]''', also called '''polao''', '''pilau''' or '''pulao''', is a dish in which a grain, such as [[rice]] or [[cracked wheat]], is browned in [[oil]], and then cooked in a seasoned [[stock]]. Depending on the local cuisine it may also contain a variety of meat and vegetables. Pilaf and similar dishes are common to Middle Eastern, Central, South Asian, Latin American and Caribbean cuisine.\n\nThis version of pulao rice is a bit of a fiddle but worth making it if you have the time.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 Cups [[Basmati rice]] (well rinsed under cold water)\n| 1 Knorr chicken cube\n| 2 oz [[Clarification|ghee]] or oil\n| 6 whole [[cloves]]\n| 6 black or green [[cardamom pods]] (slightly crushed under a flat knife)\n| 1 5cm (2\") rolled [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]] stick\n| 4 cups boiling water\n| &#189; teaspoon [[turmeric]] powder\n| pinch of [[saffron]] strands\n| 1 oz flaked [[almonds]]\n| 1 oz seedless [[sultanas]]\n| 2 medium [[onions]], chopped (1 for garnish, 1 for the rice)\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a large heavy pan melt the [[Clarification|ghee]] and fry both of the chopped [[onions]] until browned\n| remove half of the [[onions]] and reserve, leaving most of the oil in the pan\n| Add dry spices and fry for 2 minutes\n| Add the rice and coat with the oil and spices\n| Sprinkle the crumbled stock cube over the rice mixture\n| Add water and bring to the boil, cover and simmer for 10-12 minutes. Don't lift the lid\n| Remove from heat and leave undisturbed for a further 10 minutes.\n| Meanwhile, reheat the reserved onions for a garnish.\n| Add the [[sultanas]] and the almonds and fry for the last minute or so.\n| Place rice on a serving dish and fork in the onions and [[almonds]]\n| Leave the woody spices in for authenticity, but don't eat them!\n}}\n===Variations===\n\nAt the last minute, stir in cooked frozen [[peas]], chopped [[sweet peppers]], [[sweetcorn]] or any [[vegetables]] of your choosing.\n\nSwitch sultanas raisins or dried apricots.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pulaorice #onions #sultanas #almonds #clarification #stock #crackedwheat #rice #cardamompods #sweetcorn #pilaf </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

Depending on the local cuisine it may also contain a variety of vegetables. Pilaf and similar dishes are common to Middle Eastern, Central, South Asian, Latin American and Caribbean cuisine.\n\nThis version of pulao rice is a bit of a fiddle but worth making it if you have the time.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 Cups [[Basmati rice]] (well rinsed under cold water)\n| 1 Knorr vegetable stock cube (dissolved in 4 cups of hot water)\n| 2 oz [[vegetable oil]]\n| 6 whole [[cloves]]\n| 6 black or green [[cardamom pods]] (slightly crushed under a flat knife)\n| 1 5cm (2\") rolled [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]] stick\n| 4 cups boiling water\n| &#189; teaspoon [[turmeric]] powder\n| pinch of [[saffron]] strands\n| 1 oz flaked [[almonds]]\n| 1 oz seedless [[sultanas]]\n| 2 medium [[onions]], chopped (1 for garnish, 1 for the rice)\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a large heavy pan melt the [[oil]] and fry both of the chopped [[onions]] until browned\n| remove half of the [[onions]] and reserve, leaving most of the oil in the pan\n| Add dry spices and fry for 2 minutes\n| Add the [[rice]] and coat with the oil and spices\n| Add water and bring to the boil, cover and simmer for 10-12 minutes. Don't lift the lid\n| Remove from heat and leave undisturbed for a further 10 minutes.\n| Meanwhile, reheat the reserved onions for a garnish.\n| Add the [[sultanas]] and the almonds and fry for the last minute or so.\n| Place rice on a serving dish and fork in the onions and almonds.\n| Leave the woody spices in for authenticity, but don't eat them!\n}}\n===Variations===\nSwitch sultanas raisins for dried apricots \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onions #rice #sultanas #pilaf #pulaoricev #crackedwheat #basmatirice #almonds #cinnamon #cardamompods #turmeric </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Pumpkin and chickpea curry",
                "revisions": [
                    {

title": "Puri",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Puri, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#puri #foodprocessor #vegetableoil #yogurt #dough #flour #tava #panfried #chapati #indiandishes #strongwhiteflour \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Puri or poori is an unleavened flatbread, from India or Pakistan, that is quickly fried rather than being cooked on a tava\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1193\n|PortionCalories = 198\n|DatePublished=27th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 6 - Makes 6 puri\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 40 minutes\n |CookTime = 5 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Puri recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A different fried bread!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Lovely to dip into daal.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nPuri or poori is an unleavened flatbread, from India or Pakistan, that is quickly fried rather than being cooked on a [[tava]].  It should be a little smaller than a [[roti]] or a [[chapati]], about 13 cm (5\") round.\n\nWhilst kneading [[dough]] can be therapeutic, if time is your enemy, then the [[food processor]] is your friend.\n\nPuris are the perfect accompaniment to most [[Indian dishes]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 cup [[atta flour]] or [[strong white flour]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n| 2 tablespoons [[yogurt]] (optional)\n| Vegetable oil for frying\n| &#189; cup water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Tip all of the ingredients and half of the water into the [[food processor]] with a plastic blade or dough hook attachment\n| Blitz the mixture whilst adding a more water a little at a time until you have a soft, pliable dough that is not too sticky\n| Remove from the processor, dust with a little [[flour]] and rest for 30 minutes in a bowl, covered with a damp tea-towel\n| Divide into 6 equal parts and roll into balls\n| With a rolling pin on a floured surface, roll each roti out into a disc, about 13 cm (5\") round\n| Heat 2.5 cm (1\") oil in a wok or large heavy-based frying pan \n| Deep fry each puri, holding it under the oil with a slotted spoon until it puffs up\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe immediately\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Puri]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Puri]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Puri]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Puri]]\n[[Category:Starters|Puri]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Pupusa]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#puri #foodprocessor #vegetableoil #yogurt #dough #flour #tava #panfried #chapati #indiandishes #strongwhiteflour </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

You can flip it over and [[brown]] the other side if you wish\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe immediately with a selection of chutneys, [[pickles]] or [[dips]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#batter #ravadosa #tava #frying #flour #corianderleaves #plainflour #vegetableoil #relishes #maida #panfried </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This recipe does not need preparing in advance\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1198\n|PortionCalories = 299\n|DatePublished=20th November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 25 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Red lentil kedgeree with avocado & tomato recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Vegetarian kedgeree</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A fabulous variation on kedgeree for the vegetarians amongst us.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nA vegetarian slant on the popular Indian breakfast dish that is perfect for a light supper or snack.\n\nThis recipe  does '''not''' need preparing in advance, but as supermarkets seem unable to sell ripe avocados at a reasonable price, if at all, it might be worth buying unripe avocados, leaving them on a window sill until nice and soft and making this recipe when they are just right.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 150 g [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]]\n| 150 g red [[Lentils|lentils]]\n| 15 g [[Ghee|ghee]] or [[Butter|butter]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 2 cloves of [[garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 2 tablespoons korma, Madras or [[Vindaloo curry|vindaloo curry]] paste\n| 1 [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]\n| 450 ml [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 1 ripe [[Avocado|avocado]]\n| 4 [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]]\n| 2 tablespoons chopped fresh [[Coriander|coriander]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 [[lime]], sliced to garnish\n| Chopped spring onions (optional)\n| Thinly sliced raw onions (optional)\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Soak the [[Rice|rice]] and [[Lentils|lentils]] in cold water for 10 minutes, drain well.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] and [[Butter|butter]] in a large pan and [[Sautee|sautee]] the [[Onion|onion]] gently for 5 minutes\n| Add the crushed garlic and the korma paste and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a few minutes\n| Tip in the [[Rice|rice]] and [[Lentils|lentils]] and [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]], stir to coat with [[Oil|oil]].\n| Add the [[Stock|stock]], stir once and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| [[Simmer|Simmer]], covered for 15 minutes - check that the lentils and rice are properly cooked.  If they are not cooked after 15 minutes, sprinkle a little more water over them if they are drying out and give them another 5 minutes. Some lentils take longer than others.\n| Peel and [[Dice|dice]] the [[Avocado|avocado]] and toss in the [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], chop the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Coriander|coriander]] and mix in with the [[Avocados|avocados]].\n| Season with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]].\n| Serve the [[Rice|rice]] and [[red lentils]], topped with the [[Tomato|tomatoes]], [[avocados]] and [[herbs]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe garnished with [[Lime|lime]] slices.\n\nAfter making this a few times we discovered that raw onions with a splash of lemon juice made a contrasting and refreshing garnish.\n===Variations===\nA few [[Nuts|nuts]] or [[Toasted|toasted]] [[Almonds|almonds]] would be nice added at the last minute.\n\nAdd 3 or 4 cloves of peeled and crushed garlic with the onions.\n===Chef's notes===\nThe prepared Indian curry pastes are a [[cheat]], but a great stand-by for recipes like this.  If you have your own fresh [[Spices|spices]] they you will know what to use to make an equivalent fresh [[Spice|spice]] mix.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes|Kedgeree]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #lentils #butter #avocados #onion #redlentilkedgereewithavocadoandtomato #lemonjuice #coriander #avocado #bayleaf #lime </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Red onion khichdi, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#redonionkhichdi #rice #butter #garlic #chilli #coriander #cuminseeds #turmeric #basmatirice #yoghurt #bread \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Khichdi is a kind of Indian risotto, but made with basmati rice. In India, it is usually made with half rice and half lentils\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1028\n|PortionCalories = 514\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 2 to 4 servings\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 35 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 25 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Red onion khichdi recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice rice!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Thanks Julia, this was lovely.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Khichdi]] is a kind of Indian [[Risotto|risotto]], but made with [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]].  In India, it is usually made with half [[Rice|rice]] and half [[Lentils|lentils]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 30ml [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Butter|butter]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 1 bulb [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Fresh ginger|fresh ginger]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 tablespoon fresh green [[Chilli|chilli]], finely chopped (leave [[Seeds|seeds]] in)\n| 1 [[Red onion|red onion]], finely chopped\n| 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| 150g [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]]\n| 600ml warm [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 45ml Greek-style [[Yoghurt|yogurt]]\n| [[Salt]], to taste\n| 1 tablespoon [[Coriander|coriander]], finely chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] and half of the [[Butter|butter]] in a largish saucepan over a medium heat.\n| Add the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] and when they begin to spit, add the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Chilli|chilli]] and [[Onion|onion]] and cook for 2 minutes.\n| Add the [[Turmeric|turmeric]] and [[rice]] and saut\u00e9 for a further 2 minutes.\n| Pour in the [[Stock|stock]], bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]], uncovered, until the liquid has been absorbed by the [[Rice|rice]].\n| Add the [[Yoghurt|yogurt]] and [[Salt|salt]] and cook for a few minutes longer.\n| Sir in the remaining [[Butter|butter]] and the [[Coriander|coriander]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nIt can be eaten as a [[Snack|snack]] with Indian [[Bread|bread]] or served as an [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] to a [[Main course|main course]].\n===Variations===\nThis is just a basic recipe.  Feel free to add cooked [[Vegetable|vegetables]] of your choice.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#redonionkhichdi #rice #butter #garlic #chilli #coriander #cuminseeds #turmeric #basmatirice #yoghurt #bread </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

teaspoon black [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]]\n| 4 green [[Chillies|chillies]] - deseeded\n| &#189; tablespoon [[Ghee|ghee]]\n| Pinch of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| Pinch of [[Sugar|sugar]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Peel and slice the [[Mangoes|mangoes]] into small slices or cubes (see [[Preparing a mango]])\n| Whip the [[Yogurt|yogurt]] and add the [[Salt|salt]] and [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| Remove the [[Coconut|coconut]] (see [[Preparing a coconut]])\n| In a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]], grind the [[Coconut|coconut]] and [[Chillies|chillies]] to a paste and add to the [[Yogurt|yogurt]]\n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]] until they pop\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Fry|fry]] for 5 minutes\n| Remove from the heat, allow to cool and stir in the [[Yogurt|yogurt]]\n| Mix well and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe at room temperature as a [[Side dish|side dish]] to an Indian banquet\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#yogurt #coconut #fry #sidedish #mangoes #ripemangoraita #ghee #mustardseeds #onion #chillies #preparingamango </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Roast duck roti",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Roast duck roti a spicy Indian rice pancake recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#nectarines #rice #limejuice #ghee #grill #coconutmilk #coconut #roastduckroti #ginger #chillipeppers #onions \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A hot and spicy South Indian rice cake with roast duck, coconut and nectarines\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4025\n|PortionCalories = 1006\n|DatePublished=29th June 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Roast duck spicy rice cake served with [[nectarines]]\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Roast duck with fruit roti.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">One of my favourite recipes</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Gorgeous, especially with the nectarines.  They cut through the fattiness of duck.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Murghi roti]] and its many variations are some of my favourite recipes, hot and spicy coconut rice with a crunchy chewy texture. That's why I keep trying new ways of varying it.  This time I used a large [[Sous vide hoisin duck breasts|Sous vide hoisin duck breast]] as the meat basis for this dish.\n\nBecause the dish is quite hot and spicy, it is very easy to lose the taste and even the texture of the duck if it is cut into small pieces. Thick slices are the way to go with this piquant South Indian style recipe. \n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 225 g (8 oz) uncooked [[basmati rice]].\n| 200 ml [[coconut milk]]\n| 1 x 160 g cooked [[Duck]] breast, sliced thickly - I used a leftover [[Sous vide hoisin duck breasts|Sous vide hoisin duck breast]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]] or vegetable [[Oil|oil]]\n| 5 [[Fat|fat]] [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 5 cm (2\") [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and roughly [[Grated|grated]]\n| 150 g (5 oz) [[Onions|onions]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 fresh [[coconut]], flesh removed and grated\n| 3 hot [[Chilli peppers|chilli peppers]] (red or green), finely chopped - de-seeded if desired\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n| 2 [[nectarines]], chopped\n| 1 [[nectarine]], sliced for garnish\n}}\n'''spices'''\n''The charm of this dish is the 'bite' of the whole spices, don't be tempted to grind them!''\n* 2 teaspoons whole [[coriander seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon whole [[cumin seeds]] (white)\n* 1/2 a teaspoon of whole [[fenugreek seeds]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Duck rice cake grilled side.jpg|Spicy duck rice cake after being grilled\nImage:Duck roti fried.jpg|Frying the rice cake - keep turning it so you get lots of crunchy surfaces\nImage:Duck roti rice puree.jpg|The rice cake mixture - it's quite moist\nImage:Sliced Duck roti rice cake.jpg|Next time I would cut the duck into thick slices\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Quickly wash and drain the [[rice]] but don't rinse it as you normally would, this dish is best with rice of a starchy consistency. \n| Cook in boiling water for 7 to 11 minutes.\n| Rinse the cooked rice in cold water until it is cold.  Drain well.\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade together with 200 ml of [[coconut milk]] and blend to a thick creamy pur\u00e9e.  Remember, the inside is not going to change much whilst being cooked and will remain at roughly the same consistency as it was when first mixed. If it looks too wet, leave it to rest for 30 minutes. A lot of the excess liquid will be absorbed into the rice.\n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a [[frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] all of the [[Spices|spices]] for half a minute, then add the [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and allow them to cook for a minute or so.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and reduce the heat a little and let them cook until translucent; about 5 minutes.\n| Slice the duck breast quite thickly and add to the onion mixture together with the 2 chopped [[nectarines]], the [[Coconut|coconut]] and [[Chilli|chilli]]. Mix well and remove from the heat.\n| Lightly [[Oil|oil]] a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] put on a gentle heat.\n| Mix the [[Rice|rice]] pur\u00e9e and duck together and tip this into the pan.\n| Ensure the mixture is evenly distributed and cook gently for about 10 minutes, stirring every few minutes so the crunchy base gets evenly distributed.\n| Preheat the [[Grill|grill]].\n| Oil a large oven tray and spread the cooked mixture evenly and [[Brown|brown]] under the hot [[Grill|grill]] until it gets a little crunchy.\n| Sprinkle with [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and serve immediately with sliced [[nectarines]].\n}}\n{{Template:SeeAlso Roti}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#nectarines #rice #limejuice #ghee #grill #coconutmilk #coconut #roastduckroti #ginger #chillipeppers #onions </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

The salt helps to remove a little of the moisture so firming the flesh\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1528\n|PortionCalories = 382\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 40 minutes plus 2 or more hours marinading\n|PrepTime = 10 minutes plus 2 or more hours marinading\n|CookTime = 30 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Rock salmon with garlic and coriander.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A faded memory</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I really don't remember making this, but the camera never lies. gas 4) after step 4\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Generously season the [[Rock salmon|rock salmon]] with [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| Drizzle the [[Citrus|citrus]] juice, [[Zest|zest]] and [[Nam pla|nam pla]] over the [[Fish|fish]]\n| Roll the [[Fish|fish]] in the marinade to ensure it's well coated\n| Refrigerate for an hour or two\n| In a pan, gently [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] in the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] until soft, about 4 minutes\n| Stir in the [[Chilli|chilli]] flakes, [[Ginger root|ginger root]] and any juice\n| [[Oil]] a small ovenproof dish and lay the [[Fish|fish]] in it together with the juices\n| Cover with the [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and then ladle the [[Onion|onion]] mixture over the top\n| [[Bake]] uncovered for 20 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot, with [[Lime|lime]] or [[Orange|orange]] [[Wedges|wedges]] and [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]].\n\n===Variations===\n\nUse [[basa]], [[ling]], [[Halibut|halibut]] or [[conger eel]] as an alternate fish for this dish\n\nHaving a fridge clean, I added a chopped [[sweet pepper]] and a few [[celery]] sticks at the same time as the [[onions]] and [[garlic]].\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#orange #fish #onion #rocksalmonwithgarlicandcoriander #garlic #lime #gingerroot #oliveoil #nampla #zest #chilli </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Roti",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Roti, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#roti #yogurt #foodprocessor #vegetableoil #griddled #grilled #barbecued #strongwhiteflour #wheatflour #ghee #frying \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Roti is the traditional Indian bread, normally eaten with curries or cooked vegetables\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1193\n|PortionCalories = 198\n|DatePublished=9th March 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 6 - Makes 6 roti\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 55 minutes\n |PrepTime = 40 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Roti recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A curry must-have.</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Great for dipping in curry sauce.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nRoti is the traditional Indian bread, normally eaten with [[curries]] or cooked vegetables. It is made most often from [[wheat flour]], cooked on a flat or slightly concave iron griddle called a [[tawa]]. It is similar to a [[tortilla]] in appearance. Like breads around the world, roti is a staple accompaniment to other foods, maybe spread with [[ghee]] (clarified butter) or [[yogurt]].\n\nWhilst kneading [[dough]] can be therapeutic, if time is your enemy, then the [[food processor]] is your friend.\n\nRoti are the perfect accompaniment to most Indian dishes.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 cup [[atta flour]] or [[strong white flour]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n| 2 tablespoons [[yogurt]] (optional)\n| &#189; cup water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Tip all of the ingredients and half of the water into the [[food processor]] with a plastic blade or dough hook attachment\n| Blitz the mixture whilst adding a more water a little at a time until you have a soft, pliable dough that is not too sticky\n| Remove from the processor, dust with a little [[flour]] and rest for 30 minutes in a bowl, covered with a damp tea-towel\n| Divide into 6 equal parts and roll into balls\n| With a rolling pin on a floured surface, roll each roti out into a 13cm (5\") disc, about the thickness of a small coin (penny, dime, nickel etc)\n| Without using any [[oil]], heat a [[tava]] or [[frying]] pan until very hot\n| Cook each roti for about 2 minutes a side until flecked with brown patches. They should puff up slightly.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nKeep warm whilst the remaining rotis are are cooked.\n{{Template:SeeAlso Roti}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Roti]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Roti]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Roti]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Roti]]\n[[Category:Starters|Roti]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Roti]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#roti #yogurt #foodprocessor #vegetableoil #griddled #grilled #barbecued #strongwhiteflour #wheatflour #ghee #frying </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

title": "Sambar dhal",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sambar dhal, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#sambardhal #lentils #garlic #mustardseeds #tomatoes #turmeric #simmer #corianderleaves #onions #scant #poppadoms \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Sambar dhal (sambar dal), (sanber daal is a lentil stew or chowder\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1369\n|PortionCalories = 342\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment=Sambar dal, [[naan bread|nan]], [[plain rice|rice]] and [[yogurt]]\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 40 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Sambar dhal recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">My favourite pitta dip</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is great to dip flatbreads in.  I prefer home-made pittas with this.  Leave some of the spices whole, it makes it taste truly authentic.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n[[Image:Sambar dhal ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Sambar dhal, the ingredients]]\n\nSambar dhal (sambar [[Dal|dal]]), (sanber daal is a [[Lentil|lentil]] [[Stew|stew]] or [[Chowder|chowder]]. It is very popular in the cooking of southern regions of [[India]] especially in Tamil Nadu, Kerala, Karnataka and Andhra Pradesh.\n\nA nice [[Vegetarian|vegetarian]] [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] or even a main dish if served with [[Pillau rice|pillau rice]] and [[poppadoms]] or [[Nan breads|nan breads]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 250 g (8 oz) [[Red lentils|red lentils]]\n| 850 ml (1.5 pints) water or [[vegetable stock]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 4 [[Green chillies|green chillies]], sliced lengthways\n| 1 tablespoon chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]]\n| 250 g (8 oz) [[Aubergine|aubergine]], cut into strips\n| 240 g (8 oz) can of peeled [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] or [[ghee]]\n| 2 [[Onions|onions]], peeled and chopped\n| 4 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed (or to taste)\n| 2 cm (1 \") [[Ginger root|ginger root]], peeled and [[Grated|grated]] - Try [[Home-made lazy ginger|homemade lazy ginger]] instead.\n| 1 teaspoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]] [[Ground|ground]] to a powder\n| 1 teaspoon white [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon black [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 [[scant]] teaspoon [[jaggery]] or [[sugar]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rinse the [[Lentils|lentils]], place in a large pan, cover with cold water and bring to the [[Boil|boil]], then [[Simmer|simmer]] for 10 minutes.\n| Add the [[Turmeric|turmeric]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and [[turmeric]] powder, [[Aubergines|aubergines]] and [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Juice|juice]], salt & sugar.  Cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 30 minutes or until the [[Lentils|lentils]] are very soft.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a small pan. Saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] for 4 minutes or until soft and golden.\n| Add the [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]] and [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]] and [[Fry|fry]] for 2 minutes.\n| Stir the onion mix into the [[Lentils|lentils]] and serve.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nI like to powder half of the spices and very roughly grind the remaining half to get a coarse spice mix that holds little taste-bursts when you get them.\n==See also==\n* [[Dal|A selection of other Daal recipes]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sambardhal #lentils #garlic #mustardseeds #tomatoes #turmeric #simmer #corianderleaves #onions #scant #poppadoms </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

2\n|TotalTime = 1 hour\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 45 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Sardine curry puffs recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Fishy puffs</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Dinky mini fish pasties</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nA far more interesting version of the curry pasties sometimes found in our fish and chip shops.\n\n'''For the [[Curry paste|curry paste]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 fresh [[Bay|bay]] leaf\n| 2 whole [[Clove|clove]] buds\n| &#189; teaspoon cardomom seeds (green or black), removed from pods\n| 1 tablespoon [[Coriander|coriander]] seed\n| 2 teaspoons white [[Cumin|cumin]] seeds\n| 1 teaspoon ground [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| 4 small hot [[Dried|dried]] [[Chillies|chillies]]\n| 2 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 2 tablespoons [[Malt|malt]] [[Vinegar|vinegar]]\n}}\n'''For the curry puffs'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 3 tablespoons [[Vegetable|vegetable]] [[Oil|oil]]\n| 1 small [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 1 can [[Sardines|sardines]] in [[Oil|oil]], drained\n| Juice of 1 [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| 1 teaspoon sea [[Salt|salt]]\n|* 1 500g (1 lb 2 oz) packet of [[Puff pastry|puff pastry]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - Gas 5)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a small pan, dry roast the [[Bay|bay]] leaf, [[Cloves|cloves]], cardomom seeds, [[Coriander|coriander]] seeds until the [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]] starts to [[Brown|brown]], allow them to cool a little.\n| Add all of the [[Curry paste|curry paste]] ingredients to the [[Grinding|grinding]] attachment of a [[Food processor|food processor]] and blend to a paste.\n| [[Fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] in the [[Oil|oil]] until softened, about 4 minutes.\n| Add the [[Curry paste|curry paste]] and sizzle [[Fry|fry]] it for at least 3 minutes, stirring all the while.\n| Add 6 fl oz of [[Boiling|boiling]] water and cook until the [[Sauce|sauce]] thickens, about 10 minutes.\n| Add the [[Sardines|sardines]] and fold them into the [[Sauce|sauce]] to ensure they are coated, but don't let them break up.\n| Drizzle with the [[Lemon|lemon]] juice, sprinkle with [[Salt|salt]], stir gently to mix and leave for 1 hour to marinade.\n| Roll the [[Puff pastry|puff pastry]] out to 2.5 mm (1/8\") thick and cut into 13 cm (5\") rounds.\n| Preheat the oven to 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - Gas 5)  \n| Distribute the curried [[Fish|fish]] evenly between the rounds, [[Brush|brush]] the edges with the beaten [[Egg|egg]] and crimp to seal.\n| [[Brush]] the puffs with the remaining beaten [[Egg|egg]].\n| [[Bake]] for 25 minutes so the pastry is risen and [[Brown|brown]].\n}}\n===Chef's tip===\n\nIf the pastry browns before it has properly risen, lay a piece of [[tin-foil]] loosely over the puffs.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy It could be made entirely with prawns but in this version I'm using a mixture of [[king prawns]] and [[cod fillet]]. Any white fish would do.\n\nThis is a fairly quick [[Curry|curry]], nice and creamy with lots of [[Coconut|coconut]] flavours.  As with all authentic [[Indian curries]] there are lots of whole [[Spices|spices]] that you are not supposed to eat.  Pick them out as you eat. You'll get a surprise if you bite down on a [[Cardamom|cardamom]] pod or a [[Clove|clove]]!\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 250g [8.5oz] mixture of large [[Prawns|prawns]] and any [[white fish]] cut into [[Coconut|coconut]] cut from a block\n| A tablespoon of [[dessicated coconut]]\n| 2 [[Indian green chillies]] [[Split|split]] lengthwise and deseeded\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add the [[Seafood|seafood]] pieces to a [[Lock & Lock box]] together with the [[Turmeric|turmeric]] and [[Salt|salt]], close the ld and shake gently to coat evenly\n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a [[Wok|wok]] or [[Frying pan|frying pan]], not too hot or you'll have a kitchen full of smoke\n| [[Stir-fry]] the [[Seafood|seafood]] for a few minutes turning often\n| Remove the cooked [[Seafood|seafood]], place in a clean bowl and set to one side\n| On a low heat in the same pan add all the [[Spices|spices]] apart from the [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for 2 or 3 minutes so the [[Ghee|ghee]] is nicely flavoured\n| Pour in the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] and add the [[Coconut block|coconut block]], cook for another few minutes\n| Add the [[Prawns|prawns]] and [[Chillies|chillies]], bring to a simmer then cook gently cook for 10 minutes\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Seafood malai curry ingredients.jpg|thumb|right|300px|The title": "Simple slow cooker fruity pork curry",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Simple slow cooker fruity pork curry\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#slowcooker #simpleslowcookerfruityporkcurry #porkfillet #ghee #fry #curry #leeks #rice #juice #leek #naanbreads #slowcooker\n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=I thought I would make a nice simple fruity pork curry and cook it in the Slow Cooker\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=30th December 2022\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  2 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  5 minutes\n|CookTime =  2 hours, 10 minutes\n|TotalCalories = 1015\n|PortionCalories = 507\n|Image = [[Image:Simple slow cooker fruity pork curry recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice way of using leeks</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.2</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Also made a decent curry - thanks!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nI thought I would make a nice simple fruity [[Curry|curry]] and cook it in the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]]; feeling lazy!\n\nOur [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] is neat as it also has the ability to [[Fry|fry]] so the [[Pork|pork]] and [[Leeks|leeks]] can be [[Fried|fried]] off in the [[Slow cooker|slow cooker]] first.  If your slow [[Cooker|cooker]] cannot fry then either start the [[Frying|frying]] in a [[Frying pan|frying pan]], of just  ignore the frying, it won't make a massive difference.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| A pinch of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 large [[Leek|leek]], cleaned, cut in half lengthwise and then chopped into 'rings'.\n| 1 [[Pork fillet|pork fillet]]\n| 4 [[Cloves of garlic|cloves of garlic]], peeled and chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Ghee|ghee]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| \u00bd teaspoon [[Mixed herbs|mixed herbs]]\n| 300ml [[Orange]] and [[Mango]] [[Juice|juice]]\n| 1 heaped tablespoon of [[Curry powder|curry powder]]\n| 3 tablespoons of [[Sultanas|sultanas]]\n| 6 soft [[Apricots|apricots]], cut into quarters\n| 1 stick of [[Rhubarb|rhubarb]], chopped - I've used some that was [[Frozen|frozen]] from the summer\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add the [[Black pepper|black pepper]], [[Oil|oil]] and [[Ghee|ghee]] to your [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]], set to [[Hob|hob]]-mode (or [[Frying pan|frying pan]])\n| [[Fry]] the [[Pork fillet|pork fillet]] for 5 minutes, turning now and then\n| Add the [[Leeks|leeks]] and [[Fry|fry]] for another 5 minutes, adding the chopped [[Garlic|garlic]] for the last minute or so\n| Set the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] to high slow-cook\n| Add the remaining ingredients, mix very well and and cook for 2 hours, stirring now and then if you are able\n| Slice the [[Pork fillet|pork fillet]] and serve with [[Side dishes|side dishes]] of your chosing\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Simple slow cooker fruity pork curry.jpg|Simple slow cooker fruity pork curry; the basic ingredients\nImage:Simple slow cooker fruity pork curry after one hour.jpg|Pork curry after one hour in the slow cooker\nImage:Slow cooked pork fillet carved for curry.jpg|Slow cooked pork fillet carved and ready for the curry sauce\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nWe've chosen a [[Vegetable|vegetable]] [[Rice|rice]] and [[Naan breads|naan breads]], sprinkled with [[Coconut Merchant Toasted Coconut Chips]].\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you don't have [[Ghee|ghee]], just double the amount of [[Oil|oil]]. Normal [[Orange juice|orange juice]] will be fine too.\n===Variations===\nMaking a slightly different version of this tonight so making notes in case it's a keeper.\n\nLargely similar, the main differences being:\n* Smaller [[pork fillet]]\n* One large [[onion]] and one [[leek]]\n* A few trimmed chunks off-cuts from [[Treacle Cured Bacon from Russell's of Upwell's]]\n* Two large [[portobello mushrooms]]\n* 400 ml [[grape juice]] instead of 300ml [[Orange]] and [[Mango]] [[Juice|juice]]\n* More of both curry powders and a teaspoon of hot chilli powder\n* A teaspoon of mixed [[cardamom pods]]\n* Half a [[coconut block]] - '''only need a quarter in future'''\n\nThis was nice but it was much too hot for Anne, sorry.  Only use 1 tbs of curry powder and very little chilli powder in future. \ud83d\ude13\n===Chef's noters===\nI've mixed my [[Curry|curry]] powder [[Blend|blend]] and [[Taste Sensation Kashmiri Curry Powder]], together with \u00bd teaspoon of [[Turmeric|turmeric]] and a pinch of [[Fenugreek|fenugreek]]; I like to fiddle with my [[Spices|spices]]!\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n[[Category:Taste Sensation recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#slowcooker #simpleslowcookerfruityporkcurry #porkfillet #ghee #fry #curry #leeks #rice #juice #leek #naanbreads</code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

1055\n|PortionCalories = 527\n|DatePublished=13th April 2013\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2-4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  50 minutes\n|PrepTime =  20 minutes\n|CookTime =  30 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Smoked haddock pilaf recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nicer than kedgeree</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Fabulous recipe Rosemary - having this again next week - thanks! x</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis dish is very similar to [[Kedgeree|kedgeree]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 40g [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]]\n| 1 [[Scotch bonnet|scotch bonnet]] [[Chilli|chilli]], chopped\n| [[Garlic]], to taste, chopped\n| 1 small piece [[Fresh ginger|fresh ginger]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 2 teaspoons [[Pakistani basar]]\n| 250g [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]]\n| 1 [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 375ml [[Fish stock|fish stock]]\n| 400g un-dyed [[Smoked haddock|smoked haddock]] fillet, boned, skin on, cut into 4 equal portions\n| 2 free-range [[Eggs, hard-boiled|eggs, hard-boiled]], peeled, [[Grated|grated]]\n| 2 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], trimmed, finely sliced\n| Fresh [[Coriander|coriander]], to taste, chopped\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 180\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large, heavy-based saucepan.\n| Add the [[Chilli|chilli]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Ginger|ginger]] and saut\u00e9 for a minute or two. \n| Add the [[Pakistani basar]] and cook for a further few seconds, stirring constantly.\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] and stir until it is well coated with the [[Oil|oil]].\n| Add the [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]], and the seasoning. \n| Pour over the [[Stock|stock]], bring to a [[Simmer|simmer]], and remove from the heat.\n| Tip the [[Rice|rice]] mixture into a [[Casserole dish|casserole dish]].\n| Arrange the [[Fish|fish]] on the top, pushing it slightly under the surface.\n| Cover and cook for 20-25 minutes.\n| Remove from the [[Oven|oven]], then leave to stand for 5-7 minutes without removing the lid.\n| Take off the lid, remove the skin from the [[Fish|fish]] and immediately add the [[Grated|grated]] [[Egg|egg]], spring  [[Onions|onions]] and [[Coriander|coriander]].\n| Using two forks, gently mix the [[Rice|rice]], while also breaking the [[Fish|fish]] into flakes and mixing everything else in as you go. \n| Remove the [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]] and cover with a [[Tea towel|tea towel]], and the lid. \n| Leave for a further 5 minutes to remove any excess [[Steam|steam]]. \n| Mix again lightly and serve directly from the dish onto hot plates.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Salad|salad]] or [[Vegetables|vegetables]].\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Adapted from a recipe by '''[http://www.bbc.co.uk/food/recipes/smoked_haddock_pilaf_84768 Simon Hopkinson]'''\n\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Haddock pilaf]]\n[[Category:British recipes|Haddock pilaf]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Haddock You could cook from frozen; just add an extra 30 minutes cooking time for the defrosting to occur in the sous-vide cooker.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide cooking]]\n{{Template:Sous Vide, Smoking and Curing UK}}\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#currysauce #rib #frozen #vacuumseal #spicyrecipes #britishrecipes #sousviderecipes #meatrecipes #sousvideribeyesteakcurry #curry #beefrecipes</code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Spiced salt recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#dried #celery #spicedsalt #blender #vegetables #thermomix #chives #spice #dehydrator #coffee #grinding \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe is to make a basic spiced salt.\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=9th June 2017\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 8 - Makes about 750g\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  5 minutes (plus dehydrating time)\n|PrepTime =  5 minutes (plus dehydrating time)\n|CookTime = None\n|TotalCalories = 25\n|PortionCalories = 25 \n|Image = [[Image:Spiced salt recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Keeps for ages</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Easy to make and it keeps for ages as long as you keep it dry</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe is to make a basic [[Spice|spice]]d [[Salt|salt]].  You can play around with your own combination of ingredients - just make sure that they are absolutely [[Dried|dried]] out before use, or they could go mouldy.  This can be made in a [[Thermomix]], a good [[Blender|blender]] or a [[Coffee|coffee]]/[[spice]] grinder.\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n| 65g [[Dried|dried]] [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and [[Herbs|herbs]] (see [[Chef's notes|chef's notes]] below)\n| 6 large [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 50g [[Dried|dried]] [[Bird's Eye chillies|bird's eye chillies]] (or others of your choice)\n| 40g [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]]\n| 20g [https://www.amazon.co.uk/Engevita-Savoury-Yeast-Condiment-Pack/dp/B00A4C48LQ/ref=pd_lpo_vtph_543_bs_tr_t_2?_encoding=UTF8&psc=1&refRID=7T45S5NDXR6ZXEHKTMM6 Engevita Yeast Flakes]\n| 600g [[Salt|salt]] of your choice - I used [[Salt#Himalayan Pink Rock Salt|Pink Himalayan Rock Salt]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| If using a [[Thermomix]], place all of the ingredients into the bowl and grind '''30 secs/ Speed 6-8-10'''.\n| If using a normal [[Blender|blender]] or [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]], I would suggest [[Grinding|grinding]] it in smaller batches and the mixing together at the end.\n| Whichever method you use, just grind until you are happy with the texture - I like mine to be a little coarse\n| Transfer to clean [[Glass|glass]] jars or [[Lock&Lock boxes]] and if kept dry, it will keep for at least 18 months.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Adapted from a recipe in '''Fast and Easy Indian Cooking''' (Thermomix UK)\n===Chef's notes===\nFor the [[Dehydrated|dehydrated]] [[Vegetables|vegetables]], I used the following ingredients:\n\n*750g [[Celery|celery]]\n\n*2 medium [[Red onions|red onions]]\n\n*Several [[Clove|clove]] of [[Garlic|garlic]]\n\n*A few [[Chives|chives]]\n\nand [[Dried|dried]] them in a [[Dehydrator|dehydrator]].\n\nIf you don't have a [[Dehydrator|dehydrator]], you can buy [[Dried|dried]] [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic granules|garlic granules]] and [[Chives|chives]], but you will need to dry the [[Celery|celery]] in the [[Oven|oven]].  To do this, slice the [[celery]] as thinly as you can and spread out on [[Baking trays|baking trays]] - the [[celery]] pieces can be close, but shouldn't be touching.  Put your [[oven]] on to its lowest setting and place the trays inside. Leave until totally shrivelled and dried.  This could take several hours, so do it on a day when you won't want the oven for anything else.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Salt spiced]]\n[[Category:British recipes|Salt spiced]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Salt spiced]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Salt spiced]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes|Salt spiced]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Salt spiced]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Salt spiced]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Salt spiced]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Salt spiced]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes|Salt spiced]]\n[[Category:Dehydrated|Salt spiced]]\n[[Category:Uncooked|Salt spiced]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#dried #celery #spicedsalt #blender #vegetables #thermomix #chives #spice #dehydrator #coffee #grinding </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Spicy basa fish fillets with pineapple",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Spicy basa fish fillets with pineapple an Indian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#fish #mustardoil #pineapple #chillipowder #turmeric #fennelseeds #fry #ginger #curryleaves #bayleaves #simmer \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I have adapted this West Bengal fish recipe to use basa. It can be made with any similar firm fish fillets such as haddock, pollock or mackerel\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1517\n|PortionCalories = 379\n|DatePublished=13th November 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Served with plain rice and naan bread\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 25 minutes\n|PrepTime =  1 hour\n|CookTime =  25 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Basa fish fillets with pineapple recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Basa is The Best</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A great recipe and basa is better tasting than cod and less than half the price.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nI have adapted this West Bengal fish recipe to use [[basa]].  It can be made with any similar firm [[Fish|fish]] fillets such as [[Haddock|haddock]], [[pollock]] or [[Mackerel|mackerel]].  I halved the amount of oil used in the original recipe, however, you can see from the frying picture, the dish is still quite oily.\n\nWhen I first tasted this dish I wasn't sure about it as it is a little unusual, by the end though I wanted more and it's been requested again for next week!\n\nAuthentic dishes like this are served together with all of the leaves and whole spices.  It is for the diner to either eat or remove the spices from the plate.  It's quite fun and once you get used to it you won't ever bother picking all the spices out before serving.\n\nThe original recipe: [[Illich maachh annanas]] ([[Hilsa]] (''shad'') with [[Pineapple|pineapple]]) is from Mr Pushpash Pent's wonderful \"[[India]]\" recipe book:  ISBN 978-0714859026, a worthy addition to any cook's bookshelf.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 600 g (1lb 5 oz) [[Basa fillets|basa fillets]]\n| 1.5 teaspoons of [[Ground|ground]] [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| 1 thumb-sized piece of fresh peeled [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Grated|grated]].  I now use my [[Home made lazy ginger|home made lazy ginger]] for recipes like this\n| 1 tablespoon of whole [[Fennel seeds|fennel seeds]]\n| 75ml [[Mustard oil|mustard oil]]\n| 4 [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]] or 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 2 whole [[Cloves|cloves]]\n| 4 [[Green cardamom pods|green cardamom pods]]\n| 1 [[Stick of cinnamon|stick of cinnamon]] about 2.5 cm (1 inch) long\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 6 slices of drained canned [[Pineapple|pineapple]], chopped\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Lock and lock cheat.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The easy way to coat the fish - see Chef's notes\nImage:Frying the fish curry.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Frying the fish (qty: 2 people)\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Cut the fillets into even sized pieces\n| Place in a shallow dish and rub with the [[Turmeric|turmeric]] and a few pinches of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| Pop in the [[Fridge|fridge]] and leave for 40 minutes to [[Marinade|marinade]].  It won't hurt if it's left for longer\n| In a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]], make a paste with the [[Grated|grated]] [[Ginger|ginger]]. Add a little water (or the [[Vinegar|vinegar]] from the [[Lazy ginger|lazy ginger]]) if it needs a thinning a little\n| Add half of the [[Seeds|seeds]] and pound to a paste (or use a [[Spice|spice]]/[[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]\n| In a [[Wok|wok]] or [[Frying pan|frying pan]], heat a few tablespoons of the [[Mustard oil|mustard oil]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Fish|fish]] pieces for about a minute a side. Do this in small batches, removing the cooked [[Fish|fish]] and keep to one side while the [[Rest|rest]] is being cooked\n| In the same pan, with all of the [[Fish|fish]] removed, heat the remaining [[Mustard oil|mustard oil]], the [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]] or [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]], [[Cloves|cloves]], [[Cardamom pods|cardamom pods]], [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]] and the remaining whole [[Fennel seeds|fennel seeds]]\n| [[Stir-fry]] these for a few minutes\n| Add the [[Ginger paste|ginger paste]] and the [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for another 3 minutes, stirring now and then\n| Put in chopped [[Pineapple|pineapple]] and season with a pinch of [[Salt|salt]] then add 125 ml (4,5 fl oz) of water, bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 5 minutes\n| Add the [[Fish|fish]] pieces, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for a further 15 minutes. Shimmy the now and then to ensure the fish does not stick.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]].\n===Chef's notes===\nA really quick way to coat the fish evenly with [[salt]] and [[turmeric]] is to add them to a [[Lock & Lock]]-style box together with the fish.  Close the lid and shake well.  As you can see from the photograph it gives the fish really good even covering.  It is similar to Jamie Oliver's 'plastic bag' method - only better!\n\nInstead of mustard oil, a - At a push you could use [[Olive oil|olive oil]] / [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] and [[Fry|fry]] a tablespoon of [[Black mustard seeds|black mustard seeds]] in the [[Oil|oil]], then use as [[Mustard oil|mustard oil]]t a push you could use [[Olive oil|olive oil]] / [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] and [[Fry|fry]] a tablespoon of [[Black mustard seeds|black mustard seeds]] in the [[Oil|oil]], then use as [[Mustard oil|mustard oil]]\n\nAlthough not authentic for an Indian recipe, I used 1 teaspoon of [[chipotole]] [[chilli powder]] which is quite hot (7/10 [[Scoville heat scale]]).  It was spicy but bearable for others who may not be used to hotter curries.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fish #mustardoil #pineapple #chillipowder #turmeric #fennelseeds #fry #ginger #curryleaves #bayleaves #simmer </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
