Basa is an excellent firm and flavoursome\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 769\n|PortionCalories = 192\n|DatePublished=16th November 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Spicy battered fish balls with [[pillau rice]]\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 55 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Spicy battered fish balls on skewers recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Barbecued batter?</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.53</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">That's a new one on me - better than frying though</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nThis is a recipe that I have adapted from Pat Chapman's \"Kinga Nishat\" recipe - ''Skewered spicy [[Batter|batter]] [[Prawns|prawns]]''.\n\n[[Basa]] is an excellent firm and flavoursome [[Fish|fish]] that is also sustainable.  It is a good substitute for [[Prawns|prawns]].\n\nWhen I made this with [[masa harina]] it did not stick well to the fish, however it was really tasty so it will be made again, with the proper ingredients next time.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 packs [[Basa|basa]] fillets (about 650 g)\n| 4 tablespoons freshly squeezed [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 1 tablespoon freshly Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| 1 tablespoon freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Root ginger|root ginger]]\n| 2 [[Eggs|eggs]] - beaten\n| 4 tablespoons [[Single cream|single cream]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Gram flour|gram flour]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Lovage seeds|lovage seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[turmeric]]\n| &#189; teaspoon fine [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cut the [[Basa|basa]] fillets into skewerable chunks - you may need to fold the basa as you skewer it if it's very thin.\n| Add the [[Basa|basa]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] to a [[Lock and Lock box|lock and lock box]], close, shake well and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 30 minutes or so to [[Marinade|marinade]].\n| Whisk the egg in another bowl and add the remaining ingredients.  The consistency should be like [[double cream]]. Adjust by adding more flour or cream.\n| Pour the egg mixture into the [[Lock and Lock box]], close and shake like mad.\n| [[Refrigerate]] for a further 15 minutes.\n| Skewer the [[Basa|basa]] and [[Barbecue|barbecue]] for 10 to 15 minutes or alternatively, shallow [[Fry|fry]] in [[Ghee|ghee]] or [[Butter|butter]] and skewer before serving.\n}}\n===Variations===\nTry this with large [[King prawns|king prawns]], [[Scampi|scampi]] or [[Crayfish|crayfish]].\n===Chef's notes===\nWhen I came to make this i discovered that I had run out of [[gram flour]].  I made it with [[masa harina]] and a little [[plain flour]] to get to the consistency of [[double cream]].\n[[Plain flour]] or [[self raising flour]] would be just as good if you did not have [[gram flour]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#basa #gramflour #spicybatteredfishballsonskewers #lemonjuice #masaharina #plainflour #doublecream #prawns #refrigerate #garlic #griddled </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Spicy battered fish fillets, Indian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#basa #spicybatteredfishfillets #refrigerate #garlic #lemonjuice #marinade #frying #singlecream #egg #rootginger #grated \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I recently made Spicy battered fish balls on skewers in which I used basa to adapt Pat Chapman's \"Kinga Nishat\" recipe from 250 Favourite Curries and\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 388\n|PortionCalories = 97\n|DatePublished=23rd October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment =\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 55 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Spicy battered fish fillets.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Wow - Yummilicious!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I love basa!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nI recently made [[Spicy battered fish balls on skewers]]]] in which I used [[basa]] to adapt Pat Chapman's \"Kinga Nishat\" recipe from 250 Favourite Curries and Accompaniments - 1992.  ISBN 0-7499-1185-9.  It was incredibly tasty but on reflection, cutting the [[basa]] into small chunks, [[frying]] separately and then placing on skewers seemed rather involved and pointless.\n\nThis time I used the spicy batter to coat the whole fillets and then shallow fried them.  The result was fantastic, the batter sticking really well to the fish.  Do try this, it is a rather special recipe!\n\n[[Basa]] is an excellent firm and flavoursome [[Fish|fish]] that is also sustainable.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 packs [[Basa|basa]] fillets (about 320 g) [\u00a32.00 Morrisons - May 2011]\n| 2 tablespoons freshly squeezed [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 1 tablespoon freshly Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| 1 tablespoon freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Root ginger|root ginger]]\n| 1 [[egg]] - beaten\n| 2 tablespoons [[Single cream|single cream]], [[sour cream]], [[yogurt]] or even [[milk]]\n| 1.5 tablespoons of [[Gram flour|gram flour]]\n| 1 teaspoon of whole [[Lovage seeds|lovage seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon of whole [[fennel seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[turmeric]]\n| &#189; teaspoon fine [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Basa|basa]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] to a [[Lock and Lock box|lock and lock box]], close, shake well and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 30 minutes or so to [[Marinade|marinade]].\n| Whisk the egg in another bowl and add the remaining ingredients, whisk to the consistency of thickish [[double cream]]. Adjust by adding more flour or cream.\n| Pour the egg mixture into the [[Lock and Lock box]], close and shake like mad.\n| [[Refrigerate]] for a further 15 minutes or until you are ready to use it.\n| Shallow [[Fry|fry]] in [[Ghee|ghee]], [[Butter|butter]] or [[olive oil]] until the batter is golden and the fish is cooked.  Try not to disturb it too much or the batter will come away from the fish.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#basa #spicybatteredfishfillets #refrigerate #garlic #lemonjuice #marinade #frying #singlecream #egg #rootginger #grated </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This would last 2 people a couple of days if you keep the dressing and [[Spices|spices]] in a [[Air-tight container|airtight containers]] and only cut the [[Vegetable|vegetables]] up when ready to use them.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 4 [[Chicken breast|chicken breast]] fillets cut into thin slices\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Olive oil|olive oil]] to [[Fry|fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces\n}}\n'''[[Chicken|chicken]] [[Marinade|marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 4 [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n}}\n'''[[Salad|salad]] items'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| &#189; This stops the bits going everywhere. Then roast the crushed remains, every part gets nicely toasted this way.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#spicychickensalad #chicken #salad #jaggery #oliveoil #cashews #marinade #lockandlock #chickenbreast #springonions #favouriterecipes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

However, once cooked it just imparts a warm flavour, nothing like the smell of a Gym!\n\nThis needs to be prepared a day in advance for the [[Marinade|marinade]] to penetrate the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n}}\n'''cooking the [[Chicken|chicken]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1.6 kg (3.5 lb) [[Chicken drumsticks|chicken drumsticks]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Sunflower oil|sunflower oil]]\n| A grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 400ml can [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| 4 large [[Green chillies|green chillies]] de-seeded and finely chopped into rings\n}}\n'''the [[Marinade|marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 1 [[Scant|scant]] tablespoon [[Cardamom pods|cardamom pods]] in their shells ([[Brown|brown]] and/or green)\n| 1 tablespoon [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Ginger root|ginger root]], peeled and [[Grated|grated]] (use any [[Juice|juice]] too!)\n| 2 [[Green Indian chillies|green indian chillies]], deseeded and thinly sliced\n| 1 teaspoon freshly [[Ground cumin seeds|ground cumin seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon freshly [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]] seeds\n| 80 ml plain [[Natural yogurt|natural yogurt]]\n| [[Zest]] and [[Juice|juice]] of one [[Lime|lime]]\n}}\n'''to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]]\n| 20 ml [[Yogurt|yogurt]] drizzled over the dish\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chicken marinade.jpg|thumb|300px|right|After 30 seconds of shaking!\nImage:Chicken marinade ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Marinade ingredients, ready to mix.\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Remove the skin from the [[Chicken drumsticks|chicken drumsticks]].\n| Cut 3 or 4 deep slashes, right down to the bone of the [[Drumsticks|drumsticks]] so the [[Marinade|marinade]] can penetrate the flesh.\n| Add the [[Chicken drumsticks|chicken drumsticks]] to a large [[Lock and Lock box]].\n| Using a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]], crush the shells of the [[Cardamom pods|cardamom pods]] to release the [[Seeds|seeds]].  Discard the shells.\n| Crush the [[Cardamom seeds|cardamom seeds]] in the [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] and add to the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces.\n| Add the remaining [[Marinade|marinade]] ingredients to the [[Lock and Lock box|lock and lock box]], close the lid and shake violently for 30 seconds.  That's the mixing done!\n| Leave in a cool place overnight to [[Marinate|marinate]], shaking now and then.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] or large pan and add a good grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| Remove the [[Chicken|chicken]] and set the [[Marinade|marinade]] to one side.\n| Gently [[Brown|brown]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] all over.\n| Add the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] and the reserve [[Marinade|marinade]] and ring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| [[Simmer]] for 35 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and a drizzle of [[Yogurt|yogurt]], accompanied by [[Plain rice|plain rice]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#marinade #chicken #chickendrumsticks #spicychickenwithcoconutandcardamom #coconutmilk #cardamompods #corianderleaves #pestleandmortar #blackpepper #juice #yogurt </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Cover (with foil or clingfilm) and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 30 minutes or longer.\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - gas 5)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Line a [[Grill|grill]] rack with [[Foil|foil]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 30 to 35 minutes until golden [[Brown|brown]] and cooked through.\n}}\n''For the '[[Fried]] [[Rice|rice]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onion|onion]] for 4 minutes\n| Add the [[Rice and peas|rice and peas]] then [[Stir fry|stir fry]] for 3 to 4 minutes until the [[Rice|rice]] is properly reheated.\n| Serve immediately.\n}}\n===Variations===\nThe chicken pieces could be cooked on a [[Barbecue|barbecue]] just as easily. Turn them often.\n==See also==\n* [[Chicken tikka]]\n* [[Chicken tikka (cheat)]]\n* [[Chicken tikka masala]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinaded]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #rice #ginger #chickentikka #onion #garlic #spicychickenwithfriedrice #fried #barbecue #chillipowder #marinate </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It is particularly suitable for firm [[white fish]].\n\nNote: a part of this recipe ideally needs to be prepared the day before (although 1 hour marinating is adequate if you are pushed for time)\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 675g (1.5 lb) firm [[white fish]]; ([[Basa|basa]], [[Hoki|hoki]], [[Cod|cod]], [[Halibut|halibut]], [[Bream|bream]], [[Bass|bass]]) - [[bones]] removed and cut into bite-sized chunks\n| 2 medium [[Onions|onions]], peeled, one finely chopped, one sliced\n| 3 cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 2.5 cm (1\") peeled [[Root ginger|root ginger]], [[Grated|grated]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 3 [[Dried|dried]] [[Red chillies|red chillies]] (reduce amount if necessary to your taste) - crushed\n| 500 ml (1 large pot) plain natural [[Yoghurt|yogurt]] - the acidic type, not Greek-style\n| 1 teaspoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]\n| Good pinch of [[Salt|salt]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n}}\n'''To garnish'''\n* Freshly chopped [[Coriander|coriander]], [[parsley]] or [[basil leaves]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]], pound the finely chopped [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Spices|spices]] so you have a smooth paste.\n| Add the [[Spice|spice]] mix to a large bowl, add the [[Yogurt|yogurt]] and mix well to combine.\n| Add the [[Fish|fish]] to this mixture and coat well.  [[Refrigerate|Refrigerate]] for at least 1 hour so the flavours infuse.  Marinate overnight if possible.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] and [[Ghee|ghee]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and gently [[Fry|fry]] the chopped [[Onions|onions]] until just coloured - about 5 minutes.\n| Reduce the heat, add the [[Fish|fish]] and all of the [[Marinade|marinade]] and cook on a gentle heat for 15 minutes.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Spicy fish in yoghurt simmering.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Simmering in the wok\nImage:Spicy fish cooked in yoghurt recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Basa fillets marinading\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nArrange in a large serving bowl and dress with the chopped [[Herbs|herbs]] - serve with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]] \n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#spices #fish #ghee #garlic #onions #spicyfishcookedinyogurt #whitefish #yogurt #grated #basilleaves #basa </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Spicy mango chicken",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Spicy mango chicken, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #spicymangochicken #lemon #nutmeg #chickenstock #mango #ghee #mangoes #onions #turmeric #wok \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=If you've not tried cooking with mangoes, this is a great dish to start with. Ideally they should feel slightly soft when gently squeezed\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3073\n|PortionCalories = 768\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Fresh mangoes\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 50 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 1 hour 35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Spicy mango chicken.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Mine looked better than yours \ud83d\ude3c</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Though without your recipe, I couldn't have made it at all!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nIf you've not tried cooking with mangoes, this is a great dish to start with.  Ideally they should feel slightly soft when gently squeezed.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 3 [[tablespoons]] [[ghee]]\n| 900g (2 lbs) [[chicken]] pieces, skinned\n| 2 large [[onions]], peeled and sliced\n| 2 [[garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 2 large [[mangoes]], peeled and roughly chopped, keep &#189; of one [[mango]] sliced neatly for a garnish\n| &#188; teaspoon grated [[nutmeg]]\n| &#188; teaspoon [[ground black pepper]]\n| 1 level teaspoon [[sea salt]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n| Zest of &#189; [[lemon]]\n| 225ml (8 fl oz) [[chicken stock]]\n| 115ml (4 fl oz) [[single cream]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[ghee]] in a large pan or [[wok]] and brown the [[chicken]] pieces a few at a time and reserve.  Take care as ghee tends to smoke and burn easily\n| Add the [[onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[stir-fry]] for 5 minutes or until soft and translucent\n| Add the chopped [[mangoes]], [[nutmeg]], [[black pepper]], [[sea salt]], [[turmeric]] and [[lemon]] zest\n| Stir-fry for a few more minutes and add the [[chicken stock]]\n| Cover the pan and simmer gently for 45 minutes so the [[chicken]] is tender\n| Remove the [[chicken]] and keep warm in a casserole dish in a slow oven. [150\u00b0C, 300\u00b0F,Gas Mk 2] \n| Reduce the sauce to about half and then add the [[lemon]] juice and [[cream]]. Cook for a further 5 minutes being careful not to let the sauce boil and curdle\n| Put the sauce in a [[blender]] or force through a sieve\n| Add the sauce to the casserole and leave in the oven for another 15 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot in a large bowl with the reserved [[mango]] pieces on top\n\nServe with [[plain rice]] and fried [[almonds]] or [[cashew nut]]s\n\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #spicymangochicken #lemon #nutmeg #chickenstock #mango #ghee #mangoes #onions #turmeric #wok </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

If you are serving this as a [[main course]] it does not have to be as dry.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tablespoon [[vegetable oil]]\n| 2 [[onions]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 teaspoon [[ground coriander]] seeds\n| &#189; teaspoon [[ground cumin]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[chili powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[garam masala]]\n| 1 green [[chili]], de-seeded and sliced into rings\n| 1 large [[tomato]], chopped\n| 2 [[cloves garlic, crushed]]\n| 2.5 cm (1 \") peeled [[ginger root]], [[grated]]\n| 450 g (1 lb) lean [[beef]] mince\n| 225 g (&#189; lb) [[frozen peas]], [[defrosted]]\n| 225 g (&#189; lb) [[potatoes]], peeled and cut into very small cubes\n| Juice of half a [[lemon]]\n| A big handful of chopped [[coriander leaves]]\n| [[Sea salt]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Fry]] the [[onions]] in the [[oil]] until slightly [[brown]]\n| Add the [[tomatoes]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[ginger]] and [[chillies]] and [[fry]] for a few more minutes\n| Add all of the [[spices]] apart from the [[coriander leaves]], stir well and [[fry]] for a minute\n| Add the mince and cook on a high heat until [[browned]]\n| Add the [[potatoes]] and a few tablespoons of hot water to help cook the [[potatoes]], cover and cook for 10 minutes\n| Add the [[peas]] and continue to cook, uncovered, until the [[potatoes]] are cooked\n| Add the [[lemon juice]] and [[coriander leaves]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe as a meat dish or use as a filling for meat samosas.\n\nUse 1.5 tablespoons of filling for each sheet of filo pastry to make meat samosas.\n\n==See also==\n* If you're not an expert then, see: '''[[How to fold samosas|how to fold samosas]]'''.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#potatoes #corianderleaves #fry #spicymeatsamosafilling #onions #maincourse #garammasala #ginger #garlic #vegetableoil #tomato </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Spicy sorrel flavoured chicken Indian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #sorrel #ground #spicysorrelflavouredchicken #onions #greenchillies #ginger #ghee #jointingachicken #simmer #englishsorrel \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I've been looking for a recipe in which to use sorrel which we grow in our garden.  This hot curry fits the bill!\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2000\n|PortionCalories = 500\n|DatePublished=13th November 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 45 minutes\n|PrepTime =  45 minutes\n|CookTime =  1 hour\n|Image = [[Image:Spicy sorrel flavoured chicken recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Sumac works too...</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I've made this with sumac from our tree, just as good as sorrel.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nI've been looking for a recipe in which to use [[Sorrel|sorrel]] which we grow in our garden.  It has a sharp lemony flavour, which until now I've only found useful in [[Salads|salads]].  \n[[Image:25 grams of sorrel leaves.jpg|thumb|300px|right|25 grams of sorrel leaves, larger stems trimmed]]\n\nI found this Hyderabadi recipe in Mr Pushpash Pent's wonderful \"[[India]]\":  ISBN 978-0714859026\n\nI've adapted it very slightly to make it easier for me to replicate here in the UK.\n\nThe sorrel in the original recipe is [[gongura (''Hibiscus sabdariffa'')]], which is described as sour, so our [[English sorrel]] will probably be a reasonable substitute. \n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Ghee|ghee]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[olive oil]] - not authentic, but healthier than using all saturated fat (ghee)\n| 4 medium [[Onions|onions]], peeled and sliced\n| 1 thumb sized piece of [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and [[Grated|grated]]\n| 4 [[Fat|fat]] [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 x 750g (1lb 10 oz) whole [[Chicken|chicken]] cut into pieces and skin removed: [[Jointing a chicken|see here]].\n| Pinch of [[Salt|salt]]\n| 25 g [[Sorrel|sorrel]] leaves, chopped\n| 2 [[Green chillies|green chillies]], de-seeded and roughly chopped\n| 2 [[Red chillies|red chillies]], de-seeded and roughly chopped\n| 1 teaspoon [[Garam masala|garam masala]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] to powder\n| 1 teaspoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] to powder\n| 1 level teaspoon [[Chipotole chilli powder|chipotole chilli powder]] - ''optional if you want it quite hot''\n| 2 teaspoons [[Poppy seeds|poppy seeds]], [[Dry roasted|dry roasted]] then [[Ground|ground]] to a paste with a little water\n\n}}\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Heat the [[Ghee|ghee]] and oil in a heavy based pan or [[Dutch Oven|dutch oven]] over a medium heat.\n| Gently [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] for 8 minutes but don't let them colour\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for another few minutes\n| Add the [[Salt|salt]] and the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces, reduce the heat to low, cover and cook for 40 minutes or until the [[Chicken|chicken]] is properly cooked.  Stir the chicken now and then. Don't worry that it will be too dry, the chicken released quite a lot of liquid so it eventually  stews in it's own juices, so to speak.\n| While the [[Chicken|chicken]] is cooking, bring a small pan of water to the [[Boil|boil]] and add the [[Green chillies|green chillies]] and [[Sorrel|sorrel]] leaves and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 2 minutes.\n| Drain and allow to cool a little before blending to a paste in a feed processor or [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] - add a drop or two of the [[Boiled|boiled]] water if the paste is too dry\n| Add the remaining [[Spices|spices]] and [[Poppy seed|poppy seed]] paste to the [[Chicken|chicken]] and cook for 4 minutes\n| Stir in the [[Sorrel|sorrel]] paste and cook for 2 minutes more.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Plain rice|plain rice]], plain [[Naan|naan]] and a [[Yogurt|yogurt]] [[Dip|dip]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #sorrel #ground #spicysorrelflavouredchicken #onions #greenchillies #ginger #ghee #jointingachicken #simmer #englishsorrel </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Spicy vegetable samosa filling, an Indian vegetarian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#corianderleaves #fry #maincourse #groundcoriander #stirfried #gingerroot #lemon #chilli #cabbage #vegetableoil #lemonjuice \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is basically the filling for vegetable samosas, however it could easily be served as a main course with pilau rice or naan breads\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1414\n|PortionCalories = 353\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4 or as a filling for samosas for 4 people\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Spicy vegetable samosa filling recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Great idea</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Like you suggested, I couldn't be bothered to make the samosas, just used the filling alone - yum!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is basically the filling for vegetable samosas, however it could easily be served as a [[main course]] with [[pilau rice]] and [[naan breads]]\nBecause it is meant to be a samosa filling it should be quite dry or you will have a shock when you [[deep fry]] them!  If you are serving this as a [[main course]] it does not have to be as dry.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n| 1 [[onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 2 [[cloves garlic, crushed]]\n| 3 medium potatoes, peeled and cut into small cubes\n| &#189; cup [[frozen peas]], [[defrosted]]\n| &#189; cup finely sliced [[cabbage]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[desiccated coconut]] (you can [[Preparing a coconut|prepare this yourself if you wish]])\n| 1 green [[chilli]], de-seeded and sliced into rings\n| &#189; teaspoon [[garam masala]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[chilli powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[turmeric powder]]\n| 2.5 cm (1 \") peeled [[ginger root]], [[grated]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[ground coriander]] seeds\n| &#189; teaspoon [[ground cumin]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n| Juice of half a [[lemon]]\n| A big handful of chopped [[coriander leaves]]\n| [[Sea salt]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Boil the potatoes, peel and roughly mash them\n| Cook the peas by boiling or microwaving \n| Cook the cabbage by boiling or microwaving so it's to your liking\n| [[Fry]] the [[onions]] in the [[oil]] until slightly [[brown]]\n| Add all of the spices apart from the coriander and stir-fry for 3 minutes\n| Add the mashed potatoes, peas and cabbage and stir-fry for a little longer, mixing well\n| Add all of the [[spices]] apart from the [[coriander leaves]], stir well and [[fry]] for a minute\n| Add the [[lemon juice]] and [[coriander leaves]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe as a vegetable main course or use as a filling for vegetable samosas.\n\nIf you're not an expert then see: '''[[How to fold samosas|how to fold samosas]]'''.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#corianderleaves #fry #maincourse #groundcoriander #stirfried #gingerroot #lemon #chilli #cabbage #vegetableoil #lemonjuice </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This vegetarian dish is made with a potato stuffing\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 250\n|PortionCalories = 31\n|DatePublished=27th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Servings: 8 - Makes 8 stuffed parathas\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  2 hours 50 minutes\n|PrepTime = 2 hours 30 minutes\n|CookTime =  20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Stuffed parathas recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice, very nice!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">And not at all greasy, like the ones you get from the Indian take-away. \ud83d\udc73</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nAnother easy to make Indian flatbread.  This vegetarian dish is made with a potato (Aloo) stuffing.\n\nI made these with [[strong wholemeal flour]] as I had run out of [[Flour#Durum atta or semolina flour|durum atta]].  I think they are nice this way.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 portion [[Aloo stuffing (for parathas)|aloo stuffing for parathas]] \n| 1 Cup [http://www.google.co.uk/search?q=Golden+Temple+flour Golden Temple Flour] (duram atta) - [[Strong flour]] can be used as a substitute.\n| 1/3 \u2014 &#189; cup water\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Salt]]\n| 2-3 teaspoons [[ghee]], [[butter]] or [[vegetable oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Starting with 1/3 cup of water, add all of the ingredients in a bowl (or a [[food processor]])\n| Knead or blitz the mixture into a smooth elastic [[dough]] adding more water if required.  This will take about 5 minutes if hand-kneading\n| Diving in eight equal sized balls\n| Lightly [[oil]] a Tupperware-type container add the balls, cover and leave to rest for at room temperature for at least 30 minutes, ideally a few hours.\n| Roll out the [[dough]] so it's just large enough to cover the potato ball\n| Wrap the potato with the dough\n| Flour the wrapped dough ball and place the ''messy'' side down\n| Roll out to a 6\" circle (I forgot to photo this, I was too busy eating the results!)\n| Don't worry too much if the potato comes through the dough.  It won't puff up all cheffy, but it'll taste just as good.\n| Place the paratha in a very hot [[frying pan]] or [[tava]] \n| Heat for a minute then flip over for another minute.  I then splash a little oil in the pan and cook for another 2 minutes per side.  You can see when they are done. You can oil the paratha rather than the pan.  I just find it easier this way.\n| (I like to use olive oil as I feel it's healthier, even if it's not authentic)\n}}\n\n<gallery widths=270px heights=270px perrow=5>\n\nImage:Paratha dough.jpg|Paratha dough -  rested\n\nImage:Aloo stuffing for parathas.jpg|Aloo stuffing\n\nImage:Aloo filling, partially wrapped.jpg|Aloo filling, partially wrapped\n\nImage:Aloo filling, totally wrapped.jpg|Aloo filling, totally wrapped\n\nImage:Stuffed parathas.jpg|A plate of success (less the 3 that I ate)\n\nImage:Stuffed parathas recipe.jpg|Closer detail\n\n</gallery>\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Paratha]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Paratha]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Paratha]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Paratha]]\n[[Category:Starters|Paratha]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Paratha]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Paratha]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Paratha]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#stuffedparathas #dough #foodprocessor #vegetableoil #tava #ghee #strongflour #strongwholemealflour #panfried #butter </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

and [[Pepper|pepper]] and mix together. \n| Stir in the cubed [[Chicken|chicken]] and chill in the [[Fridge|fridge]] for 3 hours or overnight if preferred.\n| When ready to serve thread the [[Chicken|chicken]] on to metal [[skewers]] or soaked wooden skewers with the [[Onion|onion]] [[Wedges|wedges]].\n| Put on to a lightly [[Oil|oil]]ed [[Grill|grill]] rack, drizzle with a little extra \n| Arrange on serving plates with [[Lime wedges|lime wedges]] and sprigs of fresh [[Coriander|coriander]]. \n| Serve with a [[Tomato|tomato]], [[Red onion|red onion]] and [[Coriander|coriander]] title": "Tandoori chicken pizza",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tandoori chicken pizza, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tandoorichickenpizza #pizza #pizzastone #pizzadough #lemonjuice #mozzarella #yogurt #tomatoes #skewers #chorizosausages #chickentikka \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Following the recent scare over processed meat, I felt less inclined to use chorizo sausages for our regular home made pizza\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 992\n|PortionCalories = 496\n|DatePublished=28th March 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  4 hours, 16 minutes\n|PrepTime =  4 hours\n|CookTime =  16 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Tandoori chicken pizza.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Morrisons or Aldi</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Both do great flavoured spicy chicken which is great for this dish.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Processed meat leads to an early death|Following the recent scare over processed meat]], I felt less inclined to use [[chorizo sausages]] for our regular homemade [[pizza]] so I thought I would use fresh chicken breasts and flavour them with a pseudo-tandoori flavouring instead.  This does take quite a while to prepare, but only takes a few minutes of your time over a long period.  If you want to cheat even more, then use a packet of pre cooked tandoori chicken that most supermarkets sell.  Of course if you want to go the whole-hog, you can make everything from scratch with this [[chicken tikka|chicken tikka recipe]].\n\nI would normally skewer and grill the chicken as the pieces are too small to sit over the grid on a grill pan but as the [[skewers]] could not be found at the last minute I pan fried the chicken instead.  Just cook on a high heat until most of the liquid cooks off.\n\n'''for the  tandoori chicken'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 pack pre cooked tandoori chicken pieces\n}}\n''OR:''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 [[chicken breasts]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[lemon juice]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[curry paste]] / Patak's Madras paste / Patak's vindaloo paste etc.\n| 1 small pot [[yogurt]]\n}}\n'''for the pizza topping - 2 pizzas'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 medium tomatoes\n| Half a small onion, peeled and thinly sliced\n| 1 ball [[mozzarella]] cheese\n| [[Extra virgin olive oil]]\n| [[Sea Salt|Sea salt]]\n| [[Freshly ground black pepper]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Slice the chicken very thinly, add to a bowl with a tablespoon of [[lemon juice]] and a good pinch of salt.  Leave for 1 hour.\n* Mix whatever curry paste you are using into a pot of [[yogurt]]\n* Stir this in to the chicken pieces and leave in a cool place to marinade for 2 or 3 hours \n* Make the [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]] as instructed\n* If using a [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]], preheat the [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]] under a very hot [[Grill|grill]] for about 20 minutes. Place it about 8cm (3\") from the heat source.\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Tandoori chicken pizza ready to bake.jpg|300px\nImage:Tandoori chicken pizza pan fried.jpg|300px\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cook the chicken whichever way you please: skewered and [[grilled]] or [[barbecued]] or even pan fried, picking the chicken pieces out of the marinade leaving some of the marinade on the chicken, most of it will cook off.<br />\n|''Pan fried tandoori chicken''\n| Make 1 [[Pizza|pizza]] per person\n| Dust your work surface with [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]]\n| Divide the [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]] into two and roll out into two thin 25.5 cm (10 inch) [[Pizzas|pizzas]]\n| You can leave them in a warm place for an hour or so to rise.  I quite like them cooked immediately they are rolled out for a more crispy finish.\n| Prick the pizza all over with a fork. This prevents it puffing up too much and burning while it is cooking\n| With a deft move, slide the pizza from the [[Pizza peel|pizza peel]], on to the preheated [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]].\n| Cook on one side only for about 2 minutes or until lightly [[Browned|browned]].\n| Repeat for the other side.\n| Remove from the [[Oven|oven]] and add the cooked chicken, [[mozzarella]], [[tomatoes]], a few [[onion]] rings and a drizzle of olive oil.\n| Return to the [[Oven|oven]] and cook until the cheese is nicely melted.\n| Repeat for the second [[Pizza|pizza]] whilst you prepare the first.\n| Keep the first [[Pizza|pizza]] warm at the bottom of the [[Oven|oven]] whilst you make the second.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with one of these [[cole slaw|cole slaw recipes]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Pizza recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tandoorichickenpizza #pizza #pizzastone #pizzadough #lemonjuice #mozzarella #yogurt #tomatoes #skewers #chorizosausages #chickentikka </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

title": "Tarka dhal",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tarka dhal Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tarkadhal #splitpeas #garlic #simmer #onion #curryleaves #mustardseeds #spices #stock #chana #garammasala \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Tarka dhal comes in many guises, but usually contains yellow split peas, chana dhal, and/or red lentils (masoor dhal), various spices, chilli and\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1494\n|PortionCalories = 747\n|DatePublished=13th November 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 2 to 4 people\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 55 minutes\n |PrepTime = 5 minutes\n |CookTime = 50 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Tarka dhal recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Lovely lentils</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.9</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This simple, but spicy dish goes with any curry and naan breads.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n\nTarka dhal comes in many guises, but usually contains yellow [[Split peas|split peas]], [[Chana|chana]] dhal, and/or red [[Lentils|lentils]] (masoor dhal), various [[Spices|spices]], [[Chilli|chilli]] and [[Garlic|garlic]].  In UK Indian restaurants, it can be served thick or thin, but in India, a thin and [[Soup|soup]]-like consistency is the norm. The use of [[mustard seeds]] and [[curry leaves]] as ingredients comes from southern India.  \"Tadka\" refers to the process of heating the spices in oil and pouring over the cooked lentils.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 200 g yellow [[Split peas|split peas]]\n| 1 litre water or [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 15 ml [[Oil|oil]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[ghee]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], thinly sliced\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, [[Diced|diced]] (I used 2 bulbs)\n| 4 Indian [[Green chillies|green chillies]], chopped\n| 2 teaspoons black [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Turmeric|turmeric]], ground\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Garam masala|garam masala]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Coriander|coriander]], ground\n| A few [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]]\n| 1 tin chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] or 400g ripe tomatoes, peeled and roughly chopped\n| Seasoning\n| Fresh [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rinse the [[Split peas|split peas]] and place in a saucepan covered with the water or [[Stock|stock]].\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], skim and lower the heat.\n| Cover, and then [[Simmer|simmer]] for 30-40 minutes until the [[Split peas|peas]] are cooked.\n| Meanwhile, heat the [[Oil|oil]] and the [[ghee]] in a [[Frying pan|frying pan]].\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Fry|fry]] until slightly [[Browned|browned]].\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Fry|fry]] until the garlic is golden.  \n| Tip into bowl and reserve.\n| Add the [[Mustard seeds|mustard seeds]] to the same pan and when they have started to pop, stir in the [[turmeric]], [[Garam masala|garam masala]], [[Coriander|coriander]] and [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]].\n| Cook for a further minute then add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]].\n| Season and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 7 minutes.\n| Add the [[Spice|spice]] mixture to the [[Split peas|split peas]], return to the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for a further 10-15 minutes.\n| Add more [[Stock|stock]] if it becomes too thick.\n| Serve in soup bowls and place some of the [[Onion|onion]] on the top\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Naan bread|naan bread]] or chapattis.\n===Variations===\nIf you want to make a thick tarka dhal, double the amount of [[Split peas|split peas]].  Experiment with different [[Spices|spices]]. You can also substitute [[Split peas|split peas]] for [[chana]] dhal for a different flavour.\n===Chef's notes===\nTo reduce the need for skimming, use bottled water.  I actually slow fry the [[onions]] for about 2 hours, adding the [[garlic]] and [[chillies]] towards the end.  This allows the ingredients to caramelise nicely.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Tarka dhal]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Tarka dhal]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Tarka dhal]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Tarka dhal]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Tarka dhal]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Tarka dhal]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes|Tarka dhal]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Tarka dhal]]\n[[Category:Starters|Tarka dhal]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Tarka dhal]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tarkadhal #splitpeas #garlic #simmer #onion #curryleaves #mustardseeds #spices #stock #chana #garammasala </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

use about the same amount as you would for [[jacket potatoes]].\n| 2 tablespoons [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]]\n| [[Juice]] from 2 [[Limes|limes]] and [[grated]] [[zest]] from 1 [[lime]]\n| 1 tablespoon of Thai red [[Curry paste|curry paste]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]] or [[Jaggery|jaggery]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 350g raw [[Prawns|prawns]], peeled and de-veined\n| 2 tablespoons of desiccated [[Coconut|coconut]]\n| A handful of fresh [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]], roughly torn\n| 142 ml pot of [[Sour cream|sour cream]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6)\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Thai prawn grilling.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Thai prawns, grilled\nImage:Thai prawn baked sweet potatoes ingredients.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Thai prawn baked sweet potatoes - the ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[Sweet potatoes|sweet potatoes]] on a [[baking tray]] as they tend to leave a sticky residue while cooking\n| [[Bake]] for about 45 to 55 minutes or until soft to the press\n| Meanwhile, mix the [[Oil|oil]], [[Lime juice|lime juice]], Thai paste, [[Sugar|sugar]] and seasoning\n| Stir in the [[Prawns|prawns]] and [[Marinate|marinate]] while the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] cook\n| Put the [[Grill|grill]] on high, slide the [[Prawns|prawns]] on to a [[foil]]-lined grill tray, pour over most of the [[marinade]] and grill for 4 minutes, turning once, but [[Basting|basting]] with the [[Marinade|marinade]]\n| Sprinkle the [[Coconut|coconut]] over the [[Prawns|prawns]] and return to the [[Grill|grill]] for a minute so it toasts and browns a little\n| Cut a cross in the top of the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and with a cloth, squeeze them together to split them open\n| Spoon in the [[Prawn|prawn]] mixture and a little [[Marinade|marinade]]\n| Garnish with [[Sour cream|sour cream]] and torn [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with a green salad and fresh tomatoes.\n===Chef's notes===\nYou could of course make this with normal [[Potatoes|potatoes]]\nI have used the fabulous [[green curry paste]] instead of Thai red curry paste. \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#thaiprawnbakedsweetpotatoes #prawns #marinade #potatoes #sweetpotatoes #grill #sourcream #basilleaves #coconut #miseenplace #limes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

No need to stand over three rings on the [[Hob|hob]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n| 200g [[Basmati rice]], washed and soaked for 1 hour\n| Pinch of [[Saffron strands|saffron strands]]\n| 3 [[Eggs|eggs]], thoroughly washed\n| 400g [[Smoked haddock|smoked haddock]] or [[Cod|cod]]\n| 200ml [[Milk]]\n| 50g [[Butter|butter]], chopped into small pieces\n| 150g [[Yoghurt|yogurt]]\n| [[Chilli powder]]. to taste\n| [[Salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]], to taste\n| 30g [[Heston's spiced butter]]\n| [[Fresh herbs]] to garnish, finely chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add 1kg water to the bowl and place the [[Rice|rice]], mixed with the [[Saffron|saffron]] in the internal [[Steaming|steaming]] basket.\n| Put the [[Eggs|eggs]] on top of the [[Rice|rice]].\n| Put the [[Haddock|haddock]] in a container  that fits easily into the Varoma bowl. \n| Pour enough [[Milk|milk]] over the [[Fish|fish]] to just cover. \n| Place the container in the Varoma and position it over the [[Thermomix]] bowl.\n| Cook for 14 minutes / Temp. Varoma / Speed 4. \n| After 10 minutes it may [[Help|help]] to open lid of the [[Thermomix]] and fluff the [[Rice|rice]] around the [[Eggs|eggs]].\n| Remove the [[Fish|fish]] from the Varoma, drain and leave to cool.\n| Remove the [[Eggs|eggs]], cool and shell before setting aside. \n| Place [[Rice|rice]] in a bowl and mix with the 50g of [[Butter|butter]].\n| Remove skin and [[bones]] from the [[Fish|fish]] and [[Flake|flake]].\n| Mix in with the [[Rice|rice]], together with the [[Yoghurt|yogurt]], seasoning and [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]].\n| Chop 2 of the [[Eggs|eggs]] and add to the [[Rice|rice]] mixture.\n| Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour].\n| Grease an ovenproof dish and gently transfer the [[Kedgeree|kedgeree]] mixture to it.\n| Dot with [[Heston's spiced butter]] and [[Bake|bake]] for about 15 minutes.\n| Cut the remaining [[Egg|egg]] lengthwise into quarters to garnish the [[Kedgeree|kedgeree]] and sprinkle the [[herbs]] over the top.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n* Lightly adapted from a recipe by '''[http://www.forumthermomix.com/index.php?topic=94.0 Thermomixer]'''\n===Variations===\nYou can also use [[Smoked salmon|smoked salmon]] or a mixture of [[Fish|fish]].\n==See also==\n*[[Salmon kedgeree]]\n*[[Buttery kedgeree]]\n*[[Red lentil kedgeree with avocado & tomato]]\n*[['Greasy spoon' kedgeree]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Kedgeree thermomix]]\n[[Category:British recipes|Kedgeree thermomix]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Kedgeree thermomix]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes|Kedgeree thermomix]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Kedgeree thermomix]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes|Kedgeree thermomix]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Kedgeree thermomix]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes|Kedgeree thermomix]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes|Kedgeree thermomix]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #eggs #fish #thermomix #butter #yoghurt #kedgeree #chillipowder #salmonkedgeree #thermomixrecipeskedgereethermomix #saffronstrands </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Try it with [[Shoulder|shoulder]] of [[Mutton|mutton]] if you can obtain it.\n[[Image:Timitar gosht ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Timitar gosht, the ingredients]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 560g (1 &frac14; lb) [[Shoulder|shoulder]] of [[Lamb|lamb]], trimmed of [[Fat|fat]] and cut into cubes\n| [[Juice]] from 1 [[Lime|lime]]\n| 6 [[Fat|fat]] [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 2.5 cm piece  of [[Ginger root|ginger root]], peeled and [[Grated|grated]]\n| 1.5 teaspoons [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] to a powder\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 1.25 teaspoons [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]] or [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]]\n| 2 large [[Onions|onions]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 450 g can peeled [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Mashed|mashed]] or the equivalent amount of fresh [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and mashed. Good use for your [[Tomato press|tomato press]]!\n| 3 to 6 fresh [[Green chillies|green chillies]], cut into rings\n| 15 [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]], torn or chopped\n| Small bunch of [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a bowl, add the [[Meat|meat]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Turmeric|turmeric]], [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and 1 teaspoon of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]].  Mix well and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for an hour or so to [[Marinade|marinade]].\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] for 5 minutes or until just [[Browning|browning]].\n| Turn up the heat, add the [[Meat|meat]] with [[Marinade|marinade]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a few minutes.  Reduce the heat to a [[Simmer|simmer]], cover and cook for 10 minutes, stirring now and then.\n| Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], remaining [[Salt|salt]], [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Coriander|coriander]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] gently, covered, for 50 minutes, stirring now and then.\n| Add the [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]], stir well and serve.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nTo pad this out, I also added a portion of frozen butternut squash, extra liquid squeezed out.  A few teaspoons of brown sugar made this dish perfect. Test, taste and adjust to suit your preference.\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]] and [[Nan breads|nan breads]].\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mutton recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlic #fat #simmer #basilleaves #lamb #tomatoes #timatargosht #marinade #onions #shoulder #wok </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tuna curry, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tunacurry #tuna #tomatoes #chillipowder #groundcumin #fry #bayleaves #cuminseeds #simmer #potatoes #fishstock \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A nice, hot fishy curry!\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2069\n|PortionCalories = 517\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Tuna curry with cashew nut pilau rice\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Tuna curry recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">\ud83d\udc1f\ud83d\udc1f\ud83d\udc1f</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Mmm.. .. tuna</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nA nice, hot [[Fish|fishy]] curry!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 tablespoons [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]], plus a little extra for sealing the [[Tuna|tuna]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], sliced\n| 1 red or [[Yellow pepper|yellow pepper]], thinly sliced\n| 3-4 bulbs [[Garlic, crushed|garlic, crushed]]\n| 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| ?? teaspoons [[Bird's eye chilli paste|bird's eye chilli paste]]\n| 1 x 400g tin of chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 2 large [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and and cut into 2.5cm cubes\n| 300ml [[Fish stock|fish stock]]\n| 4 [[Tuna|tuna]] steaks\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large [[Deep frying|deep frying]] pan and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] for 2 minutes or until they begin to splutter.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Pepper|pepper]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]] and [[Fry|fry]] until the onion has started to [[Brown|brown]].\n| Stir in the [[Salt|salt]], [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]], [[Coriander|coriander]] and [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] and cook for about 3 minutes.\n| Add the [[Bird's eye chilli paste|bird's eye chilli paste]] and cook for a further 1 minute.\n| Pour in the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Fish stock|fish stock]] and add the [[Potatoes|potatoes]].\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for about 15 minutes.\n| Meanwhile, heat a little oil in a frying pan and seal the [[Tuna|tuna]] for 2 minutes on each side.\n| Add the [[Tuna|tuna]] fillets to the curry, cover, and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 5 minutes or more until the fish is tender.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with  [[Cashew nut pilau rice|cashew nut pilau rice]],  [[Naan bread|naan bread]] or any other Indian [[flatbread]].\n===Variations===\nTry this with [[Swordfish|swordfish]] steaks.\n\nSubstitute fresh [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] for tinned if desired, but they must be well ripened.  Also add other [[Vegetables|vegetables]] of your choice.\n===Chef's notes===\nUse your common sense as to how hot you wish this curry to be.  Just add the [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] and the [[Bird's eye chilli paste|bird's eye chilli paste]] a little at a time and keep tasting.  Remember that as the liquid evaporates, the more concentrated the heat will be.  The [[Garlic|garlic]] quantity may seem excessive, but it isn't, honestly! \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tunacurry #tuna #tomatoes #chillipowder #groundcumin #fry #bayleaves #cuminseeds #simmer #potatoes #fishstock </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Turmeric crusted turbot with goan curry sauce",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Turmeric crusted turbot with goan curry sauce recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#sauce #fish #seeds #fry #curryleaves #onion #nage #dessert #shallots #tomatoes #turmeric \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Robust, creamy fish with a spicy coating and a sharp fiery goan curry sauce.\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=29th September 2016\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 3\n|TotalTime =  30 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  20 minutes\n|TotalCalories = 1610\n|PortionCalories = 530\n|Image = [[Image:Turmeric crusted turbot with goan curry sauce recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Very authentic</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">But then it should be.  I've never met two more passionate foodies, than Nik & Edwina.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe is reproduced with the kind permission of [[Nik and Edwina's Cookbook]].\nRobust, creamy fish with a spicy coating and a sharp fiery goan curry sauce\nTo quote: \"This is a divine dish; the smooth, robust, creamy [[Fish|fish]] goes incredibly well with its spicy crusting, and with the sharp, fiery, sweet/sour [[Sauce|sauce]].\"\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n}}\n====The fish:- ====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 x 150g fillets of [[Turbot|turbot]], skin on \n| 15 fresh [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]], finely chopped \n| \u00bd teaspoons black [[Onion|onion]] [[Seeds|seeds]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground|ground]] [[Turmeric|turmeric]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] \n}}\n====The Goan spice mix:- ====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 10 [[Cloves|cloves]] \n| 1 tablespoon [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]] \n| 1\u00bd teaspoons [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]] \n| 2 black [[Cardamoms|cardamoms]], [[Seeds|seeds]] taken out, pods discarded. If you can\u2019t get black, green will do nicely \n| 2 [[Star anise|star anise]] \n| 3 [[Dried|dried]] hot [[Red chillies|red chillies]] \n| 2 tablespoons [[White wine vinegar|white wine vinegar]] \n| 1 tablespoon [[Caster Sugar|caster sugar]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]] \n}}\n====The sauce:- ====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 4 small [[Shallots|shallots]], finely chopped \n| \u00bd teaspoon mild red [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] \n| 2 large [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], chopped \n| 125mls [[Nage]]\n| 125mls thin [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] \n}}\n====To serve:- ====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Steamed]] [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]] for 2\n| [[Steamed]] [[Spinach|spinach]] for 2\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| To make the [[Spice|spice]] mix, [[Dry roast|dry roast]] the dry spice mix [[Spices|spices]] in a pan until they start to smell lovely. Blitz them in a liquidizer with the [[Rest|rest]] of the spice mix ingredients. Set aside.\n| To make the [[Sauce|sauce]], heat a [[Dessert|dessert]] spoon of [[Coconut|coconut]] or [[Ground nut|ground nut]] [[Oil|oil]] in a heavy bottomed [[Saucepan|saucepan]] and [[Fry|fry]] the chopped [[Shallots|shallots]] over a medium heat till they\u2019re soft, and are starting to go golden.\n| Add the [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] and stir for a minute, then add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and stir till they\u2019ve disintegrated, and are starting to go quite dry.\n| Turn the heat down low, and add the [[Spice|spice]] mix you\u2019ve set aside, and cook slowly, stirring, till the [[Oil|oil]] is starting to separate from the mix.\n| Add the [[Nage|nage]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for a few minutes, then bring the heat back up and add the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] and simmer gently for five minutes.\n| Season, and check the flavour; it should be quite fiery, with a sharp sweet/sour flavour.\n| [[Sieve]] the [[Sauce|sauce]] into a bowl, clean the pan, discarding the remaining contents, and return the sauce to the pan. Keep warm.\n| To cook the [[Fish|fish]], rub it with the [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]], [[Onion|onion]] [[Seeds|seeds]], [[Turmeric|turmeric]] and [[Salt|salt]] and leave for 10 minutes. Then heat a [[Dessert|dessert]] spoon of [[Coconut oil|coconut oil]] in a [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and add the fish, skin side down.\n| [[Fry]] for about 2 minutes, so the skin is nice and crisp, then turn it over, take the heat down a bit, and cook for another 3 minutes.\n| Meanwhile, put neat [[Pile|pile]]s of [[Rice|rice]] on two plates (we use those steel tower thingies, they\u2019re open ended metal rings 7cm in diameter and 6cm tall), then place a piece of [[Fish|fish]] on each plate, add a neat pile of [[Spinach|spinach]], then pour a generous dollop of [[Sauce|sauce]] neatly around, and serve.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* https://sites.google.com/site/nikandedwinascookbook/Home/fish/turmeric-crusted-turbot-with-goan-curry-sauce\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n[[Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sauce #fish #seeds #fry #curryleaves #onion #nage #dessert #shallots #tomatoes #turmeric </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Not for me.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> - [[User:PSmith]] </span></span>}}\n\nUpma or uppuma, the popular South Indian breakfast dish is usually made with Semolina (called Rava or Suji in India).\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 cup [[Wheat]] [[Rava]] ([[Semolina]])\n| 1 tablespoon [[Cooking oil]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Mustard seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin]] seeds\n| 1 teaspoon grated [[Ginger root]]\n| 3 [[Green chillies]]\n| 1 [[onion]], peeled and chopped\n| [[Salt]] to taste\n| 3/4 cup of chopped [[Vegetables]] of choice: [[Peas]], [[carrots]], [[aubergines]], [[potatoes]], [[cauliflower]], [[cabbage]], [[tomatoes]]\n| 3 tablespoons of [[grated]] [[coconut]]\n| 4 teaspoons of [[coriander leaves]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Lemon juice]] (optional)\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Dry-roast]] the [[semolina]] until it just begins to turn [[brown]], then set aside.\n| In a large saucepan/[[wok]], heat the [[cooking oil]].\n| Add [[mustard seeds]] and wait for them to sputter. Then add [[cumin]], [[ginger]], green [[chillies]] and chopped [[onions]] and [[fry]] until [[onions]] caramelise.\n| Add [[vegetables]], [[salt]] and 1.5 cups of water, and bring to [[boil]].\n| Add the [[roasted]] [[rava]], turn down the heat, and mix quickly to avoid lumps forming.\n| The upma is done when all the water is absorbed by the [[rava]].\n| Garnish with [[grated]] [[coconut]], chopped [[cilantro]] leaves and [[lemon juice]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot or cold\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Upma]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Upma]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Upma]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Upma]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes|Upma]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Upma]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Upma]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#upma #rava #lemonjuice #grated #onions #coconut #cookingoil #cumin #vegetables #semolina #mustardseeds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

[[Grated|grated]], &frac12; [[Julienned|julienned]] (cut into very thin strips)\n| 6 [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]]\n| 100g [[Coconut block|coconut block]]\n| 2 large [[Onions|onions]], peeled and slices\n| 200g tinned [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] or equivalent amount of fresh tomatoes\n| 2 tablespoons of [[tomato puree]]\n| 1 green [[Chili|chili]], chopped finely\n| 1 tablespoon [[Malt vinegar|malt vinegar]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Ghee|ghee]], [[Oil|oil]] or [[Butter|butter]]\n| [[Sea salt]] to taste\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Grind all of the whole [[Spices|spices]], except for the [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]],  to a powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]].\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Oil|oil]] to a heavy [[Frying pan|frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]], [[Brown|brown]] the [[Meat|meat]] quickly over a high heat, remove and reserve.\n| [[Fry]] the [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Grated|grated]] [[Ginger|ginger]] until the onions are sort, about 8 minutes.\n| Add the [[Ground|ground]] [[Spices|spices]] and [[Fry|fry]] for a minute more.\n| Stir in the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[tomato puree]], [[Vinegar|vinegar]], [[Julienned|julienned]] [[Ginger|ginger]], meat and 1/4 a cup of boiling water and mix well.\n| Cover and cook until the [[Meat|meat]] is tender, about 30 to 40 minutes.  If the [[Meat|meat]] is still tough, add another 1/4 cup of [[Boiling|boiling]] water and continue cooking for 20 minutes more.\n| Remove the cover, add the [[Coconut block|coconut block]], green [[Chili|chili]], season with [[salt]], mix well and cook until the [[Coconut|coconut]] is dissolved.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Venison curry reduced.jpg|Reduced\nImage:Venison curry the start.jpg|The start\nImage:Venison curry ingredients.jpg|The ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]] and [[naan breads]]\n===Variations===\nAdd cubed [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and a little extra liquid at the start.\n\nI f you don't have curry leaves, just use a couple of bay leaves.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#venisoncurry #ginger #tomatopuree #onions #coconutblock #curryleaves #fry #julienned #chili #spices #grated </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Abel and Cole\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2392\n|PortionCalories = 598\n|DatePublished=27th April 2014\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 4 hours 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 4 hours\n |Image = [[Image: Very fruity pumpkin curry slow cooker recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Earthy food</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Great for a grey winter's day</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image: Very fruity pumpkin curry slow cooker.jpg|thumb|300px|right|After 4 hours]]\nThis is my very fruity variation of [[Pumpkin and chickpea curry]] which I've adapted for the [[slow cooker]].  We had the remnants of an [[Abel & Cole]] fruit and vegetable box to use up so this was ideal!  We'll be ok for our [[5 a day]] this weekend!\n\nThis Is a great recipe for using up very hard or very firm pears and another recipe for your [http://www.guardian.co.uk/lifeandstyle/wordofmouth/2009/may/14/ghent-vegetarian-city-healthy-belgium Gent night]\n\nI have to say that this was one of the best curries I've made in a long while.\n\n'''spice powder'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Grind the following to a powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]:\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[White cumin|white cumin]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[fenugreek seeds]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[Coriander|coriander]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[poppy seeds]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[garam masala]]\n}}\n'''curry'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] or [[ghee]]\n| A big pinch of freshly ground [[black pepper]]\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 5 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 2.5 cm [[Root ginger|root ginger]], peeled and [[Grated|grated]]\n| 1 large [[Red chillies|red chilli]], chopped into rings\n| 450g (1lb) [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] or [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] flesh, peeled and cubed\n| 2 firm [[pears]], peeled, cored and cut into bite-sized chunks\n| 30g mixed dried fruit of your choice\n| 1 tablespoon [[Curry paste|curry paste]]\n| 1 400g can of [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]], rinsed and drained\n| 300 ml [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[jaggery]] or brown sugar \n}}\n'''add during the last 30 minutes of cooking'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 [[kiwi fruit]], peeled and cut into bite-sized chunks\n| 1 [[Banana|banana]], sliced\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\nSet your [[slow cooker]] to medium\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[wok]] or [[frying pan]].  Add the oil or [[ghee]] and a big pinch of [[black pepper]]\n| Gently [[fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] for 4 minutes.  Add the ginger and garlic and fry for a further 2 minutes, stirring so the garlic does not burn\n| Add [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Spices|spices]] and [[Fry|fry]] for a further minute\n| Transfer the spice mix and the remaining ingredients (apart from the last two) into your [[slow cooker]]\n| Mix very well and slow cook for 4 hours\n| Add the [[kiwi fruit]] and sliced [[banana]] 30 minutes before the cooking is completed \n| Add the [[Stock|stock]], bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] until the [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] is soft (about 20 to 40 minutes) \n}}\nIf the [[pears]] are soft then add them for the last 30 minutes so they don't go to mush.\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with homemade [[Naan bread|naan bread]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Abel and Cole veg box recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#slowcooker #pumpkin #fry #blackpepper #pears #kiwifruit #banana #ghee #veryfruitypumpkincurryslowcookerrecipe #simmer #wok </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Wholemeal puri, Indian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#wholemealpuri #foodprocessor #strongwhiteflour #vegetableoil #chapati #indiandishes #barbecued #dough #yogurt #unleavened #flour \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Wholemeal puri or wholemeal poori is an unleavened flatbread, from India or Pakistan, that is quickly fried rather than being cooked on a tava\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1193\n|PortionCalories = 198\n|DatePublished=27th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 6 - Makes 6 puri\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 45 minutes\n|PrepTime = 40 minutes\n|CookTime = 5 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Puri recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Puffy, puffy puri</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Love these, but I can never get mine to look like that - what's the trick?</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nWholemeal puri or wholemeal poori is an [[unleavened]] [[flatbread]], from India or Pakistan, that is quickly fried rather than being cooked on a [[tava]].  It should be a little smaller than a [[roti]] or a [[chapati]], about 13 cm (5\") round.\n\nWhilst kneading [[dough]] can be therapeutic, if time is your enemy, then the [[food processor]] is your friend.\n\nPuris are the perfect accompaniment to most [[Indian dishes]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 cup [[atta flour]] or [[strong white flour]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n| 2 tablespoons [[yogurt]] (optional)\n| Vegetable oil for frying\n| &#189; cup water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Tip all of the ingredients and half of the water into the [[food processor]] with a plastic blade or dough hook attachment\n| Blitz the mixture whilst adding a more water a little at a time until you have a soft, pliable dough that is not too sticky\n| Remove from the processor, dust with a little [[flour]] and rest for 30 minutes in a bowl, covered with a damp tea-towel\n| Divide into 6 equal parts and roll into balls\n| With a rolling pin on a floured surface, roll each roti out into a disc, about 13 cm (5\") round\n| Heat 2.5 cm (1\") oil in a wok or large heavy-based frying pan \n| Deep fry each puri, holding it under the oil with a slotted spoon until it puffs up which should only take a few seconds\n| Drain on kitchen paper\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe immediately\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Puri]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Puri]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Puri]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Puri]]\n[[Category:Starters|Puri]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Puri]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#wholemealpuri #foodprocessor #strongwhiteflour #vegetableoil #chapati #indiandishes #barbecued #dough #yogurt #unleavened #flour </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

I agree, Cock Brand curry pastes are very good.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nYellow [[Curry|curry]] ([[Thai]]: &#3649;&#3585;&#3591;&#3585;&#3632;&#3627;&#3619;&#3637;&#3656;, RTGS: [[Kaeng kari|kaeng kari]],  [k&#603;&#720;&#331; kar\u00ec&#720;]; [[Chinese]]: &#40643;&#21654;&#21937;) is one of the more popular [[Curries|curries]] often found in Western Thai restaurants.\n\nMy favourite curry pastes are the [[Cock Brand pastes]].  They go off quickly, even if [[Refrigerated|refrigerated]], but if they are [[Frozen|frozen]], they keep for years.  Even better, you can just remove a few tablespoons of the curry paste even it is frozen.  Brilliant!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 3 tablespoons of yellow [[Curry paste|curry paste]]\n| 400g can of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| 450g (1 lb) of [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces.  Breast [[Meat|meat]] is good but I feel the cuts with [[bones]] impart more flavour\n| 3 medium [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and cut into quarters\n| 125g packet of fresh [[Baby sweet corn|baby sweetcorn]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Nam pla|nam pla]] ([[Fish sauce|fish sauce]])\n}}\n'''to garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 30g [[Fried]] [[Onions|onions]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Part [[Boil|boil]] the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] for 7 minutes and set to one side\n| Cut your [[Chicken|chicken]] into bite-sized pieces, cutting through the bone with a cleaver if needed\n| Halve the [[Baby sweetcorn|baby sweetcorn]] cobs\n| Mix the can of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] well and add to a pan or [[Wok|wok]] together with the yellow [[Curry paste|curry paste]]\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces, [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Baby sweetcorn|baby sweetcorn]] cobs and [[Nam pla|nam pla]]\n| Bring the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] to the [[Boil|boil]] and reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 15 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe garnished with crispy [[Fried|fried]] [[Onions|onions]] on a bed of [[Plain rice|plain rice]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#babysweetcorn #coconutmilk #potatoes #chicken #fried #currypaste #onions #nampla #yellowcurry #boil #curry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
